{"chapter_id": "1.1.1.", "chapter_title": "Exhaust emissions at normal and low ambient temperature, evaporative emissions, emissions of", "raw_text": "crankcase gases, the durability of pollution control exhaust devices and on-board diagnostic\n(OBD) systems of motor vehicles equipped with positive-ignition (P.I.) engines which have at\nleast 4 wheels.\n\n(1)\nAs defined in Annex 7 to the Consolidated Resolution on the Construction of Vehicles (R.E.3), (document\nTRANS/WP.29/78/Rev.1/Amend.2 as last amended by Amend.4)."}
{"chapter_id": "1.1.2.", "chapter_title": "Exhaust emissions, the durability of anti-pollution devices and on-board diagnostic (OBD) systems", "raw_text": "of vehicles of Categories M1 and N1 equipped with compression-ignition (C.I.) engines which\nhave at least 4 wheels and a maximum mass not exceeding 3 500 kg."}
{"chapter_id": "1.1.3.", "chapter_title": "Exhaust emissions at normal and low ambient temperature, evaporative emissions, emissions of", "raw_text": "crankcase gases, the durability of pollution control exhaust devices and on-board diagnostic\n(OBD) systems of hybrid electric vehicles (HEV) equipped with positive-ignition (P.I.) engines\nhaving at least four wheels."}
{"chapter_id": "1.1.4.", "chapter_title": "Exhaust emissions, the durability of anti-pollution devices and on-board diagnostic (OBD) systems", "raw_text": "of hybrid electric vehicles (HEV) of Categories M1 and N1 equipped with compression-ignition\n(C.I.) engines, having at least four wheels and a maximum mass not exceeding 3 500 kg."}
{"chapter_id": "1.1.5.", "chapter_title": "It does not apply to:", "raw_text": "– Vehicles with a maximum mass of less than 400 kg and to vehicles having a maximum design speed\nof less than 50 km/h.\n\n– Vehicles whose unladen mass is not more than 400 kg if they are intended for carrying passengers\nor 550 kg if they are intended for carrying goods and whose maximum engine power does not\nexceed 15 kW."}
{"chapter_id": "1.1.6.", "chapter_title": "At the request of the manufacturer, type approval pursuant to this Regulation may be extended from", "raw_text": "M1 or N1 vehicles equipped with compression-ignition engines which have already been type\napproved, to M2 and N2 vehicles having a reference mass not exceeding 2 840 kg and\nmeeting the conditions of Paragraph 7. (extension of approval)."}
{"chapter_id": "1.1.7.", "chapter_title": "Vehicles of Category N1 equipped with compression-ignition engines or equipped with positive-", "raw_text": "ignition engines fuelled with NG or LPG are not subject to this Regulation provided they have\nbeen type-approved pursuant to Regulation No.49 as amended by the last series of\namendments."}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.", "chapter_title": "This Regulation does not apply to vehicles equipped with positive-ignition engines fuelled with NG or", "raw_text": "LPG used for driving motor vehicles of Category M1 having a maximum mass exceeding 3\n500 kg, M2, M3, N2, N3 to which Regulation No.49 is applicable."}
{"chapter_id": "2.", "chapter_title": "DEFINITIONS", "raw_text": "For the purposes of this Regulation:\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.", "chapter_title": "\"Vehicle type\" means a category of power-driven vehicles that do not differ in such", "raw_text": "essential respects as:"}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.1.", "chapter_title": "The equivalent inertia determined in relation to the reference mass as", "raw_text": "prescribed in Annex 4, Paragraph 5.1, and"}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.2.", "chapter_title": "The engine and vehicle characteristics as defined in Annex 1.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.", "chapter_title": "\"Reference mass\" means the \"unladen mass\" of the vehicle increased by a uniform", "raw_text": "figure of 100 kg for test according to Annexes 4 and 8,"}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.1.", "chapter_title": "\"Unladen mass\" means the mass of the vehicle in running order without", "raw_text": "driver, passengers or load, but with the fuel tank 90% full and the usual set\nof tools and spare wheel on board, where applicable;"}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.", "chapter_title": "\"Maximum mass\" means the technically permissible maximum mass declared by", "raw_text": "the vehicle manufacturer (this mass may be greater than the maximum mass\nauthorised by the national administration);"}
{"chapter_id": "2.4.", "chapter_title": "\"Gaseous pollutants\" means the exhaust gas emissions of carbon monoxide,", "raw_text": "oxides of nitrogen, expressed in NO2 equivalent, and hydrocarbons expressed of:\n\n(a) C1H1.85 for petrol (E0);\n\n(b) C1H1.86 for diesel (B0);\n\n(c) C1H2.525 for LPG;\n\n(d) C1H4 for NG;\n\n(e) C1H1.89O0.016 for petrol (E5);\n\n(f) C1H1.86O0.005 for diesel (B5)."}
{"chapter_id": "2.5.", "chapter_title": "\"Particulate pollutants\" means components of the exhaust gas which are removed", "raw_text": "from the diluted exhaust gas at a maximum temperature of 325 K (52° C) by means\nof the filters described in Annex 4;"}
{"chapter_id": "2.6.", "chapter_title": "\"Exhaust emissions\" means:", "raw_text": "For positive-ignition (P.I.) engines, emissions of gaseous pollutants;\n\nFor compression-ignition (C.I.) engines, emissions of gaseous and particulate pollutants;"}
{"chapter_id": "2.7.", "chapter_title": "\"Evaporative emissions\" means the hydrocarbon vapours lost from the fuel system", "raw_text": "of a motor vehicle other than those from exhaust emissions;"}
{"chapter_id": "2.7.1.", "chapter_title": "\"Tank breathing losses\"  are hydrocarbon emissions caused by", "raw_text": "temperature changes in the fuel tank (assuming a ratio of C1H2.33);\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "2.7.2.", "chapter_title": "\"Hot soak losses\" are hydrocarbon emissions arising from the fuel system", "raw_text": "of a stationary vehicle after a period of driving (assuming a ratio of C1H2.20)."}
{"chapter_id": "2.8.", "chapter_title": "\"Engine crankcase\" means the spaces in or external to an engine which are", "raw_text": "connected to the oil sump by internal or external ducts through which gases and\nvapours can escape;"}
{"chapter_id": "2.9.", "chapter_title": "\"Cold start device\" means a device that temporarily enriches the air/fuel mixture of", "raw_text": "the engine thus assisting the engine to start;"}
{"chapter_id": "2.10.", "chapter_title": "\"Starting aid\" means a device which assists engine start up without enrichment of", "raw_text": "the air/fuel mixture of the engine, e.g. glow plug, injection timing change, etc.;\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "2.11.", "chapter_title": "Engine capacity means;", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.11.1.", "chapter_title": "For reciprocating piston engines, the nominal engine swept volume;", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.11.2.", "chapter_title": "For rotary piston engines (Wankel), twice the nominal swept volume of a", "raw_text": "combustion chamber per piston."}
{"chapter_id": "2.12.", "chapter_title": "\"Pollution control devices\" means those components of a vehicle that control", "raw_text": "and/or limit exhaust and evaporative emissions."}
{"chapter_id": "2.13.", "chapter_title": "\"OBD\" means an on-board diagnostic system for emission control, which has the", "raw_text": "capability of identifying the likely area of malfunction by means of fault codes stored\nin computer memory."}
{"chapter_id": "2.14.", "chapter_title": "\"In-service test\" means the test and evaluation of conformity conducted in", "raw_text": "accordance with Paragraph 8.2.1. of this Regulation."}
{"chapter_id": "2.15.", "chapter_title": "\"Properly maintained and used\" means, for the purpose of a test vehicle, that such", "raw_text": "a vehicle satisfies the criteria for acceptance of a selected vehicle laid down in\nParagraph 2 of Appendix 3 to this Regulation."}
{"chapter_id": "2.16.", "chapter_title": "\"Defeat Device\" means any element of design which senses temperature, vehicle", "raw_text": "speed, engine rotational speed, transmission gear, manifold vacuum or any other\nparameter for the purpose of activating, modulating, delaying or deactivating the\noperation of any part of the emission control system, that reduces the effectiveness of\nthe emission control system under conditions which may reasonably be expected to\nbe encountered in normal vehicle operation and use.  Such an element of design may\nnot be considered a defeat device if:"}
{"chapter_id": "2.16.1.", "chapter_title": "The need for the device is justified in terms of protecting the engine against", "raw_text": "damage or accident and for safe operation of the vehicle, or"}
{"chapter_id": "2.16.2.", "chapter_title": "The device does not function beyond the requirements of engine starting, or", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.16.3.", "chapter_title": "Conditions are substantially included in the Type I or Type VI test procedures.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.17.", "chapter_title": "\"Family of vehicles\" means a group of vehicle types identified by a parent vehicle", "raw_text": "for the purpose of Annex 12."}
{"chapter_id": "2.18.", "chapter_title": "\"Fuel requirement by the engine\" means the type of fuel normally used by the", "raw_text": "engine:\n\n(a) Petrol (E0 or E5);\n\n(b) LPG (liquefied petroleum gas);\n\n(c) NG (natural gas);\n\n(d) Either petrol or LPG;\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n(e) Either petrol or NG;\n\n(f) Diesel fuel (B0 or B5)."}
{"chapter_id": "2.19.", "chapter_title": "\"Approval of a vehicle\" means the approval of a vehicle type with regard to the", "raw_text": "limitation of the following conditions: (1)"}
{"chapter_id": "2.19.1.", "chapter_title": "Limitation of exhaust emissions by the vehicle, evaporative emissions,", "raw_text": "crankcase emissions, durability of pollution control devices, cold start\npollutant emissions and on-board diagnostics of vehicles fuelled with\nunleaded petrol, or which can be fuelled with either unleaded petrol and LPG\nor NG (Approval B)."}
{"chapter_id": "2.19.2.", "chapter_title": "Limitation of emissions of gaseous and particulate pollutants, durability of", "raw_text": "pollution control devices and on-board diagnostics of vehicles fuelled with\ndiesel fuel (Approval C)."}
{"chapter_id": "2.19.3.", "chapter_title": "Limitation of emissions of gaseous pollutants by the engine, crankcase", "raw_text": "emissions, durability of pollution control devices, cold start emissions and on-\nboard diagnostics of vehicles fuelled with LPG or NG (Approval D)."}
{"chapter_id": "2.20.", "chapter_title": "\"Periodically regenerating system\" means an anti-pollution device (e.g. catalytic", "raw_text": "converter, particulate trap) that requires a periodical regeneration process in less than\n4000 km of normal vehicle operation.  During cycles where regeneration occurs,\nemission standards can be exceeded.  If a regeneration of an anti-pollution device\noccurs at least once per Type I test and that has already regenerated at least once\nduring vehicle preparation cycle, it will be considered as a continuously regenerating\nsystem which does not require a special test procedure.  Annex 13 does not apply to\ncontinuously regenerating systems.\n\nAt the request of the manufacturer, the test procedure specific to periodically regenerating systems will not\napply to a regenerative device if the manufacturer provides data to the type approval authority\nthat, during cycles where regeneration occurs, emissions remain below the standards given in\nParagraph 5.3.1.4. applied for the concerned vehicle category after agreement of the technical\nservice."}
{"chapter_id": "2.21.", "chapter_title": "Hybrid Vehicles (HV)", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.21.1.", "chapter_title": "General Definition of Hybrid Vehicles (HV):", "raw_text": "\"Hybrid vehicle (HV)\" means a vehicle with at least two different energy converters and two different\nenergy storage systems (on vehicle) for the purpose of vehicle propulsion."}
{"chapter_id": "2.21.2.", "chapter_title": "Definition of Hybrid Electric Vehicles (HEV):", "raw_text": "\"Hybrid electric vehicle (HEV)\" means a vehicle that, for the purpose of mechanical propulsion, draws\nenergy from both of the following on-vehicle sources of stored energy/power:\n\n– A consumable fuel\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n– An electrical energy/power storage device (e.g.: battery, capacitor,\nflywheel/generator etc.)"}
{"chapter_id": "2.22.", "chapter_title": "\"Mono-fuel vehicle\" means a vehicle that is designed primarily for permanent", "raw_text": "running on LPG or NG, but may also have a petrol system for emergency purposes\nfor starting only, where the petrol tank does not contain more than 15 litres of petrol;\n\n(1)\nApproval A cancelled.  The 05 series of amendments to this Regulation prohibit the use of leaded petrol."}
{"chapter_id": "2.23.", "chapter_title": "\"Bi-fuel vehicle\" means a vehicle that can run part-time on petrol and also part-time", "raw_text": "on either LPG or NG."}

{"chapter_id": "3.1.", "chapter_title": "The application for approval of a vehicle type with regard to exhaust emissions,", "raw_text": "crankcase emissions, evaporative emissions and durability of pollution control\ndevices, as well as to its on-board diagnostic (OBD) system shall be submitted by the\nvehicle manufacturer or by his authorised representative."}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.1.", "chapter_title": "Should the application concern an on-board diagnostic (OBD) system, it shall", "raw_text": "be accompanied by the additional information required in Paragraph\n4.2.11.2.7of Annex 1, together with:"}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.1.1.", "chapter_title": "A declaration by the manufacturer of:", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.1.1.1.", "chapter_title": "In the case of vehicles equipped with positive-ignition", "raw_text": "engines, the percentage of misfires out of a total number of\nfiring events that would result in emissions exceeding the\nlimits given in Paragraph 3.3.2 of Annex 11, if that percentage\nof misfire had been present from the start of a Type I test as\ndescribed in Paragraph 5.3.1 of Annex 4;"}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.1.1.2.", "chapter_title": "In the case of vehicles equipped with positive-ignition", "raw_text": "engines, the percentage of misfires out of a total number of\nfiring events that could lead to an exhaust catalyst, or\ncatalysts, overheating prior to causing irreversible damage;"}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.1.2.", "chapter_title": "Detailed written information fully describing the functional operation", "raw_text": "characteristics of the OBD system, including a listing of all relevant\nparts of the vehicle's emission control system, i.e. sensors, actuators\nand components, that are monitored by the OBD system;"}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.1.3.", "chapter_title": "A description of the malfunction indicator (MI) used by the OBD", "raw_text": "system to signal the presence of a fault to a driver of the vehicle;\n\nCopies of other type approvals with the relevant data to enable extensions of approvals;"}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.1.4.", "chapter_title": "If applicable, the particulars of the vehicle family as referred to in", "raw_text": "Annex 11, Appendix 2.\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}

If the technical service determines that the submitted vehicle does not\nfully represent the vehicle type or vehicle family described in Annex 11,\nAppendix 2, an alternative and if necessary an additional vehicle shall be\nsubmitted for test in accordance with Paragraph 3 of Annex 11."}

{"chapter_id": "5.1.", "chapter_title": "General", "raw_text": "COUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.1.", "chapter_title": "The components liable to affect the emission of pollutants shall be so", "raw_text": "designed, constructed and assembled as to enable the vehicle, in normal use,\ndespite the vibration to which they may be subjected, to comply with the\nprovisions of this Regulation."}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.2.", "chapter_title": "The technical measures taken by the manufacturer shall be such as to ensure", "raw_text": "that in conformity with the provisions of this Regulation, exhaust gas and\nevaporative emissions are effectively limited throughout the normal life of the\nvehicle and under normal conditions of use.  This will include the security of\nthose hoses and their joints and connections, used within the emission control\nsystems, which shall be so constructed as to conform with the original design\nintent.  For exhaust emissions, these provisions are deemed to be met if the\nprovisions of Paragraphs 5.3.1.4. and 8.2.3.1. respectively are complied with.\nFor evaporative emissions, these conditions are deemed to be met if the\nprovisions of Paragraphs 5.3.1.4. and 8.2.3.1. respectively are complied with."}

{"chapter_id": "5.1.5.", "chapter_title": "Provisions for electronic system security.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.5.1.", "chapter_title": "Any vehicle with an emission control computer shall include features", "raw_text": "to deter modification, except as authorised by the manufacturer.  The\nmanufacturer shall authorise modifications if these modifications are\nnecessary for the diagnosis, servicing, inspection, retrofitting or repair\nof the vehicle.  Any reprogrammable computer codes or operating\nparameters shall be resistant to tampering and afford a level of\nprotection at least as good as the provisions in ISO DIS 15031-7,\ndated October 1998 (SAE J2186 dated October 1996), provided that\nthe security exchange is conducted using the protocols and\ndiagnostic connector as prescribed in Paragraph 6.5 of Annex II,\nAppendix 1.  Any removable calibration memory chips shall be potted,\nencased in a sealed container or protected by electronic algorithms\nand shall not be changeable without the use of specialised tools and\nprocedures."}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.5.2.", "chapter_title": "Computer-coded engine operating parameters shall not be", "raw_text": "changeable without the use of specialised tools and procedures (e.g.\nsoldered or potted computer components or sealed (or soldered)\ncomputer enclosures)."}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.5.3.", "chapter_title": "In the case of mechanical fuel-injection pumps fitted to compression-", "raw_text": "ignition engines, manufacturers shall take adequate steps to protect\nthe maximum fuel delivery setting from tampering while a vehicle is\nin service."}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.5.4.", "chapter_title": "Manufacturers may apply to the approval authority for an exemption", "raw_text": "to one of these requirements for those vehicles which are unlikely to\nrequire protection.  The criteria that the approval authority will\nevaluate in considering an exemption will include, but are not limited\nto, the current availability of performance chips, the high-performance\ncapability of the vehicle and the projected sales volume of the vehicle."}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.5.5.", "chapter_title": "Manufacturers using programmable computer code systems (e.g.", "raw_text": "Electrical Erasable Programmable  Read-Only Memory,\nEEPROM) shall deter  unauthorised reprogramming.\nManufacturers shall include enhanced tamper protection strategies\nand write protect features requiring electronic access to an off-site\ncomputer maintained by the manufacturer.  Methods giving an\nadequate level of tamper protection will be approved by the authority."}

{"chapter_id": "8.2.3.2.1.", "chapter_title": "However, at the request of the manufacturer, the tests may", "raw_text": "be carried out on vehicles which have completed:\n\n− A maximum of 3,000 km for vehicles equipped with a positive-ignition engine,\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n− A maximum of 15,000 km for vehicles equipped with a compression-ignition engine.\n\nIn both these cases, the running-in procedure will be conducted by the manufacturer who shall undertake\nnot to make any adjustments to these vehicles.\n\n\n\nFigure 2"}
{"chapter_id": "8.2.3.2.2.", "chapter_title": "If the manufacturer wishes to run-in the vehicles, (\"x\" km,", "raw_text": "where x ≤ 3,000 km for vehicles equipped with a positive-\nignition engine and x ≤ 15,000 km for vehicles equipped\nwith a compression-ignition engine), the procedure will be\nas follows:\n\n(a) The pollutant emissions (Type I) will be measured at zero and at \"x\" km on the\nfirst tested vehicle,\n\n(b) The evolution coefficient of the emissions between zero and \"x\" km will be\ncalculated for each of the pollutants:\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\nEmissions \" x\" km\n\nEmissions zero km\n\nThis may be less than 1.\n\n(c) The other vehicles will not be run-in, but their zero km emissions will be multiplied\nby the evolution coefficient.\n\nIn this case, the values to be taken will be:\n\n(i) The values at \"x\" km for the first vehicle,\n\n(ii) The values at zero km multiplied by the evolution coefficient for the other vehicles."}

{"chapter_id": "1.", "chapter_title": "INTRODUCTION", "raw_text": "This Appendix sets out the criteria referred to in Paragraph 8.2.7. of this Regulation regarding the selection\nof vehicles for testing and the procedures for the in-service conformity control."}
{"chapter_id": "2.", "chapter_title": "SELECTION CRITERIA", "raw_text": "The criteria for acceptance of a selected vehicle are defined in Paragraphs 2.1. to 2.8. of this Appendix.\nInformation is collected by vehicle examination and an interview with the owner/driver."}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.", "chapter_title": "The vehicle shall belong to a vehicle type that is type approved under this Regulation and", "raw_text": "covered by a certificate of conformity in accordance with the 1958 Agreement.  It shall be\nregistered and used in a country of the Contracting Parties."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.", "chapter_title": "The vehicle shall have been in service for at least 15,000 km or 6 months, whichever is", "raw_text": "the later, and for no more than 80,000 km or 5 years, whichever is the sooner."}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.", "chapter_title": "There shall be a maintenance record to show that the vehicle has been properly", "raw_text": "maintained,\ne.g. has been serviced in accordance with the manufacturer's recommendations."}
{"chapter_id": "2.4.", "chapter_title": "The vehicle shall exhibit no indications of abuse (e.g. racing, overloading, misfuelling, or", "raw_text": "other misuse), or other factors (e.g. tampering) that could affect emission performance.\nIn the case of vehicles fitted with an OBD system, the fault code and mileage information\nstored in the computer is taken into account.  A vehicle shall not be selected for testing if\nthe information stored in the computer shows that the vehicle has operated after a fault\ncode was stored and a relatively prompt repair was not carried out."}
{"chapter_id": "2.5.", "chapter_title": "There shall have been no unauthorised major repair to the engine or major repair of the", "raw_text": "vehicle."}
{"chapter_id": "2.6.", "chapter_title": "The lead content and sulphur content of a fuel sample from the vehicle tank shall meet", "raw_text": "applicable standards and there shall be no evidence of misfuelling.  Checks may be done\nin the exhaust, etc.\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "2.7.", "chapter_title": "There shall be no indication of any problem that might jeopardise the safety of laboratory", "raw_text": "personnel."}
{"chapter_id": "2.8.", "chapter_title": "All anti-pollution system components on the vehicle shall be in conformity with the", "raw_text": "applicable type approval."}
{"chapter_id": "3.", "chapter_title": "DIAGNOSIS AND MAINTENANCE", "raw_text": "Diagnosis and any normal maintenance necessary shall be performed on vehicles accepted for testing,\nprior to measuring exhaust emissions, in accordance with the procedure laid down in Paragraphs"}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.", "chapter_title": "to 3.7. below.", "raw_text": "\n3.1.The following checks shall be carried out: checks on air filter, all drive belts, all fluid levels,\nradiator cap, all vacuum hoses and electrical wiring related to the anti-pollution system\nfor integrity; checks on ignition, fuel metering and anti-pollution device components for\nmaladjustments and/or tampering. {"chapter_id": "3.2.", "chapter_title": "The OBD system shall be checked for proper functioning. If the\nOBD malfunction indicator registers a malfunction during a preconditioning cycle, the fault\nmay be identified and repaired.  The test may be re-run and the results of that repaired\nvehicle used."}
{"chapter_id": "3.3.", "chapter_title": "The ignition system shall be checked and defective components replaced, for example", "raw_text": "spark plugs, cables, etc."}
{"chapter_id": "3.4.", "chapter_title": "The compression shall be checked.  If the result is unsatisfactory the vehicle is rejected.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.5.", "chapter_title": "The engine parameters shall be checked to the manufacturer's specifications and", "raw_text": "adjusted if necessary."}
{"chapter_id": "3.6.", "chapter_title": "If the vehicle is within 800 km of a scheduled maintenance service, that service shall be", "raw_text": "performed according to the manufacturer's instructions. {"chapter_id": "3.7.", "chapter_title": "Upon acceptance of the vehicle, the fuel shall be replaced with appropriate emission test", "raw_text": "reference fuel, unless the manufacturer accepts the use of market fuel."}
{"chapter_id": "3.8.", "chapter_title": "In the case of vehicles equipped with periodically regenerating systems as defined in", "raw_text": "Paragraph 2.20., it shall be established that the vehicle is not approaching a regeneration\nperiod. {"chapter_id": "3.8.1.", "chapter_title": "If this is the case, the vehicle must be driven until the end of the regeneration. {"chapter_id": "2.", "chapter_title": "Two different procedures are to be followed:", "raw_text": "(i) One dealing with vehicles identified in the sample, due to an emission-related defect,\ncausing outliers in the results (Paragraph 3 below).\n\n(ii) The other deals with the total sample (Paragraph 4 below)."}
{"chapter_id": "3.", "chapter_title": "PROCEDURE TO BE FOLLOWED WITH OUTLYING EMITTERS IN THE SAMPLE (1)", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.", "chapter_title": "With a minimum sample size of three and a maximum sample size as determined by the", "raw_text": "procedure of Paragraph 4, a vehicle is taken at random from the sample and the\nemissions of the regulated pollutants are measured to determine if it is an outlying emitter."}
{"chapter_id": "3.2.", "chapter_title": "A vehicle is said to be an outlying emitter when the conditions given in either Paragraph", "raw_text": ""}

{"chapter_id": "3.2.2.", "chapter_title": "In the case of a vehicle that has been type-approved according to the limit", "raw_text": "values given in Row B of the table in Paragraph 5.3.1.4, an outlying emitter is\na vehicle where the applicable limit value for any regulated pollutant is\nexceeded by a factor of 1.5."}
{"chapter_id": "3.2.3.", "chapter_title": "In the specific case of a vehicle with a measured emission for any regulated", "raw_text": "pollutant within the 'intermediate zone' (2)."}
{"chapter_id": "3.2.3.1.", "chapter_title": "If the vehicle meets the conditions of this Paragraph, the cause of the", "raw_text": "excess emission must be determined and another vehicle is then taken\nat random from the sample.\n\n(1)\nOn the basis of actual in-service data to be supplied before December 31, 2003, the requirements of this Paragraph may be\nreviewed and consider\n(a) whether the definition of outlying emitter needs to be revised with respect to vehicles that have been type-\napproved according to the limit values given in Row B of the table in Paragraph 5.3.1.4,\n(b) whether the procedure for identifying outlying emitters should be amended and\n(c) whether the procedures for in-service conformity testing should be replaced at an appropriate time by a new\nstatistical procedure.  If appropriate it will be proposed the necessary amendments.\n(2)\nFor any vehicle, the \"intermediate zone\" is determined as follows:\nThe vehicle shall meet the conditions given in either Paragraph 3.2.1 or Paragraph 3.2.2 and, in addition, the measured value for the\nsame regulated pollutant shall be below a level that is determined from the product of the limit value for the same regulated\npollutant given in Row A of the table in Paragraph 5.3.1.4 multiplied by a factor of 2.5."}
{"chapter_id": "3.2.3.2.", "chapter_title": "Where more than one vehicle meets the condition of this Paragraph,", "raw_text": "the administrative department and the manufacturer must determine if\nthe excess emission from both vehicles is due to the same cause or\nnot."}
{"chapter_id": "3.2.3.2.1.", "chapter_title": "If the administrative department and the manufacturer both", "raw_text": "agree that the excess emission is due to the same cause, the\nsample is regarded as having failed and the plan of remedial\nmeasures outlined in Paragraph 6 of Appendix 3 applies."}
{"chapter_id": "3.2.3.2.2.", "chapter_title": "If the administrative department and the manufacturer can not", "raw_text": "agree on either the cause of the excess emission from an\nindividual vehicle or whether the causes for more than one\nvehicle are the same, another vehicle is taken at random from\nthe sample, unless the maximum sample size has already\nbeen reached."}

{"chapter_id": "4.", "chapter_title": "PROCEDURE TO BE FOLLOWED WITHOUT SEPARATE EVALUATION OF OUTLYING", "raw_text": "EMITTERS IN THE SAMPLE"}
{"chapter_id": "4.1.", "chapter_title": "With a minimum sample size of three the sampling procedure is set so that the probability", "raw_text": "of a batch passing a test with 40% of the production defective is 0.95 (producer's risk =\n5%) while the probability of a batch being accepted with 75% of the production defective\nis 0.15 (consumer's risk = 15%)."}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.", "chapter_title": "For each of the pollutants given in the table of Paragraph 5.3.1.4 of this Regulation, the", "raw_text": "following procedure is used (see Figure 4/2 below).\n\nWhere:\n\nL = The limit value for the pollutant,\n\nxi = The value of the measurement for the i-th vehicle of the sample,\nn = The current sample\nnumber.\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.", "chapter_title": "The test statistic quantifying the number of non-conforming vehicles, i. e. xi > L, is", "raw_text": "computed for the sample."}
{"chapter_id": "4.4.", "chapter_title": "Then:", "raw_text": "(i) If the test statistic does not exceed the pass decision number for the sample size\ngiven in the following table, a pass decision is reached for the pollutant,\n\n(ii) If the test statistic equals or exceeds the fail decision number for the sample size\ngiven in the following table, a fail decision is reached for the pollutant,\n\n(iii) Otherwise, an additional vehicle is tested and the procedure is applied to the sample\nwith one extra unit.\n\nIn the following table the pass and fail decision numbers are computed in accordance with the International\nStandard ISO 8422:1991."}

{"chapter_id": "1.", "chapter_title": "INTRODUCTION", "raw_text": "This Annex describes the procedure for the Type I test defined in Paragraph 5.3.1 of this\nRegulation.  When the reference fuel to be used is LPG or NG, the provisions of Annex 12\nshall apply additionally.  When the vehicle is equipped with a periodically regenerating system\nas defined in Paragraph 2.20., the provisions of Annex 13 shall apply."}
{"chapter_id": "2.", "chapter_title": "OPERATING CYCLE ON THE CHASSIS DYNAMOMETER", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.", "chapter_title": "Description of the Cycle", "raw_text": "The operating cycle on the chassis dynamometer shall be that indicated in the Appendix 1 to\nthis Annex."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.", "chapter_title": "General Conditions Under which the Cycle is Carried Out", "raw_text": "Preliminary testing cycles should be carried out if necessary to determine how best to actuate\nthe accelerator and brake controls so as to achieve a cycle approximating to the theoretical\ncycle within the prescribed limits."}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.", "chapter_title": "Use of the Gearbox", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.1.", "chapter_title": "If the maximum speed which can be attained in first gear is below 15 km/h,", "raw_text": "the second, third and fourth gears shall be used for the urban cycle (Part\nOne) and the second, third, fourth and fifth gears for the extra-urban cycle\n(Part Two).  The second, third and fourth gears may also be used for the\nurban cycle (Part One) and the second, third, fourth and fifth gears for the\nextra-urban cycle (Part Two) when the manufacturer's instructions\nrecommend starting in second gear on level ground, or when first gear is\ntherein defined as a gear reserved for cross-country driving, crawling or\ntowing.\n\nVehicles which do not attain the acceleration and maximum speed values required in the\noperating cycle shall be operated with the accelerator control fully depressed until they once\nagain reach the required operating curve.  Deviations from the operating cycle shall be\nrecorded in the test report."}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.2.", "chapter_title": "Vehicles equipped with semi-automatic-shift gearboxes shall be tested by", "raw_text": "using the gears normally employed for driving, and the gear shift is used in\naccordance with the manufacturer's instructions."}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.3.", "chapter_title": "Vehicles equipped with automatic-shift gearboxes shall be tested with the", "raw_text": "highest gear (\"Drive\") engaged.  The accelerator shall be used in such a way\nas to obtain the steadiest acceleration possible, enabling the various gears\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nto be engaged in the normal order. Furthermore, the gear-change points\nshown in Appendix 1 to this Annex shall not apply; acceleration shall\ncontinue throughout the period represented by the straight line connecting\nthe end of each period of idling with the beginning of the next following period\nof steady speed.  The tolerances given in Paragraph 2.4 below shall apply."}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.4.", "chapter_title": "Vehicles equipped with an overdrive which the driver can actuate shall be", "raw_text": "tested with the overdrive out of action for the urban cycle (Part One) and with\nthe overdrive in action for the extra-urban cycle (Part Two)."}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.5.", "chapter_title": "At the request of the manufacturer, for a vehicle type where the idle speed", "raw_text": "of the engine is higher than the engine speed that would occur during\nOperations 5, 12 and 24 of the elementary urban cycle (Part One), the clutch\nmay be disengaged during the previous operation."}
{"chapter_id": "2.4.", "chapter_title": "Tolerances", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.4.1.", "chapter_title": "A tolerance of ± 2 km/h shall be allowed between the indicated speed and", "raw_text": "the theoretical speed during acceleration, during steady speed, and during\ndeceleration when the vehicle's brakes are used.  If the vehicle decelerates\nmore rapidly without the use of the brakes, only the provisions of Paragraph\n6.5.3below shall apply.  Speed tolerances greater than those prescribed\nshall be accepted during phase changes provided that the tolerances are\nnever exceeded for more than 0.5 s on any one occasion."}
{"chapter_id": "2.4.2.", "chapter_title": "The time tolerances shall be ± 1.0 s.  The above tolerances shall apply", "raw_text": "equally at the beginning and at the end of each gear-changing period (1) for\nthe urban cycle (Part One) and for the Operations No.3, 5 and 7 of the extra-\nurban cycle (Part Two)."}
{"chapter_id": "2.4.3.", "chapter_title": "The speed and time tolerances shall be combined as indicated in Appendix", "raw_text": "\n1to this Annex."}

{"chapter_id": "3.2.", "chapter_title": "Fuel", "raw_text": "When testing a vehicle against the emission limit values given in Row A of the table in\nParagraph 5.3.1.4 of this Regulation, the appropriate reference fuel must comply with the\nspecifications given in Paragraph 1 of Annex 10 or, in the case of gaseous reference fuels,\neither Paragraph 1.1.1 or Paragraph 1.2 of Annex 10a.\n\nWhen testing a vehicle against the emission limit values given in Row B of the table in\nParagraph 5.3.1.4 of this Regulation, the appropriate reference fuel must comply with the\nspecifications given in Paragraph 2 of Annex 10 or, in the case of gaseous reference fuels,\neither Paragraph 1.1.2 or Paragraph 1.2 of Annex 10a."}

{"chapter_id": "4.", "chapter_title": "TEST EQUIPMENT", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "4.1.", "chapter_title": "Chassis Dynamometer", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "4.1.1.", "chapter_title": "The dynamometer shall be capable of simulating road load within one of the", "raw_text": "following classifications:\n\nDynamometer with fixed load curve, i.e. a dynamometer whose physical characteristics\nprovide a fixed load curve shape,\n\nDynamometer with adjustable load curve, i.e. a dynamometer with at least two road load\nparameters that can be adjusted to shape the load curve."}
{"chapter_id": "4.1.2.", "chapter_title": "The setting of the dynamometer shall not be affected by the lapse of time.  It", "raw_text": "shall not produce any vibrations perceptible to the vehicle and likely to impair\nthe vehicle's normal operations."}
{"chapter_id": "4.1.3.", "chapter_title": "It shall be equipped with means to simulate inertia and load. These", "raw_text": "simulators are connected to the front roller in the case of a two-roller\ndynamometer.\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "4.1.4.", "chapter_title": "Accuracy", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "4.1.4.1.", "chapter_title": "It shall be possible to measure and read the indicated load to an", "raw_text": "accuracy of ± 5%."}
{"chapter_id": "4.1.4.2.", "chapter_title": "In the case of a dynamometer with a fixed load curve, the accuracy", "raw_text": "of the load setting at 80 km/h must be ± 5%.  In the case of a\ndynamometer with adjustable load curve, the accuracy of matching\ndynamometer load to road load shall be ± 5% at 120, 100, 80, 60\nand\n40km/h and ± 10% at 20 km/h.  Below this, dynamometer absorption shall be positive."}
{"chapter_id": "4.1.4.3.", "chapter_title": "The total inertia of the rotating parts (including the simulated inertia", "raw_text": "where applicable) shall be known and shall be within ± 20 kg of the\ninertia class for the test."}
{"chapter_id": "4.1.4.4.", "chapter_title": "The speed of the vehicle shall be measured by the speed of rotation", "raw_text": "of the roller (the front roller in the case of a two-roller dynamometer).\nIt shall be measured with an accuracy of ± 1 km/h at speeds above\n10km/h."}
{"chapter_id": "4.1.4.5.", "chapter_title": "The distance actually driven by the vehicle shall be measured by the", "raw_text": "movement of rotation of the roller (the front roller in the case of a\ntwo-roller dynamometer)."}
{"chapter_id": "4.1.5.", "chapter_title": "Load and Inertia Setting", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "4.1.5.1.", "chapter_title": "Dynamometer with fixed load curve: the load simulator shall be", "raw_text": "adjusted to absorb the power exerted on the driving wheels at a\nsteady speed of 80 km/h and the absorbed power at 50 km/h shall\nbe noted.  The means by which this load is determined and set are\ndescribed in Appendix 3 to this Annex."}
{"chapter_id": "4.1.5.2.", "chapter_title": "Dynamometer with adjustable load curve: the load simulator shall be", "raw_text": "adjusted in order to absorb the power exerted on the driving wheels\nat steady speeds of 120, 100, 80, 60, 40 and 20 km/h.  The means\nby which these loads are determined and set are described in\nAppendix 3 to this Annex."}
{"chapter_id": "4.1.5.3.", "chapter_title": "Inertia", "raw_text": "Dynamometers with electric inertia simulation shall be demonstrated to be equivalent to\nmechanical inertia systems.  The means by which equivalence is established are described\nin Appendix 4 to this Annex."}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.", "chapter_title": "Exhaust Gas-sampling System", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.1.", "chapter_title": "The exhaust gas-sampling system shall be able to measure the actual", "raw_text": "quantities of pollutants emitted in the exhaust gases to be measured.  The\nsystem that shall be used is the constant volume sampler (CVS) system.\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nThis requires that the vehicle exhaust be continuously diluted with ambient\nair under controlled conditions.  In the constant volume sampler concept of\nmeasuring mass emissions, two conditions shall be satisfied, the total\nvolume of the mixture of exhaust and dilution air shall be measured and a\ncontinuously proportional sample of the volume shall be collected for\nanalysis.  The quantities of pollutants are determined from the sample\nconcentrations, corrected for the pollutant content of the ambient air and the\ntotalised flow over the test period.\n\nThe particulate pollutant emission level is determined by using suitable filters to collect the\nparticulates from a proportional part flow throughout the test and determining the quantity\nthereof gravimetrically in accordance with Paragraph 4.3.1.1."}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.2.", "chapter_title": "The flow through the system shall be sufficient to eliminate water", "raw_text": "condensation at all conditions which may occur during a test, as defined in\nAppendix 5 to this Annex."}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.3.", "chapter_title": "Appendix 5 gives examples of three types of constant volume sampler", "raw_text": "system which satisfy the requirements of this Annex."}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.4.", "chapter_title": "The gas and air mixture shall be homogeneous at Point S2 of the sampling", "raw_text": "probe."}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.5.", "chapter_title": "The probe shall extract a true sample of the diluted exhaust gases.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.6.", "chapter_title": "The system shall be free of gas leaks.  The design and materials shall be", "raw_text": "such that the system does not influence the pollutant concentration in the\ndiluted exhaust gas.  Should any component (heat exchanger, blower, etc.)\nchange the concentration of any pollutant gas in the diluted gas, the\nsampling for that pollutant shall be carried out before that component if the\nproblem cannot be corrected."}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.7.", "chapter_title": "If the vehicle being tested is equipped with an exhaust pipe comprising", "raw_text": "several branches, the connecting tubes shall be connected as near as\npossible to the vehicle without adversely affecting his operation."}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.8.", "chapter_title": "Static pressure variations at the exhaust(s) of the vehicle shall remain within", "raw_text": "± 1.25 kPa of the static pressure variations measured during the\ndynamometer driving cycle and with no connection to the exhaust(s).\nSampling systems capable of maintaining the static pressure to within ± 0.25\nkPa are used if a written request from a manufacturer to the administration\ngranting the approval substantiates the need for the closer tolerance.  The\nback-pressure shall be measured in the exhaust pipe as near as possible to\nits end or in an extension having the same diameter."}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.9.", "chapter_title": "The various valves used to direct the exhaust gases shall be of a quick-", "raw_text": "adjustment, quick-acting type."}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.10.", "chapter_title": "The gas samples are collected in sample bags of adequate capacity. These", "raw_text": "bags shall be made of such materials as will not change the pollutant gas by\nmore than ± 2% after 20 minutes of storage.\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.", "chapter_title": "Analytical Equipment", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.1.", "chapter_title": "Provisions", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.1.1.", "chapter_title": "Pollutant gases shall be analysed with the following instruments:", "raw_text": "Carbon monoxide (CO) and carbon dioxide (CO2) analysis: analysers shall be of the non-\ndispersive infra-red (NDIR) absorption type.\n\nHydrocarbons (HC) analysis - spark-ignition engines: the analyser shall be of the flame\nionisation (FID) type calibrated with propane gas expressed equivalent to carbon atoms\n(C1).\n\nHydrocarbons (HC) analysis - compression-ignition engines: the analyser shall be of the\nflame ionisation type with detector, valves, pipework, etc., heated to 463 K (190° C) ± 10 K\n(HFID).  It shall be calibrated with propane gas expressed equivalent to carbon atoms (C1).\n\nNitrogen oxide (NOx) analysis: the analyser shall be either of the chemi-luminescent (CLA)\nor of the non-dispersive ultra-violet resonance absorption (NDUVR) type, both with an NOx-\nNO converter.\n\nParticulates:\n\nGravimetric determination of the particulates collected.\nThese particulates shall in each case be collected by two series-mounted filters in the sample\ngas flow.  The quantity of particulates collected by each pair of filters shall be as follows:\n\nV V\nM = mix ×m → m = M× ×d ep\nVep × d Vmix\nwhere:\n\nVep: flow through filters;\n\nVmix: flow through tunnel;\n\nM: particulate mass (g/km);\n\nMlimit: limit mass of particulates (limit mass in force, g/km);\nm: mass of particulates collected by filters (g);\nd: distance corresponding to the operating cycle (km).\n\nThe particulates sample rate (Vep/Vmix) shall be adjusted so that for\n\nM = Mlimit, 1 ≤ m ≤ 5 mg (when 47 mm diameter filters are used).\n\nThe filter surface shall consist of a material that is hydrophobic and inert towards the\ncomponents of the exhaust gas (fluorocarbon coated glass fibre filters or equivalent).\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.1.2.", "chapter_title": "Accuracy", "raw_text": "The analysers shall have a measuring range compatible with the accuracy required to\nmeasure the concentrations of the exhaust gas sample pollutants.\n\nMeasurement error shall not exceed ± 2% (intrinsic error of analyser) disregarding the true\nvalue for the calibration gases.\n\nFor concentrations of less than 100 ppm the measurement error shall not exceed ± 2 ppm.\n\nThe ambient air sample shall be measured on the same analyser with an appropriate range.\n\nThe microgram balance used to determine the weight of all filters shall have an accuracy of\n5µg (standard deviation) and readability of 1 µg."}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.1.3.", "chapter_title": "Ice-trap", "raw_text": "No gas drying device shall be used before the analysers unless shown to have no effect on\nthe pollutant content of the gas stream."}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.2.", "chapter_title": "Particular Requirements for Compression-ignition Engines", "raw_text": "A heated sample line for a continuous HC-analysis with the flame ionisation detector (HFID),\nincluding recorder (R) shall be used.  The average concentration of the measured\nhydrocarbons shall be determined by integration.  Throughout the test, the temperature of\nthe heated sample line shall be controlled at 463 K (190° C) ± 10 K. The heated sampling\nline shall be fitted with a heated filter (FH) 99% efficient with particles ≥ 0.3 µm, to extract any\nsolid particles from the continuous flow of gas required for analysis.\n\nThe sampling system response time (from the probe to the analyser inlet) shall be no more\nthan four seconds.\n\nThe HFID shall be used with a constant flow (heat exchanger) system to ensure a\nrepresentative sample, unless compensation for varying CFV or CFO flow is made.\n\nThe particulate sampling unit shall consist of a dilution tunnel, a sampling probe, a filter unit,\na partial-flow pump, and flow rate regulators and measuring units.  The particulate-sampling\npart flow is drawn through two series-mounted filters.  The sampling probe for the test gas\nflow for particulates shall be so arranged within the dilution tract that a representative sample\ngas flow can be taken from the homogeneous air/exhaust mixture and an air/exhaust gas\nmixture temperature of 325 K (52° C) is not exceeded immediately before the particulate filter.\nThe temperature of the gas flow in the flow meter may not fluctuate by more than ± 3 K, nor\nmay the mass flow rate fluctuate by more than ± 5%.  Should the volume of flow change\nunacceptably as a result of excessive filter loading, the test shall be stopped.  When it is\nrepeated, the rate of flow shall be decreased and/or a larger filter used.  The filters shall be\nremoved from the chamber no earlier than an hour before the test begins.\n\nThe necessary particle filters shall be conditioned (as regards temperature and humidity) in\nan open dish which has been protected against dust ingress for at least 8 and for not more\nthan 56 hours before the test in an air-conditioned chamber.  After this conditioning the\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nuncontaminated filters will be weighed and stored until they are used.  If the filters are not\nused within one hour of their removal from the weighing chamber they shall be re-weighed.\n\nThe one-hour limit may be replaced by an eight-hour limit if one or both of the following\nconditions are met;\n\nA stabilised filter is placed and kept in a sealed filter holder assembly with the ends plugged,\nor;\n\nA stabilised filter is placed in a sealed filter holder assembly which is then immediately placed\nin a sample line through which there is no flow."}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.3.", "chapter_title": "Calibration", "raw_text": "Each analyser shall be calibrated as often as necessary and in any case in the month before\ntype-approval testing and at least once every six months for verifying conformity of\nproduction.\n\nThe calibration method to be used is described in Appendix 6 to this Annex for the analysers\nreferred to in Paragraph 4.3.1. above."}
{"chapter_id": "4.4.", "chapter_title": "Volume Measurement", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "4.4.1.", "chapter_title": "The method of measuring total dilute exhaust volume incorporated in the constant volume sampler", "raw_text": "shall be such that measurement is accurate to ± 2%."}
{"chapter_id": "4.4.2.", "chapter_title": "Constant Volume Sampler Calibration", "raw_text": "The constant volume sampler system volume measurement device shall be calibrated by a\nmethod sufficient to ensure the prescribed accuracy and at a frequency sufficient to maintain\nsuch accuracy.\n\nAn example of a calibration procedure which will give the required accuracy is given in\nAppendix 6 to this Annex.  The method shall utilise a flow metering device which is dynamic\nand suitable for the high flow-rate encountered in constant volume sampler testing.  The\ndevice shall be of certified accuracy traceable to an approved national or international\nstandard."}
{"chapter_id": "4.5.", "chapter_title": "Gases", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "4.5.1.", "chapter_title": "Pure Gases", "raw_text": "The following pure gases shall be available, if necessary, for calibration and operation:\npurified nitrogen: (purity ± 1 ppm C, ± 1 ppm CO, ± 400 ppm CO2, ± 0.1 ppm NO);\n\npurified synthetic air: (purity ± 1 ppm C, ± 1 ppm CO, ± 400 ppm CO2, ± 0.1 ppm NO);\noxygen content between 18 and 21% volume;\npurified oxygen (purity ≥ 99.5% vol O2);\npurified hydrogen (and mixture containing helium): (purity ± 1 ppm C, ± 400 ppm CO2);\ncarbon monoxide: (minimum purity 99.5%);\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\npropane: (minimum purity 99.5%)."}
{"chapter_id": "4.5.2.", "chapter_title": "Calibration and Span Gases", "raw_text": "Mixtures of gases having the following chemical compositions shall be available:\n\nC3H8 and purified synthetic air (see Paragraph 4.5.1 of this Annex);\n\nCO and purified nitrogen;\n\nCO2 and purified nitrogen;\n\nNO and purified nitrogen.  (The amount of NO2 contained in this calibration gas shall not\nexceed 5% of the NO content.)\n\nThe true concentration of a calibration gas shall be within ± 2% of the stated figure.\n\nThe concentrations specified in Appendix 6 to this Annex may also be obtained by means of\na gas divider, diluting with purified N2 or with purified synthetic air.  The accuracy of the mixing\ndevice shall be such that the concentrations of the diluted calibration gases may be\ndetermined to within ± 2%."}
{"chapter_id": "4.6.", "chapter_title": "Additional Equipment", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "4.6.1.", "chapter_title": "Temperatures", "raw_text": "The temperatures indicated in Appendix 8 shall be measured with an accuracy of ± 1.5 K."}
{"chapter_id": "4.6.2.", "chapter_title": "Pressure", "raw_text": "The atmospheric pressure shall be measurable to within ± 0.1 kPa."}
{"chapter_id": "4.6.3.", "chapter_title": "Absolute Humidity", "raw_text": "The absolute humidity (H) shall be measurable to within ± 5%.\n\nThe exhaust gas-sampling system shall be verified by the method described in Paragraph 3 of Appendix\n7to this Annex.\nThe maximum permissible deviation between the quantity of gas introduced and the quantity\nof gas measured is 5%."}

{"chapter_id": "5.3.", "chapter_title": "Conditioning of Vehicle", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "5.3.1.", "chapter_title": "For compression-ignition engined vehicles for the purpose of measuring", "raw_text": "particulates, at most 36 hours and at least 6 hours before testing, the Part\nTwo cycle described in Appendix 1 to this Annex shall be used. {"chapter_id": "6.", "chapter_title": "PROCEDURE FOR BENCH TESTS", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "6.1.", "chapter_title": "Special Conditions for Carrying Out the Cycle", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "6.1.1.", "chapter_title": "During the test, the test cell temperature must be between 293 K (20° C) and", "raw_text": "303 K (30° C). The absolute humidity (H) of either the air in the test cell or\nthe intake air of the engine shall be such that:\n5.5≤ H ≤ 12.2 (g H2O/kg dry air)"}
{"chapter_id": "6.1.2.", "chapter_title": "The vehicle shall be approximately horizontal during the test so as to avoid", "raw_text": "any abnormal distribution of the fuel."}
{"chapter_id": "6.1.3.", "chapter_title": "A current of air of variable speed shall be blown over the vehicle.  The blower", "raw_text": "speed shall be within the operating range of 10 km/h to at least 50 km/h, or\nas an alternative, at the request of the manufacturer, within the operating\nrange of 10 km/h to at least the maximum speed of the test cycle being used.\nThe linear velocity of the air at the blower outlet shall be within ± 5 km/h of\nthe corresponding roller speed within the range of 10 km/h to 50 km/h.  At\nthe range over 50 km/h, the linear velocity of the air shall be within ± 10 km/h\nof the corresponding roller speed.  At roller speeds of less than 10 km/h, air\nvelocity may be zero.\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\nThe above mentioned air velocity shall be determined as an averaged value of a number of\nmeasuring points which:\n\n(a) For blowers with rectangular outlets are located at the centre of each rectangle\ndividing the whole of the blower outlet into 9 areas (dividing both horizontal and vertical\nsides of the blower outlet into 3 equal parts);\n\n(b) For circular blower outlets, the outlet shall be divided into 8 equal arcs by vertical,\nhorizontal and 45° lines.  The measurement points lie on the radial centre line of\neach arc (22.5°) at a radius of two thirds of the total (as shown in the diagram\nbelow).\n\n\n\nThese measurements shall be made with no vehicle or other obstruction in front of the fan.\n\nThe device used to measure the linear velocity of the air shall be located at between 0 and 20 cm from\nthe air outlet.\n\nThe final selection of the blower shall have the following characteristics:\n\n(c) Area: at least 0.2 m2;\n\n(d) Height of the lower edge above ground: approximately 20 cm;\n\n(e) Distance from the front of the vehicle: approximately 30 cm.\n\nAs an alternative, at the request of the manufacturer the blower speed shall be fixed at an air speed of at\nleast 6 m/s (21.6 km/h).\n\nThe height and lateral position of the cooling fan can also be modified at the request of the\nmanufacturer."}
{"chapter_id": "6.1.4.", "chapter_title": "During the test the speed is recorded against time or collected by the data-", "raw_text": "acquisition system so that the correctness of the cycles performed can be\nassessed."}

{"chapter_id": "6.5.", "chapter_title": "Decelerations", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "6.5.1.", "chapter_title": "All decelerations of the elementary urban cycle (Part One) shall be effected", "raw_text": "by removing the foot completely from the accelerator, the clutch remaining\nengaged.  The clutch shall be disengaged, without use of the gear lever, at\nthe higher of the following speeds: 10 km/h or the speed corresponding to\nthe engine idle speed.\n\nAll decelerations of the extra-urban cycle (Part Two) shall be effected by removing the foot\ncompletely from the accelerator, the clutch remaining engaged.  The clutch shall be\ndisengaged, without use of the gear lever, at a speed of 50 km/h for the last deceleration."}
{"chapter_id": "6.5.2.", "chapter_title": "If the period of deceleration is longer than that prescribed for the", "raw_text": "corresponding phase, the vehicle's brakes shall be used to enable the timing\nof the cycle to be complied with.\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "6.5.3.", "chapter_title": "If the period of deceleration is shorter than that prescribed for the", "raw_text": "corresponding phase, the timing of the theoretical cycle shall be restored by\nconstant speed or idling period merging into the following operation."}

{"chapter_id": "7.2.2.", "chapter_title": "Prior to each sample analysis, the analyser range to be used for each", "raw_text": "pollutant shall be set to zero with the appropriate zero gas."}

{"chapter_id": "1.1.", "chapter_title": "Introduction", "raw_text": "In the event that the total resistance to progress on the road cannot be reproduced on the chassis\ndynamometer between speeds of 10 km/h and 120 km/h, it is recommended that a chassis dynamometer\nhaving the characteristics defined below should be used."}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.", "chapter_title": "Definition", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.1.", "chapter_title": "The chassis dynamometer may have one or two rollers.", "raw_text": "The front roller shall drive, directly or indirectly, the inertial masses and the power absorption device."}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.2.", "chapter_title": "The load absorbed by the brake and the chassis dynamometer internal frictional effects", "raw_text": "between the speeds of 0 and 120 km/h is as follows:\n\nF = (a + b × V2) ± 0.1 x F80 (without being negative)\nwhere:\n\nF = total load absorbed by the chassis dynamometer (N)\n\na = value equivalent to rolling resistance (N)\n\nb = value equivalent to coefficient of air resistance [N/(km/h) 2]\n\nV = speed (km/h)\n\nF80 = load at 80 km/h (N)."}
{"chapter_id": "2.", "chapter_title": "METHOD OF CALIBRATING THE DYNAMOMETER", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.", "chapter_title": "Introduction", "raw_text": "This Appendix describes the method to be used to determine the load absorbed by a dynamometric brake.\nThe load absorbed comprises the load absorbed by frictional effects and the load absorbed by the power-\nabsorption device.\n\nThe dynamometer is brought into operation beyond the range of test speeds.  The device used for starting\nup the dynamometer is then disconnected: the rotational speed of the driven roller decreases.\n\nThe kinetic energy of the rollers is dissipated by the power-absorption unit and by the frictional effects.\nThis method disregards variations in the roller's internal frictional effects caused by rollers with or without\nthe vehicle.  The frictional effects of the rear roller shall be disregarded when the roller is free."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.", "chapter_title": "Calibration of the Load Indicator to 80 km/h as a Function of the Load Absorbed", "raw_text": "COUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nThe following procedure shall be used (see also Figure 2/1)."}

{"chapter_id": "2.", "chapter_title": "PRINCIPLE", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.", "chapter_title": "Drawing up Working Equations", "raw_text": "Since the dynamometer is subjected to variations in the rotating speed of the roller(s), the force at the\nsurface of the roller(s) can be expressed by the formula:\n\nF = I x γ = IM x γ + F1\nwhere:\n\nF = force at the surface of the roller(s),\n\nI = total inertia of the dynamometer (equivalent inertia of the vehicle: see the table in Paragraph 5.1),\n\nIM = inertia of the mechanical masses of the dynamometer,\nγ =  tangential acceleration at roller surface,\n\nF1 = inertia force.\n\nNote: An explanation of this formula with reference to dynamometers with mechanically simulated inertias\nis appended.\n\nThus, total inertia is expressed as follows:\n\nF1\nI = IM +\nγ\nwhere:\n\nIM can be calculated or measured by traditional methods,\n\nF1 can be measured on the dynamometer,\n\nγ can be calculated from the peripheral speed of the rollers.\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nThe total inertia (I) will be determined during an acceleration or deceleration test with values higher than\nor equal to those obtained on an operating cycle."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.", "chapter_title": "Specification for the Calculation of Total Inertia", "raw_text": "The test and calculation methods shall make it possible to determine the total inertia I with a relative error\n(Δ I/I) of less than ± 2%."}

{"chapter_id": "3.1.2.", "chapter_title": "± 2% of the theoretical value for the average value calculated for each sequence of the cycle.", "raw_text": ""}

{"chapter_id": "2.", "chapter_title": "CRITERIA RELATING TO THE VARIABLE-DILUTION SYSTEM FOR MEASURING", "raw_text": "EXHAUST-GAS EMISSIONS"}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.", "chapter_title": "Scope", "raw_text": "COUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nThis section shall specify the operating characteristics of an exhaust-gas sampling system intended to be\nused for measuring the true mass emissions of a vehicle exhaust in accordance with the provisions of this\nRegulation.\n\nThe principle of variable-dilution sampling for measuring mass emissions shall require three conditions to\nbe satisfied:"}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.1.", "chapter_title": "The vehicle exhaust gases shall be continuously diluted with ambient air under specified", "raw_text": "conditions;"}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.2.", "chapter_title": "The total volume of the mixture of exhaust gases and dilution air shall be measured", "raw_text": "accurately;"}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.3.", "chapter_title": "A continuously proportional sample of the diluted exhaust gases and the dilution air shall", "raw_text": "be collected for analysis.\n\nMass gaseous emissions shall be determined from the proportional sample concentrations and the total\nvolume measured during the test.  The sample concentrations shall be corrected to take account of the\npollutant content of the ambient air.\n\nIn addition, where vehicles are equipped with compression-ignition engines, their particulate emissions\nshall be plotted."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.", "chapter_title": "Technical Summary", "raw_text": "Figure 5/1 gives a schematic diagram of the sampling system."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.1.", "chapter_title": "The vehicle exhaust gases shall be diluted with a sufficient amount of ambient air to", "raw_text": "prevent any water condensation in the sampling and measuring system."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.2.", "chapter_title": "The exhaust-gas sampling system shall be so designed as to make it possible to measure", "raw_text": "the average volume concentrations of the CO2, CO, HC and NOx, and, in addition, in the\ncase of vehicles equipped with compression-ignition engines, of the particulate emissions,\ncontained in the exhaust gases emitted during the vehicle testing cycle."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.3.", "chapter_title": "The mixture of air and exhaust gases shall be homogeneous at the point where the", "raw_text": "sampling probe is located (see Paragraph 2.3.1.2. below)."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.4.", "chapter_title": "The probe shall extract a representative sample of the diluted gases.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.5.", "chapter_title": "The system shall enable the total volume of the diluted exhaust gases to be measured.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.6.", "chapter_title": "The sampling system shall be gas-tight.  The design of the variable-dilution sampling", "raw_text": "system and the materials that go to make it up shall be such that they do not affect the\npollutant concentration in the diluted exhaust gases.  Should any component in the system\n(heat exchanger, cyclone separator, blower, etc.) change the concentration of any of the\npollutants in the diluted exhaust gases and the fault cannot be corrected, then sampling\nfor that pollutant shall be carried out upstream from that component.\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.7.", "chapter_title": "If the vehicle tested is equipped with an exhaust system with several outlets, the", "raw_text": "connecting tubes shall be connected by a manifold installed as near as possible to the\nvehicle."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.8.", "chapter_title": "The gas samples shall be collected in sampling bags of adequate capacity so as not to", "raw_text": "hinder the gas flow during the sampling period.  These bags shall be made of materials\nwhich will not affect the concentration of pollutant gases (see Paragraph 2.3.4.4. below)."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.9.", "chapter_title": "The variable-dilution system shall be so designed as to enable the exhaust gases to be", "raw_text": "sampled without appreciably changing the back-pressure at the exhaust pipe outlet (see\nParagraph 2.3.1.1. below).\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\n\nFigure 5/1\n\nDiagram of a Variable-Dilution System for Measuring Exhaust Gas Emissions"}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.", "chapter_title": "Specific Requirements", "raw_text": "COUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.1.", "chapter_title": "Exhaust-Gas Collection and Dilution Device", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.1.1.", "chapter_title": "The connecting tube between the vehicle exhaust outlets and the mixing chamber", "raw_text": "shall be as short as possible; it shall in no event:\n\n(i) Cause the static pressure at the exhaust outlets on the vehicle being tested to differ by more than ±\n0.75 kPa at 50 km/h or more than ± 1.25 kPa for the whole duration of the test from the static\npressures recorded when nothing is connected to the vehicle exhaust outlets.  The pressure shall\nbe measured in the exhaust outlet or in an extension having the same diameter, as near as possible\nto the end of the pipe;\n\n(ii) Change the nature of the exhaust gas."}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.1.2.", "chapter_title": "Provision shall be made for a mixing chamber in which the vehicle exhaust gases", "raw_text": "and the dilution air are mixed so as to produce a homogeneous mixture at the\nchamber outlet.\n\nThe homogeneity of the mixture in any cross-paragraph at the location of the sampling probe shall not vary\nby more than ± 2% from the average of the values obtained for at least five points located at equal intervals\non the diameter of the gas stream.  In order to minimise the effects on the conditions at the exhaust outlet\nand to limit the drop in pressure inside the dilution-air conditioning device, if any, the pressure inside the\nmixing chamber shall not differ by more than ± 0.25 kPa from atmospheric pressure."}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.2.", "chapter_title": "Suction Device/Volume Measuring Device", "raw_text": "This device may have a range of fixed speeds as to ensure sufficient flow to prevent any water\ncondensation.  This result is generally obtained by keeping the concentration of CO2 in the dilute exhaust-\ngas sampling bag lower than 3% by volume."}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.3.", "chapter_title": "Volume Measurement", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.3.1.", "chapter_title": "The volume measuring device shall retain its calibration accuracy to within ± 2%", "raw_text": "under all operating conditions. {"chapter_id": "2.3.3.2.", "chapter_title": "A temperature sensor shall be installed immediately before the volume measuring", "raw_text": "device. {"chapter_id": "2.3.3.3.", "chapter_title": "The pressure measurements shall have a precision and an accuracy of ± 0.4 kPa", "raw_text": "during the test."}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.3.4.", "chapter_title": "The measurement of the pressure difference from atmospheric pressure shall be", "raw_text": "taken upstream from and, if necessary, downstream from the volume measuring\ndevice.\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}

{"chapter_id": "3.1.1.", "chapter_title": "The positive displacement pump - constant volume sampler (PDP-CVS) satisfies the", "raw_text": "requirements of this Annex by metering the flow of gas through the pump at constant\ntemperature and pressure.  The total volume is measured by counting the revolutions\nmade by the calibrated positive displacement pump.  The proportional sample is achieved\nby sampling with pump, flow-meter and flow control valve at a constant flow-rate."}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.2.", "chapter_title": "Figure 5/3 is a schematic drawing of such a sampling system.  Since various", "raw_text": "configurations can produce accurate results, exact conformity with the drawing is not\nessential.  Additional components such as instruments, valves, solenoids and switches\nmay be used to provide additional information and co-ordinate the functions of the\ncomponent system."}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.3.", "chapter_title": "The sampling equipment consists of:", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.3.1.", "chapter_title": "A filter (D) for the dilution air, which can be preheated if necessary.  This filter", "raw_text": "shall consist\nof activated charcoal sandwiched between two layers of paper, and shall be used to reduce and stabilise\nthe hydrocarbon concentrations of ambient emissions in the dilution air;"}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.3.2.", "chapter_title": "A mixing chamber (M) in which exhaust gas and air are mixed homogeneously;", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.3.3.", "chapter_title": "A heat exchanger (H) of a capacity sufficient to ensure that throughout the test", "raw_text": "the temperature of the air/exhaust-gas mixture measured at a point immediately\nupstream of the positive displacement pump is within 6 K of the designed\noperating temperature.  This device shall not affect the pollutant concentrations\nof diluted gases taken off after for analysis;"}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.3.4.", "chapter_title": "A temperature control system (TC), used to preheat the heat exchanger before", "raw_text": "the test and to control its temperature during the test, so that deviations from the\ndesigned operating temperature are limited to 6 K;"}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.3.5.", "chapter_title": "The positive displacement pump (PDP), producing a constant-volume flow of the", "raw_text": "air/exhaust-gas mixture; the flow capacity of the pump shall be large enough to\neliminate water condensation in the system under all operating conditions which\nmay occur during a test; this can be generally ensured by using a positive\ndisplacement pump with a flow capacity:"}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.3.5.1.", "chapter_title": "twice as high as the maximum flow of exhaust gas produced by", "raw_text": "accelerations of the driving cycle, or"}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.3.5.2.", "chapter_title": "sufficient to ensure that the CO2 concentration in the dilute-exhaust", "raw_text": "sample bag is less than 3% by volume for petrol and diesel, less than\n2.2% by volume for LPG and less than 1.5% by volume for NG."}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.3.6.", "chapter_title": "A temperature sensor (T1) (accuracy and precision ± 1 K), fitted immediately", "raw_text": "upstream of the volume meter and used to register the pressure difference\nbetween the gas mixture and the ambient air;\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}

{"chapter_id": "3.1.3.8.", "chapter_title": "Another pressure gauge (G2) (accuracy and precision ± 0.4 kPa) fitted so that the", "raw_text": "differential pressure between pump inlet and pump outlet can be registered;"}

{"chapter_id": "3.2.", "chapter_title": "Critical-flow Venturi Dilution Device (CFV-CVS) (Figure 5/4)", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.2.1.", "chapter_title": "The use of a critical-flow venturi in connection with the CVS sampling procedure is based", "raw_text": "on the principles of flow mechanics for critical flow.  The variable mixture flow rate of\ndilution and exhaust gas is maintained at sonic velocity which is directly proportional to\nthe square root of the gas temperature.  Flow is continually monitored, computed and\nintegrated throughout the test.\n\nThe use of an additional critical-flow sampling venturi ensures the proportionality of the gas samples taken.\nAs both pressure and temperature are equal at the two venturi inlets the volume of the gas flow diverted\nfor sampling is proportional to the total volume of diluted exhaust-gas mixture produced, and thus the\nrequirements of this Annex are met.\n\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\nFigure 5/3\n\nConstants Volume Sampler with Positive Displacement Pump (PDP-CVS)\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\n\nFigure 5/4\n\nConstant Volume Sampler with Critical-flow Venturi (CFV-CVS System)"}
{"chapter_id": "3.2.2.", "chapter_title": "Figure 5/4 is a schematic drawing of such a sampling system.  Since various", "raw_text": "configurations can produce accurate results, exact conformity with the drawing is not\nessential.  Additional components such as instruments, valve, solenoids, and switches\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nmay be used to provide additional information and co-ordinate the functions of the\ncomponent system."}
