{"chapter_id": "1.", "chapter_title": "ESTABLISHMENT OF THE CALIBRATION CURVE", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "1.1.", "chapter_title": "Each normally used operating range is calibrated in accordance with the requirements of", "raw_text": "Paragraph 4.3.3. of Annex 4 by the following procedure:"}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.", "chapter_title": "The analyser calibration curve is established by at least five calibration points spaced as uniformly", "raw_text": "as possible.  The nominal concentration of the calibration gas of the highest concentration shall\nbe not less than 80% of the full scale."}
{"chapter_id": "1.3.", "chapter_title": "The calibration curve is calculated by the least squares method.  If the resulting polynomial degree", "raw_text": "is greater than 3, the number of calibration points shall be at least equal to this polynomial degree\nplus 2."}
{"chapter_id": "1.4.", "chapter_title": "The calibration curve shall not differ by more than ± 2% from the nominal value of each calibration", "raw_text": "gas."}
{"chapter_id": "1.5.", "chapter_title": "Trace of the Calibration Curve", "raw_text": "From the trace of the calibration curve and the calibration points, it is possible to verify that the calibration\nhas been carried out correctly.  The different characteristic parameters of the analyser shall be indicated,\nparticularly:\nthe scale,\nthe sensitivity,\nthe zero point,\nthe date of carrying out the calibration."}
{"chapter_id": "1.6.", "chapter_title": "If it can be shown to the satisfaction of the technical service that alternative technology (e.g.", "raw_text": "computer, electronically controlled range switch, etc.) can give equivalent accuracy, then these\nalternatives may be used."}
{"chapter_id": "1.7.", "chapter_title": "Verification of the Calibration", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "1.7.1.", "chapter_title": "Each normally used operating range shall be checked prior to each analysis in accordance", "raw_text": "with the following:"}
{"chapter_id": "1.7.2.", "chapter_title": "The calibration shall be checked by using a zero gas and a span gas whose nominal value", "raw_text": "is within 80-95% of the supposed value to be analysed.\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "1.7.3.", "chapter_title": "If, for the two points considered, the value found does not differ by more than ± 5% of the", "raw_text": "full scale from the theoretical value, the adjustment parameters may be modified.  Should\nthis not be the case, a new calibration curve shall be established in accordance with\nParagraph 1 of this Appendix."}
{"chapter_id": "1.7.4.", "chapter_title": "After testing, zero gas and the same span gas are used for re-checking.  The analysis is", "raw_text": "considered acceptable if the difference between the two measuring results is less than\n2%."}
{"chapter_id": "2.", "chapter_title": "CHECKING FOR FID HYDROCARBON RESPONSE", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.", "chapter_title": "Detector Response Optimisation", "raw_text": "The FID shall be adjusted, as specified by the instrument manufacturer.  Propane in air should be used,\nto optimise the response, on the most common operating range."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.", "chapter_title": "Calibration of the HC Analyser", "raw_text": "The analyser should be calibrated using propane in air and purified synthetic air.  See Paragraph 4.5.2. of\nAnnex 4 (calibration and span gases).\n\nEstablish a calibration curve as described in Paragraphs 1.1. to 1.5. of this Appendix."}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.", "chapter_title": "Response Factors of Different Hydrocarbons and Recommended Limits", "raw_text": "The response factor (Rf), for a particular hydrocarbon species is the ratio of the FID C1 reading to the gas\ncylinder concentration, expressed as ppm C1.\n\nThe concentration of the test gas shall be at a level to give a response of approximately 80% of full-scale\ndeflection, for the operating range.  The concentration shall be known, to an accuracy of ± 2% in reference\nto a gravimetric standard expressed in volume.  In addition, the gas cylinder shall be pre-conditioned for\n24hours at a temperature between\n293 K and 303 K (20 and 30° C).\n\nResponse factors should be determined when introducing an analyser into service and thereafter at major\nservice intervals.  The test gases to be used and the recommended response factors are:\n\nMethane and purified air 1.00 < Rf < 1.15\n\nor 1.00 < Rf < 1.05 for NG fuelled vehicles\n\nPropylene and purified air 0.90 < Rf < 1.00\n\nToluene and purified air 0.90 < Rf < 1.00\n\nRelative to a response factor (Rf) of 1.00 for propane and purified air."}
{"chapter_id": "2.4.", "chapter_title": "Oxygen Interference Check and Recommended Limits", "raw_text": "The response factor shall be determined as described in Paragraph 2.3. above.  The test gas to be used\nand recommended response factor range is:\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\nPropane and nitrogen 0.95 < Rf < 1.05"}
{"chapter_id": "3.", "chapter_title": "EFFICIENCY TEST OF THE NOx CONVERTER", "raw_text": "The efficiency of the converter-used for the conversion of NO2 into NO is tested as follows:\n\nUsing the test set up as shown in Figure 6/1 and the procedure described below, the efficiency of\nconverters can be tested by means of an ozonator."}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.", "chapter_title": "Calibrate the analyser in the most common operating range following the manufacturer's", "raw_text": "specifications using zero and span gas (the NO content of which shall amount to about 80% of the\noperating range and the NO2 concentration of the gas mixture shall be less than 5% of the NO\nconcentration).  The NOx analyser shall be in the NO mode so that the span gas does not pass\nthrough the converter.  Record the indicated concentration."}
{"chapter_id": "3.2.", "chapter_title": "Via a T-fitting, oxygen or synthetic air is added continuously to the span gas flow until the", "raw_text": "concentration indicated is about 10% less than the indicated calibration concentration given in\nParagraph 3.1. above  Record the indicated concentration (C).  The ozonator is kept deactivated\nthroughout this process."}
{"chapter_id": "3.3.", "chapter_title": "The ozonator is now activated to generate enough ozone to bring the NO concentration down to", "raw_text": "20% (minimum 10%) of the calibration concentration given in Paragraph 3.1.\nabove.  Record the indicated concentration (d)."}
{"chapter_id": "3.4.", "chapter_title": "The NOx analyser is then switched to the NOx mode, which means that the gas mixture (consisting", "raw_text": "of NO, NO2, O2 and N2) now passes through the converter.  Record the indicated concentration\n(a)."}
{"chapter_id": "3.5.", "chapter_title": "The ozonator is now deactivated.  The mixture of gases described in Paragraph 3.2. above passes", "raw_text": "through the converter into the detector.  Record the indicated concentration (b).\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\nFigure 6/1\n\nDiagram of NOx Converter Efficiency Devices"}
{"chapter_id": "3.6.", "chapter_title": "With the ozonator deactivated, the flow of oxygen or synthetic air is also shut off.  The NO2 reading", "raw_text": "of the analyser shall then be no more than 5% above the figure given in Paragraph 3.1. above."}
{"chapter_id": "3.7.", "chapter_title": "The efficiency of the NOx converter is calculated as follows:", "raw_text": "Efficiency (%) = ⎜⎜⎛1+\nac −− bd ⎞⎟⎟⎠ × 100\n⎝"}
{"chapter_id": "3.8.", "chapter_title": "The efficiency of the converter shall not be less than 95%.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.9.", "chapter_title": "The efficiency of the converter shall be tested at least once a week.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "4.", "chapter_title": "CALIBRATION OF THE CVS SYSTEM", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "4.1.", "chapter_title": "The CVS system shall be calibrated by using an accurate flow-meter and a restricting device.  The", "raw_text": "flow through the system shall be measured at various pressure readings and the control\nparameters of the system measured and related to the flows."}
{"chapter_id": "4.1.1.", "chapter_title": "Various types of flow-meter may be used, e.g. calibrated venturi, laminar flow-meter,", "raw_text": "calibrated turbine-meter, provided that they are dynamic measurement systems and can\nmeet the requirements of Paragraphs 4.4.1. and 4.4.2. of Annex 4.\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "4.1.2.", "chapter_title": "The following Paragraphs give details of methods of calibrating PDP and CFV units, using", "raw_text": "a laminar flow-meter, which gives the required accuracy, together with a statistical check\non the calibration validity."}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.", "chapter_title": "Calibration of the Positive Displacement Pump (PDP)", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.1.", "chapter_title": "The following calibration procedure outlines the equipment, the test configuration and the", "raw_text": "various parameters which are measured to establish the flow-rate of the CVS pump.  All\nthe parameters related to the pump are simultaneously measured with the parameters\nrelated to the flow-meter which is connected in series with the pump.  The calculated flow-\nrate (given in m3/min at pump inlet, absolute pressure and temperature) can then be\nplotted versus a correlation function which is the value of a specific combination of pump\nparameters.  The linear equation which relates the pump flow and the correlation function\nis then determined.  In the event that a CVS has a multiple speed drive, a calibration for\neach range used shall be performed."}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.2.", "chapter_title": "This calibration procedure is based on the measurement of the absolute values of the", "raw_text": "pump and flow-meter parameters that relate the flow-rate at each point.  Three conditions\nshall be maintained to ensure the accuracy and integrity of the calibration curve:"}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.2.1.", "chapter_title": "The pump pressures shall be measured at tappings on the pump rather than at", "raw_text": "the external piping on the pump inlet and outlet.  Pressure taps that are mounted\nat the top centre and bottom centre of the pump drive headplate are exposed to\nthe actual pump cavity pressures, and therefore reflect the absolute pressure\ndifferentials;"}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.2.2.", "chapter_title": "Temperature stability shall be maintained during the calibration.  The laminar flow-", "raw_text": "meter is sensitive to inlet temperature oscillations which cause the data points to\nbe scattered.  Gradual changes of ± 1 K in temperature are acceptable as long as\nthey occur over a period of several minutes;"}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.2.3.", "chapter_title": "All connections between the flow-meter and the CVS pump shall be free of any", "raw_text": "leakage."}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.3.", "chapter_title": "During an exhaust emission test, the measurement of these same pump parameters", "raw_text": "enables the user to calculate the flow-rate from the calibration equation."}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.3.1.", "chapter_title": "Figure 6/2 of this Appendix shows one possible test set-up.  Variations are", "raw_text": "permissible, provided that they are approved by the administration granting the\napproval as being of comparable accuracy.  If the set-up shown in Appendix 5,\nFigure 5/3, is used, the following data shall be found within the limits of precision\ngiven:\n\nbarometric pressure (corrected) (Pb) ± 0.03 kPa\n\nambient temperature (T) ± 0.2 K\n\nair temperature at LFE (ETI) ± 0.15 K\npressure depression upstream of LFE (EPl) ± 0.01 kPa\npressure drop across the LFE matrix (EDP) ± 0.0015 kPa\nair temperature at CVS pump inlet (PTI) ± 0.2 K\nair temperature at CVS pump outlet (PTO) ± 0.2 K\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\npressure depression at CVS pump inlet (PPI) ± 0.22 kPa\npressure head at CVS pump outlet (PPO) ± 0.22 kPa\npump revolutions during test period (n) ± 1 1/min\nelapsed time for period (minimum 250 s) (t) ± 0.1 s"}

{"chapter_id": "4.2.4.2.", "chapter_title": "The air flow-rate is then converted to pump flow (Vo) in m3/rev at absolute pump inlet temperature and pressure.", "raw_text": "Q T\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nVo = S × p × 101.33 n 273.2 Pp\nwhere:\n\nVo = pump flow-rate at Tp and Pp given in m3/rev,\n\nQs = air flow at 101.33 kPa and 273.2 K given in m3/min,\n\nTp = pump inlet temperature (K),\n\nPp = absolute pump inlet pressure (kPa),\n\nn = pump speed in min-1.\nTo compensate for the interaction of pump speed pressure variations at the pump and the pump slip rate,\nthe correlation function (xo) between the pump speed (n), the pressure differential from pump inlet to pump\noutlet and the absolute pump outlet pressure is then calculated as follows:\n1∆ Pp\nxo = n Pe\nwhere:\nxo = correlation function,\n\nΔPp  = pressure differential from pump inlet to pump outlet (kPa),\n\nPe = absolute outlet pressure (PPO + Pb)(kPa).\n\nA linear least-square fit is performed to generate the calibration equations which have the formulae:\n\nVo = Do - M (xo)\nn  = A - B (ΔPp)\n\nDo, M, A and B are the slope-intercept constants describing the lines.\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\n\nFigure 6/3\n\nCFV-CVS Calibration Configuration"}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.4.3.", "chapter_title": "A CVS system that has multiple speeds shall be calibrated on each speed used.  The calibration curves", "raw_text": "generated for the ranges shall be approximately parallel and the intercept values (Do) shall increase as the\npump flow range decreases.\n\nIf the calibration has been performed carefully, the calculated values from the equation will be within ±\n0.5% of the measured value of Vo.  Values of M will vary from one pump to another. Calibration is\nperformed at pump start-up and after major maintenance."}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.", "chapter_title": "Calibration of the Critical-Flow Venturi (CFV)", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.1.", "chapter_title": "Calibration of the CFV is based upon the flow equation for a critical venturi:", "raw_text": "Qs = K v × P\n\nwhere:\n\nQs = flow,\n\nKv = calibration coefficient,\n\nP = absolute pressure (KPa),\n\nT = absolute temperature (K).\nT\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\nGas flow is a function of inlet pressure and temperature.\n\nThe calibration procedure described below establishes the value of the calibration coefficient at measured\nvalues of pressure, temperature and air flow."}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.2.", "chapter_title": "The manufacturer's recommended procedure shall be followed for calibrating electronic portions of the CFV.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.3.", "chapter_title": "Measurements for flow calibration of the critical flow venturi are required and the following data shall be found", "raw_text": "within the limits of precision given:\n\nbarometric pressure (corrected) (Pb) ± 0.03 kPa,\n\nLFE air temperature, flow-meter (ETI) ± 0.15 K,\npressure depression upstream of LFE (EPI) ± 0.01 kPa,\n\npressure drop across (EDP) LFE matrix ± 0.0015 kPa,\n\nair flow (Qs) ± 0.5%,\n\nCFV inlet depression (PPI) ± 0.02 kPa,\ntemperature at venturi inlet (Tv) ± 0.2 K."}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.4.", "chapter_title": "The equipment shall be set up as shown in Figure 3 of this Appendix and checked for leaks. Any leaks between", "raw_text": "the flow-measuring device and the critical flow venturi will seriously affect the accuracy of the calibration."}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.5.", "chapter_title": "The variable-flow restrictor shall be set to the open position, the blower shall be started and the system stabilised.", "raw_text": "Data from all instruments shall be recorded."}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.6.", "chapter_title": "The flow restrictor shall be varied and at least eight readings across the critical flow range of the venturi", "raw_text": "shall be made."}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.7.", "chapter_title": "The data recorded during the calibration shall be used in the following calculations.", "raw_text": "The air flow-rate (Qs) at each test point is calculated from the flow-meter data using the manufacturer's prescribed\nmethod.\n\nCalculate values of the calibration coefficient for each test point:\n\nK v = Qs × Tv\nPv\nwhere:\n\nQs =  flow-rate in m3/min at 273.2 K and 101.33 kPa,\n\nTv =  temperature at the venturi inlet (K),\n\nPv =  absolute pressure at the venturi inlet (kPa).\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nPlot Kv, as a function of venturi inlet pressure.  For sonic flow, Kv will have a relatively constant value.  As\npressure decreases (vacuum increases) the venturi becomes unchoked and Kv decreases.  The resultant\nKv changes are not permissible.\n\nFor a minimum of eight points in the critical region, calculate an average Kv and the standard deviation.\n\nIf the standard deviation exceeds 0.3% of the average Kv, take corrective action."}
{"chapter_id": "1.", "chapter_title": "To comply with the requirements of Paragraph 4.7. of Annex 4, the total accuracy of the CVS sampling", "raw_text": "system and analytical system shall be determined by introducing a known mass of a pollutant gas into the\nsystem whilst it is being operated as if during a normal test and then analysing and calculating the\npollutant mass according to the formulae in Appendix 8 to Annex 4 except that the density of propane\nshall be taken as 1.967 grams per litre at standard conditions. {"chapter_id": "2.", "chapter_title": "METERING A CONSTANT FLOW OF PURE GAS (CO OR C3H8) USING A CRITICAL", "raw_text": "FLOW ORIFICE DEVICE"}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.", "chapter_title": "A known quantity of pure gas (CO or C3H8) is fed into the CVS system through the calibrated", "raw_text": "critical orifice. If the inlet pressure is high enough, the flow-rate (q), which is adjusted by means of\nthe critical flow orifice, is independent of orifice outlet pressure (critical flow).  If deviations\nexceeding 5% occur, the cause of the malfunction shall be determined and corrected.  The CVS\nsystem is operated as in an exhaust emission test for about 5 to 10 minutes.  The gas collected in\nthe sampling bag is analysed by the usual equipment and the results compared to the\nconcentration of the gas samples which was known beforehand."}
{"chapter_id": "3.", "chapter_title": "METERING A LIMITED QUANTITY OF PURE GAS (CO OR C3H8) BY MEANS OF A", "raw_text": "GRAVIMETRIC TECHNIQUE"}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.", "chapter_title": "The following gravimetric procedure may be used to verify the CVS system.", "raw_text": "The weight of a small cylinder filled with either carbon monoxide or propane is determined with a precision of ± 0.01 g.\nFor about 5 to 10 minutes, the CVS system is operated as in a normal exhaust emission test, while CO or\npropane is injected into the system.  The quantity of pure gas involved is determined by means of\ndifferential weighing.  The gas accumulated in the bag is then analysed by means of the equipment\nnormally used for exhaust-gas analysis.  The results are then compared to the concentration figures\ncomputed previously."}

{"chapter_id": "3.4.2.", "chapter_title": "A current of air of variable speed shall be blown over the vehicle.  The blower speed shall", "raw_text": "be, within the operating range of 10 km/h to at least 50 km/h, or as an alternative, at the\nrequest of the manufacturer within the operating range of 10 km/h to at least the maximum\nspeed of the test cycle being used.  The linear velocity of the air at the blower outlet shall\nbe within ± 5 km/h of the corresponding roller speed within the range of 10 km/h to 50\nkm/h.  At the range over 50 km/h, the linear velocity of the air shall be within ± 10 km/h of\nthe corresponding roller speed.  At roller speeds of less than 10 km/h, air velocity may be\nzero.\n\nThe above mentioned air velocity shall be determined as an averaged value of a number of measuring points which:\n\n(a) For blowers with rectangular outlets are located at the centre of each rectangle dividing\nthe whole of the blower outlet into 9 areas (dividing both horizontal and vertical sides of\nthe blower outlet into 3 equal parts).\n\n(b) For circular blower outlets, the outlet shall be divided into 8 equal arcs by vertical,\nhorizontal and 45° lines.  The measurement points lie on the radial centre line of each\narc (22.5°) at a radius of two thirds of the total (as shown in the diagram below).\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\nThese measurements shall be made with no vehicle or other obstruction in front of the fan.\n\nThe device used to measure the linear velocity of the air shall be located at between 0 and 20 cm from the air outlet.\n\nThe final selection of the blower shall have the following characteristics:\n\n(c) Area: at least 0.2 m2;\n\n(d) Height of the lower edge above ground: approximately 0.2 m;\n\n(e) Distance from the front of the vehicle: approximately 0.3 m.\n\nAs an alternative, at the request of the manufacturer the blower speed shall be fixed at an air speed of at least 6 m/s\n(21.6 km/h).\n\nThe height and lateral position of the cooling fan can also be modified at the request of the manufacturer."}

{"chapter_id": "6.1.3.", "chapter_title": "Use of the Gearbox", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "6.1.3.1.", "chapter_title": "If the maximum speed which can be attained in first gear is below 15 km/h, the second, third and fourth gears", "raw_text": "shall be used for the urban cycle (Part One) and the second, third, fourth and fifth gears for the extra-urban\ncycle (Part Two).  The second, third and fourth gears may also be used for the urban cycle (Part One) and\nthe second, third, fourth and fifth gears for the extra-urban cycle (Part Two) when the manufacturer's\ninstructions recommend starting in second gear on level ground, or when first gear is therein defined as a\ngear reserved for cross-country driving, crawling or towing.\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nVehicles which do not attain the acceleration and maximum speed values required in the operating cycle shall be\noperated with the accelerator control fully depressed until they once again reach the required operating\ncurve.  Deviations from the operating cycle shall be recorded in the test report.\n\nVehicles equipped with semi-automatic-shift gearboxes shall be tested by using the gears normally employed for\ndriving, and the gear shift is used in accordance with the manufacturer's instructions."}
{"chapter_id": "6.1.3.2.", "chapter_title": "Vehicles equipped with automatic-shift gearboxes shall be tested with the highest gear (\"Drive\") engaged.  The", "raw_text": "accelerator shall be used in such a way as to obtain the steadiest acceleration possible, enabling the\nvarious gears to be engaged in the normal order. Furthermore, the gear-change points shown in Tables 1\nand 2 of this Annex shall not apply; acceleration shall continue throughout the period represented by the\nstraight line connecting the end of each period of idling with the beginning of the next following period of\nsteady speed.  The tolerances given in Paragraphs 6.1.3.4. and 6.1.3.5. below shall apply."}
{"chapter_id": "6.1.3.3.", "chapter_title": "Vehicles equipped with an overdrive that the driver can actuate shall be tested with the overdrive out of action", "raw_text": "for the urban cycle (Part One) and with the overdrive in action for the extra-urban cycle (Part Two)."}
{"chapter_id": "6.1.3.4.", "chapter_title": "A tolerance of ± 2 km/h shall be allowed between the indicated speed and the theoretical speed during", "raw_text": "acceleration, during steady speed, and during deceleration when the vehicle's brakes are used.  If the\nvehicle decelerates more rapidly without the use of the brakes, only the provisions of Paragraph 6.4.4.3.\nbelow shall apply.  Speed tolerances greater than those prescribed shall be accepted during phase\nchanges provided that the tolerances are never exceeded for more than 0.5 s on any one occasion."}
{"chapter_id": "6.1.3.5.", "chapter_title": "The time tolerances shall be ± 1.0 s.  The above tolerances shall apply equally at the beginning and at the end", "raw_text": "of each gear-changing period for the urban cycle (Part One) and for the operations Nos.3, 5 and 7 of the\nextra-urban cycle (Part Two).  It should be noted that the time of two seconds allowed includes the time\nfor changing gear and, if necessary, a certain amount of latitude to catch up with the cycle."}
{"chapter_id": "6.2.", "chapter_title": "Test Preparation", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "6.2.1.", "chapter_title": "Load and Inertia Setting", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "6.2.1.1.", "chapter_title": "Load Determined with Vehicle Road Test", "raw_text": "The dynamometer shall be adjusted so that the total inertia of the rotating masses will simulate the inertia and other\nroad load forces acting on the vehicle when driving on the road.  The means by which this load is\ndetermined is described in Paragraph 5. of this Annex.\n\nDynamometer with fixed load curve: the load simulator shall be adjusted to absorb the power exerted on the driving\nwheels at a steady speed of 80 km/h and the absorbed power at 50 km/h shall be noted.\n\nDynamometer with adjustable load curve: the load simulator shall be adjusted in order to absorb the power exerted on\nthe driving wheels at steady speeds of 120, 100, 80, 60 and 40 and 20 km/h."}
{"chapter_id": "6.2.1.2.", "chapter_title": "Load Determined by Vehicle Reference Mass", "raw_text": "With the manufacturer's agreement the following method may be used.\n\nThe brake is adjusted so as to absorb the load exerted at the driving wheels at a constant speed of 80 km/h, in\naccordance with Table 3.\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nIf the corresponding equivalent inertia is not available on the dynamometer, the larger value closest to the vehicle\nreference mass will be used.\n\nIn the case of vehicles other than passenger cars, with a reference mass of more than 1,700 kg or vehicles with\npermanent all-wheel drive, the power values given in Table 3 are multiplied by a factor 1.3."}
{"chapter_id": "6.2.1.3.", "chapter_title": "The method used and the values obtained (equivalent inertia − characteristic adjustment parameter) shall be", "raw_text": "recorded in the test report."}

{"chapter_id": "6.2.3.", "chapter_title": "Tyre Pressures", "raw_text": "The tyre pressures shall be the same as that specified by the manufacturer and used for the preliminary road test for\nbrake adjustment. The actual pressure used shall be recorded\nin the test report."}
{"chapter_id": "6.2.4.", "chapter_title": "Background Particulate Mass Measurement", "raw_text": "The particulate background level of the dilution air may be determined by passing filtered dilution air through the\nparticulate filter.  This shall be drawn from the same point as the particulate sample.  One measurement\nmay be performed prior to or after the test. Particulate mass measurements may be corrected by\nsubtracting the background contribution from the dilution system.  The permissible background contribution\nshall be ≤ 1 mg/km (or equivalent mass on the filter).  If the background exceeds this level, the default\nfigure of 1 mg/km (or equivalent mass on the filter) shall be employed.  Where subtraction of the\nbackground contribution gives a negative result, the particulate mass result shall be considered to be zero."}
{"chapter_id": "6.2.5.", "chapter_title": "Background Particle Number Measurements", "raw_text": "The subtraction of background particle numbers may be determined by sampling dilution air drawn from a point\ndownstream of the particle and hydrocarbon filters into the particle number measurement system.\nBackground correction of particle number measurements shall not be allowed for type approval, but may\nbe used at the manufacturer's request for conformity of production and in service conformity where there\nare indications that tunnel contribution is significant."}
{"chapter_id": "6.2.6.", "chapter_title": "Particulate Mass Filter Selection", "raw_text": "A single particulate filter without back-up shall be employed for both urban and extra-urban phases of the cycle\ncombined.\n\nTwin particulate filters, one for the urban, one for the extra-urban phase, may be used without back-up filters, only\nwhere the pressure-drop increase across the sample filter between the beginning and the end of the\nemissions test is otherwise expected to exceed 25 kPa."}

{"chapter_id": "6.3.1.", "chapter_title": "For the purpose of measuring particulates, at most 36 hours and at least 6 hours before testing, the Part Two", "raw_text": "cycle described in Paragraph 6.1. of this Annex shall be used for vehicle pre-conditioning. {"chapter_id": "6.5.3.", "chapter_title": "Bag Analysis", "raw_text": ""}

{"chapter_id": "6.6.", "chapter_title": "Calculation of Emissions", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "6.6.1.", "chapter_title": "Determination of Volume", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "6.6.1.1.", "chapter_title": "Calculation of the volume when a variable dilution device with constant flow control by orifice or venturi is used.", "raw_text": "Record continuously the parameters showing the volumetric flow, and calculate the total volume for the duration of the\ntest."}
{"chapter_id": "6.6.1.2.", "chapter_title": "Calculation of volume when a positive displacement pump is used", "raw_text": "The volume of diluted exhaust gas measured in systems comprising a positive displacement pump is\ncalculated with the following formula:\n\nV = Vo · N\nwhere:\n\nV = volume of the diluted gas expressed in litres per test (prior to correction),\n\nVo = volume of gas delivered by the positive displacement pump in testing conditions in litres per revolution,\n\nN = number of revolutions per test."}
{"chapter_id": "6.6.1.3.", "chapter_title": "Correction of Volume to Standard Conditions", "raw_text": "COUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nThe diluted exhaust-gas volume is corrected by means of the following formula:\n\nVmix = V ⋅ K1 ⋅ ⎛⎜⎜⎝ PBT−p P1 ⎟⎠⎞⎟ (1)\nwhere:\n\nK1 = = 2.6961 (2)\n\nPB = barometric pressure in the test room in kPa,\n\nP1 = vacuum at the inlet to the positive displacement pump in kPa relative to the ambient barometric pressure,\n\nTp = average temperature of the diluted exhaust gas entering the positive displacement pump during the test (K)."}
{"chapter_id": "6.6.2.", "chapter_title": "Total Mass of Gaseous and Particulate Pollutants Emitted", "raw_text": "The mass M of each pollutant emitted by the vehicle during the test shall be determined by obtaining the product of the\nvolumetric concentration and the volume of the gas in question, with due regard for the following densities\nunder above-mentioned reference conditions:\n\nIn the case of carbon monoxide (CO): d = 1.25 g/l\n\nIn the case of hydrocarbons:\n\nfor petrol (CH1.85) d = 0.619 g/1 for diesel (CH1.86) d\n= 0.619 g/1  for LPG (CH2.525) d = 0.649 g/l  for NG (CH4) d\n= 0.714 g/l\n\nIn the case of nitrogen oxides (NOx): d = 2.05 g/1"}
{"chapter_id": "6.6.3.", "chapter_title": "Mass emissions of gaseous pollutants shall be calculated by means of the following formula:", "raw_text": "Mi = Vmix ⋅ Qi ⋅ kh ⋅ Ci ⋅ 10−6 (3)\n\nd\nwhere:\n\nMi = mass emission of the pollutant i in grams per kilometre,\n\nVmix = volume of the diluted exhaust gas expressed in litres per test and corrected to standard conditions (273.2 K and\n101.33 kPa),\n\nQi = density of the pollutant i in grams per litre at normal temperature and pressure (273.2 K and 101.33 kPa),\n\nkh = humidity correction factor used for the calculation of the mass emissions of oxides of nitrogen.  There is no humidity\ncorrection for HC and CO,\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nCi = concentration of the pollutant i in the diluted exhaust gas expressed in ppm and corrected by the amount of the\npollutant i contained in the dilution air,\n\nd = distance corresponding to the operating cycle in kilometres."}
{"chapter_id": "6.6.4.", "chapter_title": "Correction for Dilution Air Concentration", "raw_text": "The concentration of pollutant in the diluted exhaust gas shall be corrected by the amount of the pollutant in the dilution\nair as follows:\n\n\nCi = Ce − Cd ⋅ ⎛⎜1 − 1 ⎞⎟\n(4)\n⎝ DF ⎠\nwhere:\n\nCi = concentration of the pollutant i in the diluted exhaust gas, expressed in ppm and corrected by the amount of i\ncontained in the dilution air,\n\nCe = measured concentration of pollutant i in the diluted exhaust gas, expressed in ppm,\n\nCd = concentration of pollutant i in the air used for dilution, expressed in ppm,\n\nDF = dilution factor.\nThe dilution factor is calculated as follows:\n\n13.4\nDF = for petrol and diesel (5a)\n\nDF = for LPG (5b)\n\nDF = for NG (5c)\nCCO2 + (CHC + CCO ) ⋅ 10−4\n\nIn these equations:\n\nCCO2 = concentration of CO2 in the diluted exhaust gas contained in the sampling bag, expressed in per cent volume,\n\nCHC = concentration of HC in the diluted exhaust gas contained in the sampling bag, expressed in ppm carbon\nequivalent,\n\nCCO = concentration of CO in the diluted exhaust gas contained in the sampling bag, expressed in ppm."}

{"chapter_id": "1.1.", "chapter_title": "General Requirements", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "1.1.1.", "chapter_title": "The dynamometer shall be capable of simulating road load within one of the following", "raw_text": "classifications:\n\n(a) Dynamometer with fixed load curve, i.e. a dynamometer whose physical characteristics provide a\nfixed load curve shape,\n\n(b) Dynamometer with adjustable load curve, i.e. a dynamometer with at least two road load\nparameters that can be adjusted to shape the load curve."}
{"chapter_id": "1.1.2.", "chapter_title": "Dynamometers with electric inertia simulation shall be demonstrated to be equivalent to", "raw_text": "mechanical inertia systems.  The means by which equivalence is established are described\nin Appendix 6 to this Annex."}
{"chapter_id": "1.1.3.", "chapter_title": "In the event that the total resistance to progress on the road cannot be reproduced on the", "raw_text": "chassis dynamometer between speeds of 10 km/h and 120 km/h, it is recommended that a\nchassis dynamometer having the characteristics defined below should be used."}
{"chapter_id": "1.1.3.1.", "chapter_title": "The load absorbed by the brake and the chassis dynamometer internal frictional effects between the speeds of", "raw_text": "0 and 120 km/h is as follows:\n\nF = (a + b·V2) ± 0.1·F80 (without being negative)\nwhere:\n\nF = total load absorbed by the chassis dynamometer (N)\n\na = value equivalent to rolling resistance (N)\n\nb = value equivalent to coefficient of air resistance (N/(km/h)2)\n\nV = speed (km/h)\n\nF80 = load at 80 km/h (N)."}

{"chapter_id": "1.2.2.", "chapter_title": "The chassis dynamometer may have one or two rollers. {"chapter_id": "1.2.3.", "chapter_title": "It shall be possible to measure and read the indicated load to an accuracy of ± 5%.", "raw_text": ""}

Below this, dynamometer absorption shall be positive."}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.5.", "chapter_title": "The total inertia of the rotating parts (including the simulated inertia where applicable) shall", "raw_text": "be known and shall be within ± 20 kg of the inertia class for the test."}

{"chapter_id": "2.", "chapter_title": "DYNAMOMETER CALIBRATION PROCEDURE", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.", "chapter_title": "Introduction", "raw_text": "This section describes the method to be used to determine the load absorbed by a dynamometer brake.  The load\nabsorbed comprises the load absorbed by frictional effects and the load absorbed by the power-absorption\ndevice.\n\nThe dynamometer is brought into operation beyond the range of test speeds.  The device used for starting up the\ndynamometer is then disconnected: the rotational speed of the driven roller decreases.\n\nThe kinetic energy of the rollers is dissipated by the power-absorption unit and by the frictional effects.  This method\ndisregards variations in the roller's internal frictional effects caused by rollers with or without the vehicle.  The\nfrictional effects of the rear roller shall be disregarded when the roller is free."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.", "chapter_title": "Calibration of the Load Indicator at 80 km/h", "raw_text": "The following procedure shall be used for calibration of the load indicator to 80 km/h as a function of the load absorbed\n(see also Figure 4):"}

{"chapter_id": "3.1.", "chapter_title": "Procedure", "raw_text": "The load-absorption curve of the dynamometer from a reference setting at a speed of 80 km/h shall be\nverified as follows:"}

{"chapter_id": "1.", "chapter_title": "SYSTEM SPECIFICATION", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "1.1.", "chapter_title": "System Overview", "raw_text": "A full-flow exhaust dilution system shall be used.  This requires that the vehicle exhaust be continuously diluted with\nambient air under controlled conditions.  The total volume of the mixture of exhaust and dilution air shall be\nmeasured and a continuously proportional sample of the volume shall be collected for analysis.  The\nquantities of pollutants are determined from the sample concentrations, corrected for the pollutant content\nof the ambient air and the totalised flow over the test period.\n\nThe exhaust dilution system shall consist of a transfer tube, a mixing chamber and dilution tunnel, a dilution air\nconditioning, a suction device and a flow measurement device. Sampling probes shall be fitted in the dilution\ntunnel as specified in Appendices 3, 4 and 5.\n\nThe mixing chamber described above will be a vessel, such as those illustrated in Figures 6 and 7, in which vehicle\nexhaust gases and the dilution air are combined so as to produce a homogeneous mixture at the chamber\noutlet."}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.", "chapter_title": "General Requirements", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.1.", "chapter_title": "The vehicle exhaust gases shall be diluted with a sufficient amount of ambient air to", "raw_text": "prevent any water condensation in the sampling and measuring system at all conditions\nwhich may occur during a test."}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.2.", "chapter_title": "The mixture of air and exhaust gases shall be homogeneous at the point where the", "raw_text": "sampling probe is located (see Paragraph 1.3.3. below).  The sampling probe shall extract\na representative sample of the diluted exhaust gas."}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.3.", "chapter_title": "The system shall enable the total volume of the diluted exhaust gases to be measured.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.4.", "chapter_title": "The sampling system shall be gas-tight.  The design of the variable-dilution sampling", "raw_text": "system and the materials that go to make it up shall be such that they do not affect the\npollutant concentration in the diluted exhaust gases.  Should any component in the system\n(heat exchanger, cyclone separator, blower, etc.) change the concentration of any of the\npollutants in the diluted exhaust gases and the fault cannot be corrected, then sampling\nfor that pollutant shall be carried out upstream from that component."}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.5.", "chapter_title": "All parts of the dilution system that are in contact with raw and diluted exhaust gas, shall", "raw_text": "be designed to minimise deposition or alteration of the particulates or particles.  All parts\nshall be made of electrically conductive materials that do not react with exhaust gas\ncomponents, and shall be electrically grounded to prevent electrostatic effects."}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.6.", "chapter_title": "If the vehicle being tested is equipped with an exhaust pipe comprising several branches,", "raw_text": "the connecting tubes shall be connected as near as possible to the vehicle without\nadversely affecting its operation.\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.7.", "chapter_title": "The variable-dilution system shall be so designed as to enable the exhaust gases to be", "raw_text": "sampled without appreciably changing the back-pressure at the exhaust pipe outlet."}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.8.", "chapter_title": "The connecting tube between the vehicle and dilution system shall be designed so as to", "raw_text": "minimize heat loss."}
{"chapter_id": "1.3.", "chapter_title": "Specific Requirements", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "1.3.1.", "chapter_title": "Connection to Vehicle Exhaust", "raw_text": "The connecting tube between the vehicle exhaust outlets and the dilution system shall be as short as\npossible; and satisfy the following requirements:\n\n(a) Be less than 3.6 m long, or less than 6.1 m long if heat insulated.  Its internal diameter\nmay not exceed 105 mm;\n\n(b) Shall not cause the static pressure at the exhaust outlets on the vehicle being tested to;\ndiffer by more than ± 0.75 kPa at 50 km/h, or more than ± 1.25 kPa for the whole duration\nof the test from the static pressures recorded when nothing is connected to the vehicle\nexhaust outlets.  The pressure shall be measured in the exhaust outlet or in an extension\nhaving the same diameter, as near as possible to the end of the pipe. Sampling systems\ncapable of maintaining the static pressure to within ± 0.25 kPa may be used if a written\nrequest from a manufacturer to the Technical Service substantiates the need for the\ncloser tolerance;\n\n(c) Shall not change the nature of the exhaust gas;\n\n(d) Any elastomer connectors employed shall be as thermally stable as possible and have\nminimum exposure to the exhaust gases."}
{"chapter_id": "1.3.2.", "chapter_title": "Dilution Air Conditioning", "raw_text": "The dilution air used for the primary dilution of the exhaust in the CVS tunnel shall be passed through a medium capable\nof reducing particles in the most penetrating particle size of the filter material by ≥ 99.95%, or through a\nfilter of at least class H13 of EN 1822:1998.  This represents the specification of High Efficiency Particulate\nAir (HEPA) filters.  The dilution air may optionally be charcoal scrubbed before being passed to the HEPA\nfilter.  It is recommended that an additional coarse particle filter is situated before the HEPA filter and after\nthe charcoal scrubber, if used.\n\nAt the vehicle manufacturer's request, the dilution air may be sampled according to good engineering practice to\ndetermine the tunnel contribution to background particulate mass levels, which can then be subtracted from\nthe values measured in the diluted exhaust."}
{"chapter_id": "1.3.3.", "chapter_title": "Dilution Tunnel", "raw_text": "Provision shall be made for the vehicle exhaust gases and the dilution air to be mixed.  A mixing orifice may be used.\nIn order to minimise the effects on the conditions at the exhaust outlet and to limit the drop in pressure\ninside the dilution-air conditioning device, if any, the pressure at the mixing point shall not differ by more\nthan ± 0.25 kPa from atmospheric pressure.\n\nThe homogeneity of the mixture in any cross-section at the location of the sampling probe\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nshall not vary by more than ± 2% from the average of the values obtained for at least five points located at\nequal intervals on the diameter of the gas stream.\n\nFor particulate and particle emissions sampling, a dilution tunnel shall be used which:\n\n(a) Shall consist of a straight tube of electrically-conductive material, which shall be earthed;\n\n(b) Shall be small enough in diameter to cause turbulent flow (Reynolds number ≥ 4000)\nand of sufficient length to cause complete mixing of the exhaust and dilution air;\n\n(c) Shall be at least 200 mm in diameter;\n\n(d) May be insulated."}
{"chapter_id": "1.3.4.", "chapter_title": "Suction Device", "raw_text": "This device may have a range of fixed speeds to ensure sufficient flow to prevent any water condensation.  This result\nis generally obtained if the flow is either:\n\n(a) Twice as high as the maximum flow of exhaust gas produced by accelerations of the\ndriving cycle; or\n\n(b) Sufficient to ensure that the CO2 concentration in the dilute-exhaust sample bag is less\nthan 3% by volume for petrol and diesel, less than 2.2% by volume for LPG and less than\n1.5% by volume for NG."}
{"chapter_id": "1.3.5.", "chapter_title": "Volume Measurement in the Primary Dilution System", "raw_text": "The method of measuring total dilute exhaust volume incorporated in the constant volume sampler shall be such that\nmeasurement is accurate to ± 2% under all operating conditions. If the device cannot compensate for\nvariations in the temperature of the mixture of exhaust gases and dilution air at the measuring point, a heat\nexchanger shall be used to maintain the temperature to within ± 6 K of the specified operating temperature.\n\nIf necessary, some form of protection for the volume measuring device may be used e.g. a cyclone separator, bulk\nstream filter, etc.\n\nA temperature sensor shall be installed immediately before the volume measuring device. This temperature sensor\nshall have an accuracy and a precision of ± 1 K and a response time of 0.1 s at 62% of a given temperature\nvariation (value measured in silicone oil).\n\nThe measurement of the pressure difference from atmospheric pressure shall be taken upstream from and, if necessary,\ndownstream from the volume measuring device.\n\nThe pressure measurements shall have a precision and an accuracy of ± 0.4 kPa during the test."}

The variable mixture flow rate of dilution and exhaust gas is maintained at sonic velocity which\nis directly proportional to the square root of the gas temperature.  Flow is continually monitored, computed\nand integrated throughout the test.\n\nThe use of an additional critical-flow sampling venturi ensures the proportionality of the gas samples taken from the\ndilution tunnel.  As both pressure and temperature are equal at the two venturi inlets the volume of the gas\nflow diverted for sampling is proportional to the total volume of diluted exhaust-gas mixture produced, and\nthus the requirements of this Annex are met.  The collecting equipment consists of:"}

{"chapter_id": "2.", "chapter_title": "CVS CALIBRATION PROCEDURE", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.", "chapter_title": "General Requirements", "raw_text": "The CVS system shall be calibrated by using an accurate flow-meter and a restricting device.  The flow through the\nsystem shall be measured at various pressure readings and the control parameters of the system measured\nand related to the flows.  The flow-metering device shall be dynamic and suitable for the high flow-rate\nencountered in constant volume sampler testing.  The device shall be of certified accuracy traceable to an\napproved national or international standard."}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.1.", "chapter_title": "Various types of flow-meter may be used, e.g. calibrated venturi, laminar flow-meter,", "raw_text": "calibrated turbine-meter, provided that they are dynamic measurement systems and can\nmeet the requirements of Paragraph 1.3.5. of this Appendix."}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.2.", "chapter_title": "The following paragraphs give details of methods of calibrating PDP and CFV units, using", "raw_text": "a laminar flow-meter, which gives the required accuracy, together with a statistical check\non the calibration validity."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.", "chapter_title": "Calibration of the Positive Displacement Pump (PDP)", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.1.", "chapter_title": "The following calibration procedure outlines the equipment, the test configuration and the", "raw_text": "various parameters that are measured to establish the flow-rate of the CVS pump.  All the\nparameters related to the pump are simultaneously measured with the parameters related\nto the flow-meter which is connected in series with the pump.  The calculated flow-rate\n(given in m3/min at pump inlet, absolute pressure and temperature) can then be plotted\nversus a correlation function that is the value of a specific combination of pump\nparameters.  The linear equation that relates the pump flow and the correlation function is\nthen determined.  In the event that a CVS has a multiple speed drive, a calibration for each\nrange used shall be performed."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.2.", "chapter_title": "This calibration procedure is based on the measurement of the absolute values of the", "raw_text": "pump and flow-meter parameters that relate the flow rate at each point.  Three conditions\nshall be maintained to ensure the accuracy and integrity of the calibration curve:"}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.2.1.", "chapter_title": "The pump pressures shall be measured at tappings on the pump rather than at", "raw_text": "the external piping on the pump inlet and outlet.  Pressure taps that are mounted\nat the top centre and bottom centre of the pump drive headplate are exposed to\nthe actual pump cavity pressures, and therefore reflect the absolute pressure\ndifferentials;\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.2.2.", "chapter_title": "Temperature stability shall be maintained during the calibration.  The laminar flow-", "raw_text": "meter is sensitive to inlet temperature oscillations which cause the data points to\nbe scattered. Gradual changes of ± 1 K in temperature are acceptable as long as\nthey occur over a period of several minutes;"}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.2.3.", "chapter_title": "All connections between the flow-meter and the CVS pump shall be free of any", "raw_text": "leakage."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.3.", "chapter_title": "During an exhaust emission test, the measurement of these same pump parameters", "raw_text": "enables the user to calculate the flow rate from the calibration equation."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.4.", "chapter_title": "Figure 8 of this appendix shows one possible test set-up.  Variations are permissible,", "raw_text": "provided that the Technical Service approves them as being of comparable accuracy.  If\nthe set-up shown in Figure 8 is used, the following data shall be found within the limits of\nprecision given:\n\nBarometric pressure (corrected)(Pb) ± 0.03 kPa\nAmbient temperature (T) ± 0.2 K\nAir temperature at LFE (ETI) ± 0.15 K\nPressure depression upstream of LFE (EPI) ± 0.01 kPa\nPressure drop across the LFE matrix (EDP) ± 0.0015 kPa   Air temperature at\nCVS pump inlet (PTI) ± 0.2 K Air temperature at CVS pump outlet (PTO) ±\n0.2 K\nPressure depression at CVS pump inlet (PPI) ± 0.22 kPa Pressure head at CVS\npump outlet (PPO) ± 0.22 kPa\nPump revolutions during test period (n) ± 1 min-1\nElapsed time for period (minimum 250 s) (t) ± 0.1 s\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\nFigure 8\n\nPDP Calibration Configuration"}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.5.", "chapter_title": "After the system has been connected as shown in Figure 8 of this Appendix, set the variable restrictor in", "raw_text": "the wide-open position and run the CVS pump for 20 minutes before starting the calibration."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.6.", "chapter_title": "Reset the restrictor valve to a more restricted condition in an increment of pump inlet depression (about 1 kPa)", "raw_text": "that will yield a minimum of six data points for the total calibration. Allow the system to stabilize for three\nminutes and repeat the data acquisition."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.7.", "chapter_title": "The air flow rate (Qs) at each test point is calculated in standard m3/min from the flow-meter data using the", "raw_text": "manufacturer's prescribed method."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.8.", "chapter_title": "The air flow-rate is then converted to pump flow (V0) in m3/rev at absolute pump inlet temperature and pressure.", "raw_text": "V0 = Qs ⋅ Tp ⋅ 101.33 n 273.2 Pp\nwhere:\n\nV0 = pump flow rate at Tp and Pp (m3/rev),\n\nQs = air flow at 101.33 kPa and 273.2 K (m3/min),\n\nTp = pump inlet temperature (K),\n\nPp = absolute pump inlet pressure (kPa),\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\nN = pump speed (min-1)."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.9.", "chapter_title": "To compensate for the interaction of pump speed pressure variations at the pump and the pump slip rate, the", "raw_text": "correlation function (x0) between the pump speed (n), the pressure differential from pump inlet to pump\noutlet and the absolute pump outlet pressure is then calculated as follows:\n1ΔPp\nx0 = n Pe\nwhere:\n\nx0 = correlation function,\n\nΔPp = pressure differential from pump inlet to pump outlet (kPa),\n\nPe = absolute outlet pressure (PPO + Pb) (kPa).\n\nA linear least-square fit is performed to generate the calibration equations which have the formula:\n\nV0 = D0 − M (x0)\n\nn = A − B (ΔPp)\n\nD0, M, A and B are the slope-intercept constants describing the lines."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.10.", "chapter_title": "A CVS system that has multiple speeds shall be calibrated on each speed used.  The calibration curves", "raw_text": "generated for the ranges shall be approximately parallel and the intercept values (D0) shall increase as the\npump flow range decreases."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.11.", "chapter_title": "If the calibration has been performed carefully, the calculated values from the equation will be within 0.5% of the", "raw_text": "measured value of V0.  Values of M will vary from one pump to another.  Calibration is performed at pump\nstart-up and after major maintenance."}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.", "chapter_title": "Calibration of the Critical-flow Venturi (CFV)", "raw_text": ""}

{"chapter_id": "2.3.2.", "chapter_title": "The manufacturer's recommended procedure shall be followed for calibrating electronic portions of the CFV.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.3.", "chapter_title": "Measurements for flow calibration of the critical flow venturi are required and the following data shall be found", "raw_text": "within the limits of precision given:\n\nBarometric pressure (corrected) (Pb) ± 0.03 kPa, LFE air temperature, flow-meter\n(ETI) ± 0.15 K,\nPressure depression upstream of LFE (EPI) ± 0.01 kPa,\nPressure drop across (EDP) LFE matrix ± 0.0015 kPa,\nAir flow (Qs) ± 0.5%,\nCFV inlet depression (PPI) ± 0.02 kPa, Temperature at venturi inlet (Tv)  ± 0.2 K."}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.4.", "chapter_title": "The equipment shall be set up as shown in Figure 9 of this Appendix and checked for leaks. Any leaks between", "raw_text": "the flow-measuring device and the critical-flow venture will seriously affect the accuracy of the calibration.\n\n\n\nFigure 9\n\nCFV Calibration Configuration"}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.5.", "chapter_title": "The variable-flow restrictor shall be set to the open position, the blower shall be started and the system stabilized.", "raw_text": "Data from all instruments shall be recorded.\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.6.", "chapter_title": "The flow restrictor shall be varied and at least eight readings across the critical flow range of the venturi", "raw_text": "shall be made."}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.7.", "chapter_title": "The data recorded during the calibration shall be used in the following calculations.  The air flow-rate (Qs) at each", "raw_text": "test point is calculated from the flow-meter data using the manufacturer's prescribed method.\n\nCalculate values of the calibration coefficient for each test point:\n\nK v = Qs Tv\nPv\nwhere:\n\nQs = flow-rate in m3/min at 273.2 K and 101.33 kPa,\n\nTv = temperature at the venturi inlet (K),\n\nPv = absolute pressure at the venturi inlet (kPa).\n\nPlot Kv as a function of venturi inlet pressure.  For sonic flow, Kv will have a relatively constant value.  As pressure\ndecreases (vacuum increases) the venture becomes unchoked and Kv decreases.  The resultant Kv\nchanges are not permissible.\n\nFor a minimum of eight points in the critical region, calculate an average Kv and the standard deviation.\n\nIf the standard deviation exceeds 0.3% of the average Kv, take corrective action."}
{"chapter_id": "3.", "chapter_title": "SYSTEM VERIFICATION PROCEDURE", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.", "chapter_title": "General Requirements", "raw_text": "The total accuracy of the CVS sampling system and analytical system shall be determined by introducing a known mass\nof a pollutant gas into the system whilst it is being operated as if during a normal test and then analysing\nand calculating the pollutant mass according to the formula in Paragraph 6.6. of Annex 4a except that the\ndensity of propane shall be taken as 1.967 grams per litre at standard conditions.  The following two\ntechniques are known to give sufficient accuracy.\n\nThe maximum permissible deviation between the quantity of gas introduced and the quantity of gas\nmeasured is 5%."}
{"chapter_id": "3.2.", "chapter_title": "CFO Method", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.2.1.", "chapter_title": "Metering a constant flow of pure gas (CO or C3H8) using a critical flow orifice device.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.2.2.", "chapter_title": "A known quantity of pure gas (CO or C3H8) is fed into the CVS system through the", "raw_text": "calibrated critical orifice.  If the inlet pressure is high enough, the flow-rate (q), which is\nadjusted by means of the critical flow orifice, is independent of orifice outlet pressure\n(critical flow). If deviations exceeding 5% occur, the cause of the malfunction shall be\ndetermined and corrected.  The CVS system is operated as in an exhaust emission test\nfor about 5 to 10 minutes.  The gas collected in the sampling bag is analysed by the usual\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nequipment and the results compared to the concentration of the gas samples which was\nknown beforehand."}
{"chapter_id": "3.3.", "chapter_title": "Gravimetric Method", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.3.1.", "chapter_title": "Metering a limited quantity of pure gas (CO or C3H8) by means of a gravimetric technique.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.3.2.", "chapter_title": "The following gravimetric procedure may be used to verify the CVS system.", "raw_text": "The weight of a small cylinder filled with either carbon monoxide or propane is determined with a precision of ± 0.01 g.\nFor about 5 to 10 minutes, the CVS system is operated as in a normal exhaust emission test, while CO or\npropane is injected into the system.  The quantity of pure gas involved is determined by means of differential\nweighing.  The gas accumulated in the bag is then analysed by means of the equipment normally used for\nexhaust-gas analysis.  The results are then compared to the concentration figures computed previously.\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}

{"chapter_id": "1.2.12.", "chapter_title": "Hydrocarbon Sampling System − Diesel Engines", "raw_text": ""}

{"chapter_id": "1.2.12.5.", "chapter_title": "The sampling system response time (from the probe to the analyser inlet) shall be", "raw_text": "no more than four seconds."}

{"chapter_id": "1.3.2.", "chapter_title": "Hydrocarbons (HC) Analysis − Spark-ignition Engines:", "raw_text": "The analyser shall be of the flame ionisation (FID) type calibrated with propane gas expressed equivalent to carbon\natoms (C1)."}
{"chapter_id": "1.3.3.", "chapter_title": "Hydrocarbons (HC) Analysis − Compression-ignition Engines:", "raw_text": "The analyser shall be of the flame ionisation type with detector, valves, pipework, etc., heated to 463 K (190° C) ± 10\nK (HFID). {"chapter_id": "2.", "chapter_title": "CALIBRATION PROCEDURES", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.", "chapter_title": "Analyser Calibration Procedure", "raw_text": "COUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.1.", "chapter_title": "Each analyser shall be calibrated as often as necessary and in any case in the month", "raw_text": "before type approval testing and at least once every six months for verifying conformity of\nproduction."}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.2.", "chapter_title": "Each normally used operating range shall be calibrated by the following procedure:", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.2.1.", "chapter_title": "The analyser calibration curve is established by at least five calibration points", "raw_text": "spaced as uniformly as possible.  The nominal concentration of the calibration gas\nof the highest concentration shall be not less than 80% of the full scale."}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.2.2.", "chapter_title": "The calibration gas concentration required may be obtained by means of a gas", "raw_text": "divider, diluting with purified N2 or with purified synthetic air.  The accuracy of the\nmixing device shall be such that the concentrations of the diluted calibration gases\nmay be determined to within ± 2%."}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.2.3.", "chapter_title": "The calibration curve is calculated by the least squares method.  If the resulting", "raw_text": "polynomial degree is greater than 3, the number of calibration points shall be at\nleast equal to this polynomial degree plus 2."}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.2.4.", "chapter_title": "The calibration curve shall not differ by more than ± 2% from the nominal value of", "raw_text": "each calibration gas."}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.3.", "chapter_title": "Trace of the Calibration Curve", "raw_text": "From the trace of the calibration curve and the calibration points, it is possible to verify that the calibration has been\ncarried out correctly.  The different characteristic parameters of the analyser shall be indicated, particularly:\n\nThe scale;\nThe sensitivity;\nThe zero point;\nThe date of carrying out the calibration."}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.4.", "chapter_title": "If it can be shown to the satisfaction of the technical service that alternative technology", "raw_text": "(e.g. computer, electronically controlled range switch, etc.) can give equivalent accuracy,\nthen these alternatives may be used."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.", "chapter_title": "Analyser Verification Procedure", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.1.", "chapter_title": "Each normally used operating range shall be checked prior to each analysis in accordance", "raw_text": "with the following:"}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.2.", "chapter_title": "The calibration shall be checked by use of a zero gas and by use of a span gas that has a", "raw_text": "nominal value within 80-95% of the supposed value to be analysed."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.3.", "chapter_title": "If, for the two points considered, the value found does not differ by more than ± 5% of the", "raw_text": "full scale from the theoretical value, the adjustment parameters may be modified.  Should\nthis not be the case, a new calibration curve shall be established in accordance with\nParagraph 1. of this Appendix."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.4.", "chapter_title": "After testing, zero gas and the same span gas are used for re-checking.  The analysis is", "raw_text": "considered acceptable if the difference between the two measuring results is less than 2%.\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.", "chapter_title": "FID Hydrocarbon Response Check Procedure", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.1.", "chapter_title": "Detector Response Optimisation", "raw_text": "The FID shall be adjusted, as specified by the instrument manufacturer.  Propane in air should be used, to optimise the\nresponse, on the most common operating range."}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.2.", "chapter_title": "Calibration of the HC Analyser", "raw_text": "The analyser should be calibrated using propane in air and purified synthetic air (see Paragraph 3 of this Appendix).\n\nEstablish a calibration curve as described in Paragraph 2.1. of this Appendix."}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.3.", "chapter_title": "Response Factors of Different Hydrocarbons and Recommended Limits", "raw_text": "The response factor (Rf), for a particular hydrocarbon species is the ratio of the FID C1 reading to the gas cylinder\nconcentration, expressed as ppm C1.\n\nThe concentration of the test gas shall be at a level to give a response of approximately 80% of full-scale deflection, for\nthe operating range.  The concentration shall be known, to an accuracy of ± 2% in reference to a gravimetric\nstandard expressed in volume.  In addition, the gas cylinder shall be pre-conditioned for 24 hours at a\ntemperature between\n293 K and 303 K (20 and 30° C).\n\nResponse factors should be determined when introducing an analyser into service and thereafter at major service\nintervals.  The test gases to be used and the recommended response factors are:\n\nMethane and purified air: 1.00 < Rf < 1.15\n\nor 1.00 < Rf < 1.05 for NG fuelled vehicles\n\nPropylene and purified air: 0.90 < Rf < 1.00\n\nToluene and purified air: 0.90 < Rf < 1.00\n\nThese are relative to a response factor (Rf) of 1.00 for propane and purified air."}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.4.", "chapter_title": "Oxygen Interference Check and Recommended Limits", "raw_text": "The response factor shall be determined as described in Paragraph 2.3.3. above.  The test gas to be used and\nrecommended response factor range is:\n\nPropane and nitrogen: 0.95 < Rf < 1.05"}
{"chapter_id": "2.4.", "chapter_title": "NOx Converter Efficiency Test Procedure", "raw_text": "The efficiency of the converter used for the conversion of NO2 into NO is tested as follows:\n\nUsing the test set up as shown in Figure 11 and the procedure described below, the efficiency of converters can be\ntested by means of an ozonator.\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "2.4.1.", "chapter_title": "Calibrate the analyzer in the most common operating range following the manufacturer's", "raw_text": "specifications using zero and span gas (the NO content of which shall amount to about\n80% of the operating range and the NO2 concentration of the gas mixture shall be less\nthan 5% of the NO concentration).  The NOx analyser shall be in the NO mode so that the\nspan gas does not pass through the converter.  Record the indicated concentration."}
{"chapter_id": "2.4.2.", "chapter_title": "Via a T-fitting, oxygen or synthetic air is added continuously to the span gas flow until the", "raw_text": "concentration indicated is about 10% less than the indicated calibration concentration\ngiven in Paragraph 2.4.1. above.  Record the indicated concentration (C).  The ozonator\nis kept deactivated throughout this process."}
{"chapter_id": "2.4.3.", "chapter_title": "The ozonator is now activated to generate enough ozone to bring the NO concentration", "raw_text": "down to 20% (minimum 10%) of the calibration concentration given in Paragraph 2.4.1.\nabove.  Record the indicated concentration (d)."}
{"chapter_id": "2.4.4.", "chapter_title": "The NOx analyser is then switched to the NOx mode, which means that the gas mixture", "raw_text": "(consisting of NO, NO2, O2 and N2 ) now passes through the converter.  Record the\nindicated concentration (a)."}
{"chapter_id": "2.4.5.", "chapter_title": "The ozonator is now deactivated.  The mixture of gases described in Paragraph 2.4.2.", "raw_text": "above passes through the converter into the detector.  Record the indicated concentration\n(b).\n\n\nFigure 11\n\nNOx Converter Efficiency Test Configuration\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "2.4.6.", "chapter_title": "With the ozonator deactivated, the flow of oxygen or synthetic air is also shut off.  The NO2", "raw_text": "reading of the analyser shall then be no more than 5% above the figure given in Paragraph\n2.4.1.above."}
{"chapter_id": "2.4.7.", "chapter_title": "The efficiency of the NOx converter is calculated as follows:", "raw_text": "Efficiency (per cent) = ⎛⎜1+ a − b ⎞⎟ ⋅ 100\n⎝ c − d⎠"}
{"chapter_id": "2.4.8.", "chapter_title": "The efficiency of the converter shall not be less than 95%.", "raw_text": ""}

{"chapter_id": "3.", "chapter_title": "REFERENCE GASES", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.", "chapter_title": "Pure Gases", "raw_text": "The following pure gases shall be available, if necessary, for calibration and operation:\n\nPurified nitrogen: (purity: ≤ 1 ppm C, ≤ 1 ppm CO, ≤ 400 ppm CO2, ≤ 0.1 ppm NO);\n\nPurified synthetic air: (purity: ≤ 1 ppm C, ≤ 1 ppm CO, ≤ 400 ppm CO2, ≤ 0.1 ppm NO);   oxygen content\nbetween 18 and 21% volume;\n\nPurified oxygen: (purity > 99.5% vol. O2);\n\nPurified hydrogen (and mixture containing helium): (purity ≤ 1 ppm C, ≤ 400 ppm CO2);\n\nCarbon monoxide: (minimum purity 99.5%);\n\nPropane: (minimum purity 99.5%)."}
{"chapter_id": "3.2.", "chapter_title": "Calibration and Span Gases", "raw_text": "Mixtures of gases having the following chemical compositions shall be available:\n\n(a) C3H8 and purified synthetic air (see Paragraph 3.1. above);\n\n(b) CO and purified nitrogen;\n\n(c) CO2 and purified nitrogen.\n\nNO and purified nitrogen (the amount of NO2 contained in this calibration gas shall not exceed 5% of the NO content).\n\nThe true concentration of a calibration gas shall be within ± 2% of the stated figure."}
{"chapter_id": "1.", "chapter_title": "SPECIFICATION", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "1.1.", "chapter_title": "System Overview", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "1.1.1.", "chapter_title": "The particulate sampling unit shall consist of a sampling probe located in the dilution", "raw_text": "tunnel, a particle transfer tube, a filter holder, a partial-flow pump, and flow rate regulators\nand measuring units."}
{"chapter_id": "1.1.2.", "chapter_title": "It is recommended that a particle size pre-classifier (e.g. cyclone or impactor) be employed", "raw_text": "upstream of the filter holder.  However, a sampling probe, acting as an appropriate size-\nclassification device such as that shown in Figure 13, is acceptable."}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.", "chapter_title": "General Requirements", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.1.", "chapter_title": "The sampling probe for the test gas flow for particulates shall be so arranged within the", "raw_text": "dilution tract that a representative sample gas flow can be taken from the homogeneous\nair/exhaust mixture."}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.2.", "chapter_title": "The particulate sample flow rate shall be proportional to the total flow of diluted exhaust", "raw_text": "gas in the dilution tunnel to within a tolerance of ± 5% of the particulate sample flow rate."}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.3.", "chapter_title": "The sampled dilute exhaust gas shall be maintained at a temperature below 325 K (52° C)", "raw_text": "within 20 cm upstream or downstream of the particulate filter face, except in the case of a\nregeneration test where the temperature must be below 192° C."}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.4.", "chapter_title": "The particulate sample shall be collected on a single filter mounted within a holder in the", "raw_text": "sampled dilute exhaust gas flow."}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.5.", "chapter_title": "All parts of the dilution system and the sampling system from the exhaust pipe up to the", "raw_text": "filter holder, which are in contact with raw and diluted exhaust gas, shall be designed to\nminimise deposition or alteration of the particulates.  All parts shall be made of electrically\nconductive materials that do not react with exhaust gas components, and shall be\nelectrically grounded to prevent electrostatic effects."}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.6.", "chapter_title": "If it is not possible to compensate for variations in the flow rate, provision shall be made", "raw_text": "for a heat exchanger and a temperature control device as specified in Appendix 2 so as to\nensure that the flow rate in the system is constant and the sampling rate accordingly\nproportional."}
{"chapter_id": "1.3.", "chapter_title": "Specific Requirements", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "1.3.1.", "chapter_title": "PM Sampling Probe", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "1.3.1.1.", "chapter_title": "The sample probe shall deliver the particle-size classification performance", "raw_text": "described in Paragraph 1.3.1.4.  It is recommended that this performance be\nachieved by the use of a sharp-edged, open-ended probe facing directly into the\ndirection of flow plus a pre-classifier (cyclone impactor, etc.).  An appropriate\nsampling probe, such as that indicated in Figure 13, may alternatively be used\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nprovided it achieves the pre-classification performance described in Paragraph\n1.3.1.4."}
{"chapter_id": "1.3.1.2.", "chapter_title": "The sample probe shall be installed near the tunnel centreline, between 10 and 20", "raw_text": "tunnel diameters downstream of the exhaust gas inlet to the tunnel and have an\ninternal diameter of at least 12 mm.\n\nIf more than one simultaneous sample is drawn from a single sample probe, the flow drawn from that probe shall be\nsplit into identical sub-flows to avoid sampling artefacts.\n\nIf multiple probes are used, each probe shall be sharp-edged, open-ended and facing directly into the direction of flow.\nProbes shall be equally spaced around the central longitudinal axis of the dilution tunnel, with the spacing\nbetween probes at least 5 cm."}
{"chapter_id": "1.3.1.3.", "chapter_title": "The distance from the sampling tip to the filter mount shall be at least five probe", "raw_text": "diameters, but shall not exceed 1.020 mm."}
{"chapter_id": "1.3.1.4.", "chapter_title": "The pre-classifier (e.g. cyclone, impactor, etc.) shall be located upstream of the", "raw_text": "filter holder assembly.  The pre-classifier 50% cut point particle diameter shall be\nbetween 2.5 μm and 10 μm at the volumetric flow rate selected for sampling\nparticulate mass emissions.  The pre-classifier shall allow at least 99% of the mass\nconcentration of 1 μm particles entering the pre-classifier to pass through the exit\nof the pre-classifier at the volumetric flow rate selected for sampling particulate\nmass emissions.  However, a sampling probe, acting as an appropriate size-\nclassification device, such as that shown in Figure 13, is acceptable as an\nalternative to a separate pre-classifier."}
{"chapter_id": "1.3.2.", "chapter_title": "Sample Pump and Flow Meter", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "1.3.2.1.", "chapter_title": "The sample gas flow measurement unit shall consist of pumps, gas flow regulators", "raw_text": "and flow measuring units."}
{"chapter_id": "1.3.2.2.", "chapter_title": "The temperature of the gas flow in the flow meter may not fluctuate by more than", "raw_text": "± 3 K, except during regeneration tests on vehicles equipped with periodically\nregenerating aftertreatment devices.  In addition, the sample mass flow rate must\nremain proportional to the total flow of diluted exhaust gas to within a tolerance of\n± 5% of the particulate sample mass flow rate.  Should the volume of flow change\nunacceptably as a result of excessive filter loading, the test shall be stopped.\nWhen it is repeated, the rate of flow shall be decreased."}
{"chapter_id": "1.3.3.", "chapter_title": "Filter and Filter Holder", "raw_text": ""}
