{"chapter_id": "1.3.4.", "chapter_title": "Filter Weighing Chamber and Balance", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "1.3.4.1.", "chapter_title": "The microgram balance used to determine the weight of a filter shall have a", "raw_text": "precision (standard deviation) of 2 μg and resolution of 1 μg or better.\n\nIt is recommended that the microbalance be checked at the start of each weighing session by weighing one reference\nweight of 50 mg.  This weight shall be weighed three times and the average result recorded.  If the average\nresult of the weighings is ± 5 μg of the result from the previous weighing session then the weighing session\nand balance are considered valid.\n\nThe weighing chamber (or room) shall meet the following conditions during all filter conditioning and weighing\noperations:\n\nTemperature maintained at 295 ± 3 K (22 ± 3° C);\n\nRelative humidity maintained at 45 ± 8%;\n\nDewpoint maintained at 9.5° C ± 3° C.\n\nIt is recommended that temperature and humidity conditions are recorded along with sample and reference\nfilter weights."}
{"chapter_id": "1.3.4.2.", "chapter_title": "Buoyancy Correction", "raw_text": "All filter weights shall be corrected for filter buoyancy in air.\n\nThe buoyancy correction depends on the density of the sample filter medium, the density of air, and the density of the\ncalibration weight used to calibrate the balance.  The density of the air is dependent on the pressure,\ntemperature and humidity.\n\nIt is recommended that the temperature and dewpoint of the weighing environment are controlled to 22° C ± 1° C and\ndewpoint of 9.5° C ± 1° C respectively.  However, the minimum requirements stated in Paragraph 1.3.4.1.\nwill also result in an acceptable correction for buoyancy effects.  The correction for buoyancy shall be\napplied as follows\nmcorr = muncorr • (1 − ((ρair ) / (ρweight ))) / 1( − ((ρair ) / (ρmedia )))\nwhere:\n\nmcorr = PM mass corrected for buoyancy\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\nmuncorr = PM mass uncorrected for buoyancy\n\nρair = density of air in balance environment\n\nρweight = density of calibration weight used to span balance\n\nρmedia = density of PM sample medium (filter) according to the table below:\n\nFilter Medium ρmedia\nTeflon coated glass fibre (e.g. TX40) 2300 kg/m3\n\nρair can be calculated as follows:\n\nPabs ⋅ Mmix\nρair =\nR ⋅ Tamb\nwhere:\n\nPabs = absolute pressure in balance environment\n\nMmix = molar mass of air in balance environment (28.836 gmol-1)\n\nR = molar gas constant (8.314 Jmol-1K-1)\n\nTamb = absolute ambient temperature of balance environment.\n\nThe chamber (or room) environment shall be free of any ambient contaminants (such as\ndust) that would settle on the particulate filters during their stabilisation.\nLimited deviations from weighing room temperature and humidity specifications will be allowed provided their total\nduration does not exceed 30 minutes in any one filter conditioning period. The weighing room should meet\nthe required specifications prior to personal entrance into the weighing room.  During the weighing operation\nno deviations from the specified conditions are permitted."}
{"chapter_id": "1.3.4.3.", "chapter_title": "The effects of static electricity shall be nullified.  This may be achieved by grounding the balance through", "raw_text": "placement upon an antistatic mat and neutralisation of the particulate filters prior to weighing using a\nPolonium neutraliser or a device of similar effect.  Alternatively nullification of static effects may be achieved\nthrough equalisation of the static charge."}

{"chapter_id": "2.3.", "chapter_title": "Reference Filter Weighing", "raw_text": "To determine the specific reference filter weights, at least two unused reference filters shall be weighed within 8 hours\nof, but preferably at the same time as, the sample filter weighings.  Reference filters shall be of the same\nsize and material as the sample filter.\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nIf the specific weight of any reference filter changes by more than ± 5μg between sample filter weighings, then the\nsample filter and reference filters shall be reconditioned in the weighing room and then reweighed.\n\nThe comparison of reference filter weighings shall be made between the specific weights and the rolling average of that\nreference filter's specific weights.\n\nThe rolling average shall be calculated from the specific weights collected in the period since the reference filters were\nplaced in the weighing room.  The averaging period shall be at least 1 day but not exceed 30 days.\n\nMultiple reconditionings and reweighings of the sample and reference filters are permitted until a period of 80 h has\nelapsed following the measurement of gases from the emissions test.\n\nIf, prior to or at the 80 h point, more than half the number of reference filters meet the ± 5 μg criterion, then the sample\nfilter weighing can be considered valid.\n\nIf, at the 80 h point, two reference filters are employed and one filter fails the ± 5 μg criterion, the sample filter weighing\ncan be considered valid under the condition that the sum of the absolute differences between specific and\nrolling averages from the two reference filters must be less than or equal to 10 μg.\n\nIn case less than half of the reference filters meet the ± 5 μg criterion the sample filter shall be discarded, and the\nemissions test repeated.  All reference filters must be discarded and replaced within 48 hours.\n\nIn all other cases, reference filters must be replaced at least every 30 days and in such a manner that no sample filter\nis weighed without comparison to a reference filter that has been present in the weighing room for at least\n1day.\nIf the weighing room stability criteria outlined in Paragraph 1.3.4. are not met, but the reference filter weighings meet\nthe above criteria, the vehicle manufacturer has the option of accepting the sample filter weights or voiding\nthe tests, fixing the weighing room control system and re-running the test.\n\n\n\nFigure 13\n\nParticulate Sampling Probe Configuration\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}

{"chapter_id": "1.1.1.", "chapter_title": "The particle sampling system shall consist of a dilution tunnel, a sampling probe and a", "raw_text": "volatile particle remover (VPR) upstream of a particle number counter (PNC) and suitable\ntransfer tubing."}
{"chapter_id": "1.1.2.", "chapter_title": "It is recommended that a particle size pre-classifier (e.g. cyclone, impactor etc) be located", "raw_text": "prior to the inlet of the VPR.  However, a sample probe acting as an appropriate size-\nclassification device, such as that shown in Figure 13, is an acceptable alternative to the\nuse of a particle size pre-classifier."}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.", "chapter_title": "General Requirements", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.1.", "chapter_title": "The particle sampling point shall be located within a dilution tunnel.", "raw_text": "The sampling probe tip (PSP) and particle transfer tube (PTT) together comprise the particle transfer system (PTS).\nThe PTS conducts the sample from the dilution tunnel to the entrance of the VPR.  The PTS shall meet the\nfollowing conditions:\n\nIt shall be installed near the tunnel centre line, 10 to 20 tunnel diameters downstream of the gas inlet, facing upstream\ninto the tunnel gas flow with its axis at the tip parallel to that of the dilution tunnel.\n\nIt shall have an internal diameter of ≥ 8 mm.\n\nSample gas drawn through the PTS shall meet the following conditions:\n\nIt shall have a flow Reynolds number (Re) of < 1700;\n\nIt shall have a residence time in the PTS of ≤ 3 seconds.\n\nAny other sampling configuration for the PTS for which equivalent particle penetration at 30 nm can be demonstrated\nwill be considered acceptable.\n\nThe outlet tube (OT) conducting the diluted sample from the VPR to the inlet of the PNC shall have the following\nproperties:\n\nIt shall have an internal diameter of ≥ 4mm;\n\nSample Gas flow through the OT shall have a residence time of ≤ 0.8 seconds.\n\nAny other sampling configuration for the OT for which equivalent particle penetration at 30 nm can be demonstrated\nwill be considered acceptable.\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.2.", "chapter_title": "The VPR shall include devices for sample dilution and for volatile particle removal.  The sampling probe for the", "raw_text": "test gas flow shall be so arranged within the dilution tract that a representative sample gas flow is taken\nfrom a homogeneous air/exhaust mixture."}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.3.", "chapter_title": "All parts of the dilution system and the sampling system from the exhaust pipe up to the PNC, which are in contact", "raw_text": "with raw and diluted exhaust gas, shall be designed to minimise deposition of the particles.  All parts shall\nbe made of electrically conductive materials that do not react with exhaust gas components, and shall be\nelectrically grounded to prevent electrostatic effects."}
{"chapter_id": "1.2.4.", "chapter_title": "The particle sampling system shall incorporate good aerosol sampling practice that includes the avoidance of", "raw_text": "sharp bends and abrupt changes in cross-section, the use of smooth internal surfaces and the minimisation\nof the length of the sampling line.  Gradual changes in the cross-section are permissible."}

{"chapter_id": "1.4.", "chapter_title": "Recommended System Description", "raw_text": "The following section contains the recommended practice for measurement of particle number.  However, any system\nmeeting the performance specifications in Paragraphs 1.2.\nand 1.3. is acceptable.\n\nFigure 14 is a schematic drawing of the recommended particle sampling system.\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\nFigure 14\n\nSchematic of Recommended Particle Sampling System"}
{"chapter_id": "1.4.1.", "chapter_title": "Sampling System Description", "raw_text": "The particle sampling system shall consist of a sampling probe tip in the dilution tunnel (PSP), a particle transfer tube\n(PTT), a particle pre-classifier (PCF) and a volatile particle remover (VPR) upstream of the particle number\nconcentration measurement (PNC) unit. The VPR shall include devices for sample dilution (particle number\ndiluters: PND1 and PND2) and particle evaporation (Evaporation tube, ET).  The sampling probe for the test\ngas flow shall be so arranged within the dilution tract that a representative sample gas flow is taken from a\nhomogeneous air/exhaust mixture.  The sum of the residence time of the system plus the T90 response\ntime of the PNC shall be no greater than 20 s."}
{"chapter_id": "1.4.2.", "chapter_title": "Particle Transfer System", "raw_text": "The sampling probe tip (PSP) and particle transfer tube (PTT) together comprise the particle transfer system (PTS).\nThe PTS conducts the sample from the dilution tunnel to the entrance to the first particle number diluter.\nThe PTS shall meet the following conditions:\n\nIt shall be installed near the tunnel centre line, 10 to 20 tunnel diameters downstream of the gas inlet, facing upstream\ninto the tunnel gas flow with its axis at the tip parallel to that of the dilution tunnel.\n\nIt shall have an internal diameter of ≥ 8 mm.\n\nSample gas drawn through the PTS shall meet the following conditions:\n\nIt shall have a flow Reynolds number (Re) of < 1700;\n\nIt shall have a residence time in the PTS of ≤ 3 seconds.\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\nAny other sampling configuration for the PTS for which equivalent particle penetration for particles of 30 nm electrical\nmobility diameter can be demonstrated will be considered acceptable.\n\nThe outlet tube (OT) conducting the diluted sample from the VPR to the inlet of the PNC shall have the following\nproperties:\n\nIt shall have an internal diameter of ≥ 4 mm;\n\nSample Gas flow through the POT shall have a residence time of ≤ 0.8 seconds.\n\nAny other sampling configuration for the OT for which equivalent particle penetration for particles of 30 nm electrical\nmobility diameter can be demonstrated will be considered acceptable."}
{"chapter_id": "1.4.3.", "chapter_title": "Particle Pre-classifier", "raw_text": "The recommended particle pre-classifier shall be located upstream of the VPR.  The pre-classifier 50% cut point particle\ndiameter shall be between 2.5 μm and 10 μm at the volumetric flow rate selected for sampling particle\nnumber emissions.  The pre-classifier shall allow at least 99% of the mass concentration of 1 μm particles\nentering the pre-classifier to pass through the exit of the pre-classifier at the volumetric flow rate selected\nfor sampling particle number emissions."}
{"chapter_id": "1.4.4.", "chapter_title": "Volatile Particle Remover (VPR)", "raw_text": "The VPR shall comprise one particle number diluter (PND1), an evaporation tube and a second diluter (PND2) in series.\nThis dilution function is to reduce the number concentration of the sample entering the particle concentration\nmeasurement unit to less than the upper threshold of the single particle count mode of the PNC and to\nsuppress nucleation within the sample.  The VPR shall provide an indication of whether or not PND1 and\nthe evaporation tube are at their correct operating temperatures.\n\nThe VPR shall achieve > 99.0% vaporisation of 30 nm tetracontane (CH3(CH2)38CH3) particles, with an inlet\nconcentration of ≥ 10,000 cm-3, by means of heating and reduction of partial pressures of the tetracontane.\nIt shall also achieve a particle concentration reduction factor (fr) for particles of 30 nm and 50 nm electrical\nmobility diameters, that is no more than 30% and 20% respectively higher, and no more than 5% lower\nthan that for particles of 100 nm electrical mobility diameter for the VPR as a whole."}
{"chapter_id": "1.4.4.1.", "chapter_title": "First Particle Number Dilution Device (PND1)", "raw_text": "The first particle number dilution device shall be specifically designed to dilute particle number concentration and\noperate at a (wall) temperature of 150° C − 400° C.  The wall temperature setpoint should be held at a\nconstant nominal operating temperature, within this range, to a tolerance of ± 10° C and not exceed the\nwall temperature of the ET (Paragraph 1.4.4.2.). The diluter should be supplied with HEPA filtered dilution\nair and be capable of a dilution factor of 10 to 200 times."}
{"chapter_id": "1.4.4.2.", "chapter_title": "Evaporation Tube", "raw_text": "The entire length of the ET shall be controlled to a wall temperature greater than or equal to that of the first particle\nnumber dilution device and the wall temperature held at a fixed nominal operating temperature between\n300° C and 400° C, to a tolerance of ± 10° C."}
{"chapter_id": "1.4.4.3.", "chapter_title": "Second Particle Number Dilution Device (PND2)", "raw_text": "COUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\nPND2 shall be specifically designed to dilute particle number concentration.  The diluter shall be supplied with HEPA\nfiltered dilution air and be capable of maintaining a single dilution factor within a range of 10 to 30 times.\nThe dilution factor of PND2 shall be selected in the range between 10 and 15 such that particle number\nconcentration downstream of the second diluter is less than the upper threshold of the single particle count\nmode of the PNC and the gas temperature prior to entry to the PNC is < 35° C."}
{"chapter_id": "1.4.5.", "chapter_title": "Particle Number Counter (PNC)", "raw_text": "The PNC shall meet the requirements of Paragraph 1.3.4."}
{"chapter_id": "2.", "chapter_title": "CALIBRATION/VALIDATION OF THE PARTICLE SAMPLING SYSTEM (1)", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.", "chapter_title": "Calibration of the Particle Number Counter", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.1.", "chapter_title": "The Technical Service shall ensure the existence of a calibration certificate for the PNC", "raw_text": "demonstrating compliance with a traceable standard within a 12 month period prior to the\nemissions test."}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.2.", "chapter_title": "The PNC shall also be recalibrated and a new calibration certificate issued following any", "raw_text": "major maintenance."}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.3.", "chapter_title": "Calibration shall be traceable to a standard calibration method:", "raw_text": "(a) By comparison of the response of the PNC under calibration with that of a calibrated\naerosol electrometer when simultaneously sampling electrostatically classified\ncalibration particles, or\n\n(b) By comparison of the response of the PNC under calibration with that of a second PNC\nwhich has been directly calibrated by the above method.\n\nIn the electrometer case, calibration shall be undertaken using at least six standard concentrations spaced as uniformly\nas possible across the PNC's measurement range. These points will include a nominal zero concentration\npoint produced by attaching HEPA filters of at least Class H13 of EN 1822:2008, or equivalent performance,\nto the inlet of each instrument.  With no calibration factor applied to the PNC under calibration, measured\nconcentrations shall be within ± 10% of the standard concentration for each concentration used, with the\nexception of the zero point, otherwise the PNC under calibration shall be rejected.  The gradient from a\nlinear regression of the two data sets shall be calculated and recorded.  A calibration factor equal to the\nreciprocal of the gradient shall be applied to the PNC under calibration. Linearity of response is calculated\nas the square of the Pearson product moment correlation coefficient (R2) of the two data sets and shall be\nequal to or greater than 0.97.  In calculating both the gradient and R2 the linear regression shall be forced\nthrough the origin (zero concentration on both instruments).\n\nIn the reference PNC case, calibration shall be undertaken using at least six standard concentrations across the PNC's\nmeasurement range.  At least 3 points shall be at concentrations below 1,000 cm-3, the remaining\nconcentrations shall be linearly spaced between 1,000 cm-3 and the maximum of the PNC's range in single\nparticle count mode. These points will include a nominal zero concentration point produced by attaching\nHEPA filters of at least Class H13 of EN 1822:2008, or equivalent performance, to the inlet of each\ninstrument.  With no calibration factor applied to the PNC under calibration, measured concentrations shall\nbe within ± 10% of the standard concentration for each concentration, with the exception of the zero point,\notherwise the PNC under calibration shall be rejected. The gradient from a linear regression of the two data\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nsets shall be calculated and recorded. A calibration factor equal to the reciprocal of the gradient shall be\napplied to the PNC under calibration.  Linearity of response is calculated as the square of the Pearson\nproduct moment correlation coefficient (R2) of the two data sets and shall be equal to or greater than 0.97.\nIn calculating both the gradient and R2 the linear regression shall be forced through the origin (zero\nconcentration on both instruments).\n\n(1)\nExample calibration/validation methods are available at http://www.unece.org/trans/main/wp29/wp29wgs/wp29grpe/pmpFCP.html"}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.4.", "chapter_title": "Calibration shall also include a check, against the requirements in Paragraph 1.3.4.8., on the PNC's detection", "raw_text": "efficiency with particles of 23 nm electrical mobility diameter.  A check of the counting efficiency with 41 nm\nparticles is not required."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.", "chapter_title": "Calibration/Validation of the Volatile Particle Remover", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.1.", "chapter_title": "Calibration of the VPR's particle concentration reduction factors across its full range of dilution settings, at the", "raw_text": "instrument's fixed nominal operating temperatures, shall be required when the unit is new and following\nany major maintenance.  The periodic validation requirement for the VPR's particle concentration reduction\nfactor is limited to a check at a single setting, typical of that used for measurement on diesel particulate\nfilter equipped vehicles.  The Technical Service shall ensure the existence of a calibration or validation\ncertificate for the volatile particle remover within a 6 month period prior to the emissions test. If the volatile\nparticle remover incorporates temperature monitoring alarms a 12 month validation interval shall be\npermissible.\n\nThe VPR shall be characterised for particle concentration reduction factor with solid particles of 30 nm, 50 nm and 100\nnm electrical mobility diameter.  Particle concentration reduction factors (fr(d)) for particles of 30 nm and 50\nnm electrical mobility diameters shall be no more than 30% and 20% higher respectively, and no more than\n5% lower than that for particles of 100 nm electrical mobility diameter.  For the purposes of validation, the\nmean particle concentration reduction factor shall be within ± 10% of the mean particle\n\nconcentration reduction factor (f r ) determined during the primary calibration of the VPR."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.2.", "chapter_title": "The test aerosol for these measurements shall be solid particles of 30, 50 and 100 nm electrical mobility diameter", "raw_text": "and a minimum concentration of 5,000 particles cm-3 at the VPR inlet.  Particle concentrations shall be\nmeasured upstream and downstream of the components.\n\nThe particle concentration reduction factor at each particle size (fr(di)) shall be calculated as follows;\n\nfr (di ) = Nin (di )\nNout (di )\nwhere:\n\nNin (di) = upstream particle number concentration for particles of diameter di;\n\nNout (di) = downstream particle number concentration for particles of diameter di; and\n\ndi = particle electrical mobility diameter (30, 50 or 100 nm).\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nNin (di) and Nout (di) shall be corrected to the same conditions.\n\n\nThe mean particle concentration reduction (f r ) at a given dilution setting shall be calculated as follows;\n\nfr = fr (30 nm) +fr (50 nm) + fr (100 nm)\n3\n\nIt is recommended that the VPR is calibrated and validated as a complete unit."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.3.", "chapter_title": "The Technical Service shall ensure the existence of a validation certificate for the VPR demonstrating effective", "raw_text": "volatile particle removal efficiency within a 6 month period prior to the emissions test.  If the volatile particle\nremover incorporates temperature monitoring alarms a 12 month validation interval shall be permissible.\nThe VPR shall demonstrate greater than 99.0% removal of tetracontane (CH3(CH2)38CH3) particles of at\nleast 30 nm electrical mobility diameter with an inlet concentration of ≥ 10,000 cm-3 when operated at its\nminimum dilution setting and manufacturers recommended operating temperature."}

{"chapter_id": "1.", "chapter_title": "OBJECT", "raw_text": "The method described in this Appendix makes it possible to check that the simulated total inertia of the dynamometer\nis carried out satisfactorily in the running phase of the operating cycle.  The manufacturer of the dynamometer\nshall specify a method for verifying the specifications according to Paragraph 3. of this Appendix."}
{"chapter_id": "2.", "chapter_title": "PRINCIPLE", "raw_text": "COUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.", "chapter_title": "Drawing-up Working Equations", "raw_text": "Since the dynamometer is subjected to variations in the rotating speed of the roller(s), the force at the surface of the\nroller(s) can be expressed by the formula:\n\nF = I · γ = IM · γ + F1\nwhere:\n\nF = force at the surface of the roller(s),\n\nI = total inertia of the dynamometer (equivalent inertia of the vehicle:  see the table in Paragraph 5.1.),\n\nIM = inertia of the mechanical masses of the dynamometer,\n\nγ = tangential acceleration at roller surface,\n\nF1 = inertia force.\n\nNote:  An explanation of this formula with reference to dynamometers with mechanically simulated inertia is appended.\n\nThus, total inertia is expressed as follows:\n\nI = Im+ F1 / γ\nwhere:\n\nIm  can be calculated or measured by traditional methods,\n\nF1  can be measured on the dynamometer,\n\ng can be calculated from the peripheral speed of the rollers.\n\nThe total inertia (I) will be determined during an acceleration or deceleration test with values higher than or equal to\nthose obtained on an operating cycle."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.", "chapter_title": "Specification for the Calculation of Total Inertia", "raw_text": "The test and calculation methods shall make it possible to determine the total inertia I with a relative error (ΔI/I) of less\nthan ± 2%."}
{"chapter_id": "3.", "chapter_title": "SPECIFICATION", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.", "chapter_title": "The mass of the simulated total inertia I shall remain the same as the theoretical value of the equivalent", "raw_text": "inertia (see Appendix 1) within the following limits:"}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.1.", "chapter_title": "± 5% of the theoretical value for each instantaneous value;", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.2.", "chapter_title": "± 2% of the theoretical value for the average value calculated for each sequence of the cycle.", "raw_text": "COUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nThe limit given in Paragraph 3.1.1. above is brought to ± 50% for one second when starting and, for vehicles with\nmanual transmission, for two seconds during gear changes."}

{"chapter_id": "1.", "chapter_title": "INTRODUCTION", "raw_text": "This Annex describes the procedure for the Type II test defined in Paragraph 5.3.2. of this Regulation."}
{"chapter_id": "2.", "chapter_title": "CONDITIONS OF MEASUREMENT", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.", "chapter_title": "The fuel shall be the reference fuel, specifications for which are given in Annexes 10 and 10a to", "raw_text": "this Regulation."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.", "chapter_title": "During the test the environmental temperature shall be between 293 and 303 K (20 and", "raw_text": "30° C).  The engine shall be warmed up until all temperatures of cooling and lubrication means and the\npressure of lubrication means have reached equilibrium."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.1.", "chapter_title": "Vehicles that are fuelled either with petrol or with LPG or NG shall be tested with the", "raw_text": "reference fuel(s) used for the Type I test."}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.", "chapter_title": "In the case of vehicles with manually-operated or semi-automatic-shift gearboxes, the test shall be", "raw_text": "carried out with the gear lever in the \"neutral\" position and with the clutch engaged."}
{"chapter_id": "2.4.", "chapter_title": "In the case of vehicles with automatic-shift gear-boxes, the test shall be carried out with the gear", "raw_text": "selector in either the \"neutral\" or the \"parking\" position."}
{"chapter_id": "2.5.", "chapter_title": "Components for Adjusting the Idling Speed", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.5.1.", "chapter_title": "Definition", "raw_text": "For the purposes of this Regulation, \"components for adjusting the idling speed\" means controls for\nchanging the idling conditions of the engine which may be easily operated by a mechanic using only the\ntools described in Paragraph 2.5.1.1.below.  In particular, devices for calibrating fuel and air flows are not\nconsidered as adjustment components if their setting requires the removal of the set-stops, an operation\nwhich cannot normally be performed except by a professional mechanic."}
{"chapter_id": "2.5.1.1", "chapter_title": "Tools which may be used to control components for adjusting the idling speed:", "raw_text": "screwdrivers (ordinary or cross-headed), spanners (ring, open-end or adjustable),\npliers, Allen keys."}
{"chapter_id": "2.5.2.", "chapter_title": "Determination of Measurement Points", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.5.2.1", "chapter_title": "A measurement at the setting in accordance with the conditions fixed by the", "raw_text": "manufacturer is performed first;"}
{"chapter_id": "2.5.2.2", "chapter_title": "For each adjustment component with a continuous variation, a sufficient number", "raw_text": "of characteristic positions shall be determined.\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "2.5.2.3", "chapter_title": "The measurement of the carbon-monoxide content of exhaust gases shall be", "raw_text": "carried out for all the possible positions of the adjustment components, but for\ncomponents with a continuous variation only the positions defined in Paragraph\n2.5.2.2.above shall be adopted."}
{"chapter_id": "2.5.2.4", "chapter_title": "The Type II test shall be considered satisfactory if one or both of the two following", "raw_text": "conditions is met:"}
{"chapter_id": "2.5.2.4.1.", "chapter_title": "none of the values measured in accordance with Paragraph 2.5.2.3.", "raw_text": "above exceeds the limit values;"}
{"chapter_id": "2.5.2.4.2.", "chapter_title": "the maximum content obtained by continuously varying one of the", "raw_text": "adjustment components while the other components are kept stable does\nnot exceed the limit value, this condition being met for the various\ncombinations of adjustment components other than the one which was\nvaried continuously."}
{"chapter_id": "2.5.2.5", "chapter_title": "The possible positions of the adjustment components shall be limited:", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.5.2.5.1.", "chapter_title": "on the one hand, by the larger of the following two values: the lowest idling", "raw_text": "speed which the engine can reach; the speed recommended by the\nmanufacturer, minus 100 revolutions per minute;"}
{"chapter_id": "2.5.2.5.2.", "chapter_title": "on the other hand, by the smallest of the following three values:", "raw_text": "the highest speed the engine can attain by activation of the idling speed components; the speed recommended by the\nmanufacturer, plus 250 revolutions per minute; the cut-in speed of automatic clutches."}
{"chapter_id": "2.5.2.6", "chapter_title": "In addition, settings incompatible with correct running of the engine shall not be", "raw_text": "adopted as measurement settings.  In particular, when the engine is equipped with\nseveral carburettors all the carburettors shall have the same setting."}
{"chapter_id": "3.", "chapter_title": "SAMPLING OF GASES", "raw_text": ""}

{"chapter_id": "4.", "chapter_title": "TEST EQUIPMENT FOR EVAPORATIVE TEST", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "4.1.", "chapter_title": "Chassis Dynamometer", "raw_text": "The chassis dynamometer shall meet the requirements of Annex 4."}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.", "chapter_title": "Evaporative Emission Measurement Enclosure", "raw_text": "The evaporative emission measurement enclosure shall be a gas-tight rectangular measuring chamber able to contain\nthe vehicle under test.  The vehicle shall be accessible from all sides and the enclosure when sealed shall\nbe gas-tight in accordance with Appendix 1 to this Annex.  The inner surface of the enclosure shall be\nimpermeable and non-reactive to hydrocarbons.  The temperature conditioning system shall be capable of\ncontrolling the internal enclosure air temperature to follow the prescribed temperature versus time profile\nthroughout the test, and an average tolerance of ± 1 K over the duration of the test.\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nThe control system shall be tuned to provide a smooth temperature pattern that has a minimum of overshoot, hunting,\nand instability about the desired long-term ambient temperature profile.  Interior surface temperatures shall\nnot be less than 278 K (5° C) nor more than 328 K (55° C) at any time during the diurnal emission test.\n\nWall design shall be such as to promote good dissipation of heat.  Interior surface temperatures shall not be below 293\nK (20° C), nor above 325 K (52° C) for the duration of the hot soak test.\n\nTo accommodate the volume changes due to enclosure temperature changes, either a variable-volume or fixed-volume\nenclosure may be used."}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.1.", "chapter_title": "Variable-volume Enclosure", "raw_text": "The variable-volume enclosure expands and contracts in response to the temperature change of the air mass in the\nenclosure.  Two potential means of accommodating the internal volume changes are movable panel(s), or\na bellows design, in which an impermeable bag or bags inside the enclosure expand(s) and contract(s) in\nresponse to internal pressure changes by exchanging air from outside the enclosure.  Any design for\nvolume accommodation shall maintain the integrity of the enclosure as specified in Appendix 1 to this Annex\nover the specified temperature range.\n\nAny method of volume accommodation shall limit the differential between the enclosure internal pressure and the\nbarometric pressure to a maximum value of ± 0.5 kPa.\n\nThe enclosure shall be capable of latching to a fixed volume.  A variable volume enclosure shall be capable of\naccommodating a + 7% change from its 'nominal volume' (see Appendix 1 to this Annex, Paragraph 2.1.1.),\ntaking into account temperature and barometric pressure variation during testing."}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.2.", "chapter_title": "Fixed-volume Enclosure", "raw_text": "The fixed-volume enclosure shall be constructed with rigid panels that maintain a fixed enclosure volume, and meet the\nrequirements below."}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.2.1.", "chapter_title": "The enclosure shall be equipped with an outlet flow stream that withdraws air at a low, constant rate from the", "raw_text": "enclosure throughout the test.  An inlet flow stream may provide make-up air to balance the outgoing flow\nwith incoming ambient air.  Inlet air shall be filtered with activated carbon to provide a relatively constant\nhydrocarbon level.  Any method of volume accommodation shall maintain the differential between the\nenclosure internal pressure and the barometric pressure between 0 and –5 kPa."}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.2.2.", "chapter_title": "The equipment shall be capable of measuring the mass of hydrocarbon in the inlet and outlet flow streams with", "raw_text": "a resolution of 0.01 gram.  A bag sampling system may be used to collect a proportional sample of the air\nwithdrawn from and admitted to the enclosure.  Alternatively, the inlet and outlet flow streams may be\ncontinuously analysed using an on-line FID analyser and integrated with the flow measurements to provide\na continuous record of the mass hydrocarbon removal.\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\n\nNote: 1. Evaporative emission control families – details clarified.\n2.Exhaust emissions may be measured during Type I test drive, but these are not used for legislative purposes.\nExhaust emission legislative test remains separate.\n\nFigure 7/1\n\nDetermination of Evaporative Emissions\n3,000 km run-in period (no excessive purge/load) Ageing of\nCanister(s) verified\nSteam clean of vehicle (if necessary)"}

Sample gas shall be drawn from the midpoint of one side wall or roof of the chamber\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nand any bypass flow shall be returned to the enclosure, preferably to a point immediately downstream of\nthe mixing fan."}

The recording system\nshall have operating characteristics at least equivalent to the signal being recorded and shall provide a\npermanent record of results.  The record shall show a positive indication of the beginning and end of the\nhot soak or diurnal emission test (including beginning and end of sampling periods along with the time\nelapsed between start and completion of each test)."}
{"chapter_id": "4.4.", "chapter_title": "Fuel Tank Heating (only applicable for gasoline canister load option)", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "4.4.1.", "chapter_title": "The fuel in the vehicle tank(s) shall be heated by a controllable source of heat: for example, a heating pad of 2,000", "raw_text": "W capacity is suitable.  The heating system shall apply heat evenly to the tank walls beneath the level of\nthe fuel so as not to cause local overheating of the fuel.  Heat shall not be applied to the vapour in the tank\nabove the fuel."}
{"chapter_id": "4.4.2.", "chapter_title": "The tank heating device shall make it possible to heat the fuel in the tank evenly by 14 K from 289 K (16° C) within", "raw_text": "60 minutes, with the temperature sensor position as in Paragraph 5.1.1. below.  The heating system shall\nbe capable of controlling the fuel temperature to ± 1.5 K of the required temperature during the tank heating\nprocess."}

The measuring points are extended approximately\n0.1 m into the enclosure from the vertical centre line of each side wall at a height of\n0.9 m ± 0.2 m."}
{"chapter_id": "4.5.2.", "chapter_title": "The temperatures of the fuel tank(s) are recorded by means of the sensor positioned in the fuel tank as in", "raw_text": "Paragraph 5.1.1. below in the case of use of the gasoline canister load option (Paragraph 5.1.5. below)."}

{"chapter_id": "5.", "chapter_title": "TEST PROCEDURE", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.", "chapter_title": "Test Preparation", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.1.", "chapter_title": "The vehicle is mechanically prepared before the test as follows:", "raw_text": "(a) The exhaust system of the vehicle shall not exhibit any leaks.\n\n(b) The vehicle may be steam-cleaned before the test.\n\n(c) In the case of use of the gasoline canister load option (Paragraph 5.1.5. below) the\nfuel tank of the vehicle shall be equipped with a temperature sensor to enable the\ntemperature to be measured at the midpoint of the fuel in the fuel tank when filled to\n40% of its capacity.\n\n(d) Additional fittings, adaptors of devices may be fitted to the fuel system in order to allow\na complete draining of the fuel tank.  For this purpose it is not necessary to modify the\nshell of the tank,\n\n(e) The manufacturer may propose a test method in order to take into account the loss of\nhydrocarbons by evaporation coming only from the fuel system of the vehicle."}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.2.", "chapter_title": "The vehicle is taken into the test area where the ambient temperature is between 293 and", "raw_text": "303 K (20° C and 30° C)."}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.3.", "chapter_title": "The ageing of the canister(s) has to be verified.  This may be done by demonstrating that it has", "raw_text": "accumulated a minimum of 3,000 km.  If this demonstration is not given, the following\nprocedure is used.  In the case of a multiple canister system each canister shall undergo the\nprocedure separately."}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.3.1.", "chapter_title": "The canister is removed from the vehicle.  Special care shall be taken during this step to avoid", "raw_text": "damage to components and the integrity of the fuel system."}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.3.2.", "chapter_title": "The weight of the canister shall be checked.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.3.3.", "chapter_title": "The canister is connected to a fuel tank, possibly an external one, filled with reference fuel, to 40%", "raw_text": "volume of the fuel tank(s)."}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.3.4.", "chapter_title": "The fuel temperature in the fuel tank shall be between 183 K and 287 K (10 and 14° C).", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.3.5.", "chapter_title": "The (external) fuel tank is heated from 288 K to 318 K (15 to 45° C) (1° C increase every 9 minutes).", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.3.6.", "chapter_title": "If the canister reaches breakthrough before the temperature reaches 318 K (45° C), the heat source", "raw_text": "shall be turned off.  Then the canister is weighed.  If the canister did not reach breakthrough\nduring the heating to 318 K (45° C), the procedure from Paragraph 5.1.3.3.\nabove shall be repeated until breakthrough occurs."}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.3.7.", "chapter_title": "Breakthrough may be checked as described in Paragraphs 5.1.5. and 5.1.6. of this Annex, or with the use of", "raw_text": "another sampling and analytical arrangement capable of detecting the emission of hydrocarbons from the\ncanister at breakthrough.\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.3.8.", "chapter_title": "The canister shall be purged with 25 ± 5 litres per minute with the emission laboratory air until 300 bed volume", "raw_text": "exchanges are reached."}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.3.9.", "chapter_title": "The weight of the canister shall be checked.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.3.10.", "chapter_title": "The steps of the procedure in Paragraphs 5.1.3.4. to 5.1.3.9. shall be repeated nine times.  The test may be", "raw_text": "terminated prior to that, after not less than three ageing cycles, if the weight of the canister after the last\ncycles has stabilised."}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.3.11.", "chapter_title": "The evaporative emission canister is reconnected and the vehicle restored to its normal operating condition.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.4.", "chapter_title": "One of the methods specified in Paragraphs 5.1.5. and 5.1.6. shall be used to precondition the evaporative", "raw_text": "canister.  For vehicles with multiple canisters, each canister shall be preconditioned separately."}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.4.1.", "chapter_title": "Canister emissions are measured to determine breakthrough.", "raw_text": "Breakthrough is here defined as the point at which the cumulative quantity of hydrocarbons emitted is equal to 2 grams."}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.4.2.", "chapter_title": "Breakthrough may be verified using the evaporative emission enclosure as described in Paragraphs 5.1.5. and", "raw_text": "\n5.1.6.respectively.  Alternatively, breakthrough may be determined using an auxiliary evaporative canister\nconnected downstream of the vehicle's canister.  The auxiliary canister shall be well purged with dry air\nprior to loading."}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.4.3.", "chapter_title": "The measuring chamber shall be purged for several minutes immediately before the test until a stable", "raw_text": "background is obtained.  The chamber air mixing fan(s) shall be switched on at this time.\n\nThe hydrocarbon analyser shall be zeroed and spanned immediately before the test."}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.5.", "chapter_title": "Canister loading with repeated heat builds to breakthrough.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.5.1.", "chapter_title": "The fuel tank(s) of the vehicle(s) is (are) emptied using the fuel tank drain(s).  This shall be done so as not to", "raw_text": "abnormally purge or abnormally load the evaporative control devices fitted to the vehicle.  Removal of the\nfuel cap is normally sufficient to achieve this."}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.5.2.", "chapter_title": "The fuel tank(s) is (are) refilled with test fuel at a temperature of between 283 K to 287 K", "raw_text": "(10 to 14° C). to 40% ± 2% of the tank(s) normal volumetric capacity.  The fuel cap(s) of the vehicle shall\nbe fitted at this point."}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.5.3.", "chapter_title": "Within one hour of being refuelled the vehicle shall be placed, with the engine shut off, in the evaporative", "raw_text": "emission enclosure.  The fuel tank temperature sensor is connected to the temperature recording system.\nA heat source shall be properly positioned with respect to the fuel tank(s) and connected to the temperature\ncontroller.  The heat source is specified in Paragraph 4.4. above.  In the case of vehicles fitted with more\nthan one fuel tank, all the tanks shall be heated in the same way as described below.  The temperatures of\nthe tanks shall be identical to within ± 1.5 K."}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.5.4.", "chapter_title": "The fuel may be artificially heated to the starting diurnal temperature of 293 K (20° C) ± 1 K.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.5.5.", "chapter_title": "When the fuel temperature reaches at least 292 K (19° C), the following steps shall be taken immediately: the", "raw_text": "purge blower shall be turned off; enclosure doors closed and sealed; and measurement initiated of the\nhydrocarbon level in the enclosure.\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.5.6.", "chapter_title": "When the fuel temperature of the fuel tank reaches 293 K (20° C), a linear heat build of 15 K (15° C) begins.", "raw_text": "The fuel shall be heated in such a way that the temperature of the fuel during the heating conforms to the\nfunction below to within ± 1.5 K.  The elapsed time of the heat build and temperature rise is recorded.\n\nTr = To + 0.2333 x t\nwhere:\n\nTr = required temperature (K);\n\nTo = initial temperature (K);\nt = time from start of the tank heat build in minutes."}
{"chapter_id": "5.1.5.7.", "chapter_title": "As soon as break-through occurs or when the fuel temperature reaches 308 K (35° C), whichever occurs first,", "raw_text": "the heat source is turned off, the enclosure doors unsealed and opened, and the vehicle fuel tank cap(s)\nremoved.  If break-through has not occurred by the time the fuel temperature 308 K (35° C), the heat source\nis removed from the vehicle, the vehicle removed from the evaporative emission enclosure and the entire\nprocedure outlined in Paragraph 5.1.7. below repeated until break-through occurs."}

{"chapter_id": "5.3.", "chapter_title": "Soak", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "5.3.1.", "chapter_title": "Within five minutes of completing the preconditioning operation specified in Paragraph 5.2.1. above the engine", "raw_text": "bonnet shall be completely closed and the vehicle driven off the chassis dynamometer and parked in the\nsoak area. The engine oil\nand coolant temperatures shall have reached the temperature of the area or within ± 3 K of it at the end of\nthe period."}
{"chapter_id": "5.4.", "chapter_title": "Dynamometer Test", "raw_text": ""}

{"chapter_id": "5.4.2.", "chapter_title": "Within two minutes of completing the Type I test drive specified in Paragraph 5.4.1. above the vehicle is driven a", "raw_text": "further conditioning drive consisting of one urban test cycle (hot start) of a Type I test.  Then the engine is\nshut off again.  Exhaust emissions need not be sampled during this operation."}
{"chapter_id": "5.5.", "chapter_title": "Hot Soak Evaporative Emissions Test", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "5.5.1.", "chapter_title": "Before the completion of the test run the measuring chamber shall be purged for several minutes until a stable", "raw_text": "hydrocarbon background is obtained.  The enclosure mixing fan(s) shall also be turned on at this time."}
{"chapter_id": "5.5.2.", "chapter_title": "The hydrocarbon analyser shall be zeroed and spanned immediately prior to the test.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "5.5.3.", "chapter_title": "At the end of the driving cycle the engine bonnet shall be completely closed and all connections between the", "raw_text": "vehicle and the test stand disconnected.  The vehicle is then driven to the measuring chamber with a\nminimum use of the accelerator pedal.  The engine shall be turned off before any part of the vehicle enters\nthe measuring chamber.  The time at which the engine is switched off is recorded on the evaporative\nemission measurement data recording system and temperature recording begins.  The vehicle's windows\nand luggage compartments shall be opened at this stage, if not already opened."}
{"chapter_id": "5.5.4.", "chapter_title": "The vehicle shall be pushed or otherwise moved into the measuring chamber with the engine switched off.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "5.5.5.", "chapter_title": "The enclosure doors are closed and sealed gas-tight within two minutes of the engine being switched off and", "raw_text": "within seven minutes of the end of the conditioning drive."}
{"chapter_id": "5.5.6.", "chapter_title": "The start of a 60 ± 0.5 minute hot soak period begins when the chamber is sealed.  The hydrocarbon", "raw_text": "concentration, temperature and barometric pressure are measured to give the initial readings CHCi, Pi and\nTi for the hot soak test.  These figures are used in the evaporative emission calculation, Paragraph 6. below.\nThe ambient temperature T of the enclosure shall not be less than 296 K and no more than 304 K during\nthe 60-minute hot soak period."}
{"chapter_id": "5.5.7.", "chapter_title": "The hydrocarbon analyser shall be zeroed and spanned immediately before the end of the", "raw_text": "60 ± 0.5 minute test period.\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "5.5.8.", "chapter_title": "At the end of the 60 ± 0.5 minute test period, the hydrocarbon concentration in the chamber shall be", "raw_text": "measured.  The temperature and the barometric pressure are also measured.  These are the final\nreadings CHCf, Pf and Tf for the hot soak test used for the calculation in Paragraph 6. below."}
{"chapter_id": "5.6.", "chapter_title": "Soak", "raw_text": ""}

{"chapter_id": "5.7.", "chapter_title": "Diurnal Test", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "5.7.1.", "chapter_title": "The test vehicle shall be exposed to one cycle of ambient temperature according to the profile specified in", "raw_text": "Appendix 2 to this Annex with a maximum deviation of ± 2 K at any time.  The average temperature\ndeviation from the profile, calculated using the absolute value of each measured deviation, shall not exceed\n± 1 K.  Ambient temperature shall be measured at least every minute.  Temperature cycling begins when\ntime Tstart = 0, as specified in Paragraph 5.7.6. below."}
{"chapter_id": "5.7.2.", "chapter_title": "The measuring chamber shall be purged for several minutes immediately before the test until a stable background", "raw_text": "is obtainable.  The chamber mixing fan(s) shall also be switched on at this time."}
{"chapter_id": "5.7.3.", "chapter_title": "The test vehicle, with the engine shut off and the test vehicle windows and luggage compartment(s) opened shall", "raw_text": "be moved into the measuring chamber.  The mixing fan(s) shall be adjusted in such a way as to maintain\na minimum air circulation speed of 8 km/h under the fuel tank of the test vehicle."}
{"chapter_id": "5.7.4.", "chapter_title": "The hydrocarbon analyser shall be zeroed and spanned immediately before the test.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "5.7.5.", "chapter_title": "The enclosure doors shall be closed and gas-tight sealed.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "5.7.6.", "chapter_title": "Within 10 minutes of closing and sealing the doors, the hydrocarbon concentration,", "raw_text": "temperature and barometric pressure are measured to give the initial readings CHCi, Pi and Ti for the diurnal\ntest. This is the point where time Tstart = 0"}
{"chapter_id": "5.7.7.", "chapter_title": "The hydrocarbon analyser shall be zeroed and spanned immediately before the end of the test.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "5.7.8.", "chapter_title": "The end of the emission sampling period occurs 24 hours ± 6 minutes after the beginning of the initial sampling,", "raw_text": "as specified in Paragraph 5.7.6. above.  The time elapsed is recorded.  The hydrocarbon concentration,\ntemperature and barometric pressure are measured to give the final readings CHC,f, Pf and Tf for the diurnal\ntest used for the calculation in Paragraph 6.  This completes the evaporative emission test procedure."}
{"chapter_id": "6.", "chapter_title": "CALCULATION", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "6.1.", "chapter_title": "The evaporative emission tests described in Paragraph 5 allow the hydrocarbon emissions from the diurnal and hot", "raw_text": "soak phases to be calculated.  Evaporative losses from each of these phases is calculated using the initial\nand final hydrocarbon concentrations, temperatures and pressures in the enclosure, together with the net\nenclosure volume.\n\nThe formula below is used:\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\nMHC = k × V × 10−4 ⎛⎜⎜ CHC.fTf ⋅ Pf − CHC.iTi ⋅ Pi ⎟⎠⎞⎟ + MHC,out − MHC,i\n⎝\nwhere:\n\nMHC = hydrocarbon mass in grams\n\nMHC,out = mass of hydrocarbon exiting the enclosure, in the case of fixed-volume enclosures for diurnal\nemission testing (grams).\n\nMHC,i = mass of hydrocarbon entering the enclosure, in the case of fixed-volume enclosures for diurnal\nemission testing (grams).\n\nCHC = measured hydrocarbon concentration in the enclosure (ppm volume in C1, equivalent)\n\nV = net enclosure volume in cubic metres corrected for the volume of the vehicle. with the windows and the\nluggage compartment open.  If the volume of the vehicle is not determined a volume of 1.42\nm3 is subtracted.\n\nT = ambient chamber temperature, in K\n\nP = barometric pressure in kPa\n\nH/C = hydrogen to carbon ratio\nk =  1.2 × (12 + H/C)\nwhere:\n\ni = is the initial reading\n\nf = is the final reading\n\nH/C = is taken to be 2.33 for diurnal test losses\n\nH/C = is taken to be 2.20 for hot soak losses."}
{"chapter_id": "6.2.", "chapter_title": "Overall Results of Test", "raw_text": "The overall hydrocarbon mass emission for the vehicle is taken to be:\n\nMtotal = MDI + MHS\nwhere:\n\nMtotal = overall mass emissions of the vehicle (grams)\n\nMDI = hydrocarbon mass emission for diurnal test (grams)\n\nMHS = hydrocarbon mass emission for the hot soak (grams).\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}

If six consecutive monthly retention checks are\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nsuccessfully completed without corrective action, the enclosure leak rate may be determined quarterly\nthereafter as long as no corrective action is required."}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.1.", "chapter_title": "The enclosure shall be purged until a stable hydrocarbon concentration is reached.  The", "raw_text": "mixing fan is turned on, if not already switched on.  The hydrocarbon analyser is zeroed,\ncalibrated if required, and spanned."}

{"chapter_id": "2.3.5.", "chapter_title": "A quantity of approximately 4 grams of propane is injected into the enclosure.  The mass", "raw_text": "of propane shall be measured to an accuracy and precision of ± 2% of the measured value."}

{"chapter_id": "2.3.9.", "chapter_title": "The process is then begun of cycling the ambient temperature from 308 K (35° C) to 293", "raw_text": "K (20° C) and back to 308 K (35° C) [308.6 K (35.6° C) to 295.2 K (22.2° C) and back to\n308.6 K (35.6° C)] over a 24-hour period according to the profile [alternative profile] specified in Appendix\n2to this Annex within 15 minutes of sealing the enclosure.  (Tolerances as specified in Paragraph 5.7.1. of\nAnnex 7)."}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.10.", "chapter_title": "At the completion of the 24-hour cycling period, the final hydrocarbon concentration,", "raw_text": "temperature and barometric pressure are measured and recorded.  These are the final\nreadings CHCf, Pf and Tf for the hydrocarbon retention check."}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.11.", "chapter_title": "Using the formula in Paragraph 2.4. below, the hydrocarbon mass is then calculated from", "raw_text": "the readings taken in Paragraphs 2.3.10. and 2.3.6. above.  The mass may not differ by\nmore than 3% from the hydrocarbon mass given in Paragraph 2.3.7. above."}
{"chapter_id": "2.4.", "chapter_title": "Calculations", "raw_text": "COUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nThe calculation of net hydrocarbon mass change within the enclosure is used to determine the chamber's\nhydrocarbon background and leak rate.  Initial and final readings of hydrocarbon concentration,\ntemperature and barometric pressure are used in the following formula to calculate the mass change.\n\nMHC = k × V × 10−4 ⎜⎜⎛ CHC,fTf× Pf − CHC,iTi× Pi ⎟⎠⎟⎞ + MHC,out − MHC,i\n⎝\nwhere:\n\nMHc = hydrocarbon mass in grams,\n\nMHC,out = mass of hydrocarbons exiting the enclosure, in the case of fixed-volume enclosures for diurnal\nemission testing (grams),\n\nMHC,i = mass of hydrocarbons entering the enclosure when a fixed-volume enclosure is used for testing\ndiurnal emissions (grams),\n\nCHc = hydrocarbon concentration in the enclosure (ppm carbon (note ppm carbon = ppm propane x 3)),\n\nV = enclosure volume in cubic metres,\n\nT = ambient temperature in the enclosure, K,\n\nP = barometric pressure, kPa,\n\nk = 17.6;\n\nwhere:\ni is the initial reading,\nf is the final reading."}
{"chapter_id": "3.", "chapter_title": "CHECKING OF FID HYDROCARBON ANALYSER", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.", "chapter_title": "Detector Response Optimisation", "raw_text": "The FID shall be adjusted as specified by the instrument manufacturer.  Propane in air should be used to\noptimise the response on the most common operating range."}
{"chapter_id": "3.2.", "chapter_title": "Calibration of the HC Analyser", "raw_text": "The analyser should be calibrated using propane in air and purified synthetic air.  See Paragraph 4.5.2. of\nAnnex 4, (calibration and span gases).\n\nEstablish a calibration curve as described in Paragraphs 4.1 to 4.5. of this Appendix."}
{"chapter_id": "3.3.", "chapter_title": "Oxygen Interference Check and Recommended Limits", "raw_text": "The response factor (Rf), for a particular hydrocarbon species is the ratio of the FID C1 reading to the gas\ncylinder concentration, expressed as ppm C1.  The concentration of the test gas shall be at a level to give\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\na response of approximately 80% of full-scale deflection, for the operating range.  The concentration shall\nbe known to an accuracy of ± 2% in reference to a gravimetric standard expressed in volume.  In addition\nthe gas cylinder shall be preconditioned for 24 hours at a temperature between 293 K and 303 K (20° C\nand\n30° C).\n\nResponse factors should be determined when introducing an analyser into service and thereafter at major\nservice intervals.  The reference gas to be used is propane with balance purified air which is taken to give\na response factor of 1.00.\n\nThe test gas to be used for oxygen interference and the recommended response factor range are given\nbelow:\n\nPropane and nitrogen 0.95 ≤ Rf ≤ 1.05"}
{"chapter_id": "4.", "chapter_title": "CALIBRATION OF THE HYDROCARBON ANALYSER", "raw_text": "Each of the normally used operating ranges are calibrated by the following procedure:"}
{"chapter_id": "4.1.", "chapter_title": "Establish the calibration curve by at least five calibration points spaced as evenly as possible over", "raw_text": "the operating range.  The nominal concentration of the calibration gas with the highest\nconcentrations to be at least 80% of the full scale."}
{"chapter_id": "4.2.", "chapter_title": "Calculate the calibration curve by the method of least squares.  If the resulting polynomial degree", "raw_text": "is greater than 3, then the number of calibration points shall be at least the number of the polynomial\ndegree plus 2."}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.", "chapter_title": "The calibration curve shall not differ by more than 2% from the nominal value of each calibration", "raw_text": "gas."}
{"chapter_id": "4.4.", "chapter_title": "Using the coefficients of the polynomial derived from Paragraph 3.2. above, a table of indicated", "raw_text": "reading against true concentration shall be drawn up in steps of no greater than 1% of full scale.\nThis is to be carried out for each analyser range calibrated.  The table shall also contain other\nrelevant data such as:\n\n(a) Date of calibration, span and zero potentiometer readings (where applicable),\n\n(b) Nominal scale,\n\n(c) Reference data of each calibration gas used,\n\n(d) The actual and indicated value of each calibration gas used together with the percentage\ndifferences.\n\n(e) FID fuel and type.\n\n(f) FID air pressure."}
{"chapter_id": "4.5.", "chapter_title": "If it can be shown to the satisfaction of the technical service that alternative technology (e.g.", "raw_text": "computer, electronically controlled range switch) can give equivalent accuracy, then those\nalternatives may be used.\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}

{"chapter_id": "4.3.", "chapter_title": "Soak Methods", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.1.", "chapter_title": "One of the following two methods, to be selected by the manufacturer, shall be utilised to", "raw_text": "stabilise the vehicle before the emission test."}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.2.", "chapter_title": "Standard Method.", "raw_text": "The vehicle is stored for not less than 12 hours nor for more than 36 hours prior to the low ambient temperature exhaust\nemission test.  The ambient temperature (dry bulb) during this period shall be maintained at an average\ntemperature of:\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n266 K (-7° C) ± 3 K during each hour of this period and shall not be less than 260 K (-13° C) nor more than 272 K (-1°\nC).  In addition, the temperature may not fall below 263 K (-10° C) nor more than 269 K (-4° C) for more\nthan three consecutive minutes."}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.3.", "chapter_title": "Forced Method", "raw_text": "The vehicle shall be stored for not more than 36 hours prior to the low ambient temperature exhaust emission test."}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.3.1.", "chapter_title": "The vehicle shall not be stored at ambient temperatures which exceed 303 K (30°", "raw_text": "C) during this period."}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.3.2.", "chapter_title": "Vehicle cooling may be accomplished by force-cooling the vehicle to the test", "raw_text": "temperature.  If cooling is augmented by fans, the fans shall be placed in a vertical\nposition so that the maximum cooling of the drive train and engine is achieved and\nnot primarily the sump.  Fans shall not be placed under the vehicle."}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.3.3.", "chapter_title": "The ambient temperature need only be stringently controlled after the vehicle has", "raw_text": "been cooled to: 266 K (-7° C) ± 2 K, as determined by a representative bulk oil\ntemperature.\n\nA representative bulk oil temperature is the temperature of the oil measured near the middle of the oil sump, not at the\nsurface or at the bottom of the oil sump.  If two or more diverse locations in the oil are monitored, they shall\nall meet the temperature requirements."}
{"chapter_id": "4.3.3.4.", "chapter_title": "The vehicle shall be stored for at least one hour after is has been cooled to 266 K", "raw_text": "(-7° C) ± 2 K, prior to the low ambient temperature exhaust emission test. {"chapter_id": "4.3.4.", "chapter_title": "If the vehicle is stabilised at 266 K (-7° C), in a separate area and is moved through a warm", "raw_text": "area to the test cell, the vehicle shall be destabilised in the test cell for at least six times\nthe period the vehicle is exposed to warmer temperatures.  The ambient temperature (dry\nbulb) during this period shall average 266 K (-7° C) ± 3 K and shall not be less than 260 K\n(-13° C) nor more than 272 K (-1° C).\n\nIn addition, the temperature may not fall below 263 K (-10° C) or exceed 269 K (-4° C), for more than three consecutive\nminutes."}

Engine start-up, immediate sampling, operation over\nthe Part One cycle and engine shut-down make a complete low ambient temperature test,\nwith a total test time of 780 seconds.  The exhaust emissions are diluted with ambient air\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nand a continuously proportional sample is collected for analysis. {"chapter_id": "5.4.2.", "chapter_title": "Operation on Track or Road", "raw_text": "When the durability test is completed on track or road, the vehicle's reference mass will be at least equal\nto that retained for tests conducted on a chassis dynamometer."}
{"chapter_id": "6.", "chapter_title": "MEASURING EMISSIONS OF POLLUTANTS", "raw_text": "At the start of the test (0 km), and every 10,000 km (± 400 km) or more frequently, at regular intervals, until\nhaving covered 80,000 km, exhaust emissions are measured in accordance with the Type I test as defined\nin Paragraph 5.3.1. of this Regulation.  The limit values to be complied with are those laid down in\nParagraph 5.3.1.4. of this Regulation.\n\nIn the case of vehicles equipped with periodically regenerating systems as defined in Paragraph 2.20. of\nthis Regulation, it shall be checked that the vehicle is not approaching a regeneration period.  If this is the\ncase, the vehicle must be driven until the end of the regeneration.  If a regeneration occurs during the\nemissions measurement, a new test (including preconditioning) shall be performed, and the first result not\ntaken into account.\n\nAll exhaust emissions results shall be plotted as a function of the running distance on the system rounded\nto the nearest kilometre and the best fit straight lines fitted by the method of least squares drawn through\nall these data points.  This calculation shall not take into account test results at 0 km.\n\nThe data will be acceptable for use in the calculation of the deterioration factor only if the interpolated 6,400\nkm and 80,000 km points on this line are within the above-mentioned limits.\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\nThe data are still acceptable when a best fit straight line crosses an applicable limit with a negative slope\n(the 6,400 km interpolated point is higher than the 80,000 km interpolated point) but the actual 80,000 km\nactual data point is below the limit.\n\nA multiplicative exhaust emission deterioration factor shall be calculated for each pollutant as follows:\n\nMi2\nD.E.F. = Mi1\nwhere:\n\nMi1 = mass emission of the pollutant i in g/km interpolated to 6,400 km,\n\nMi2 = mass emission of the pollutant i in g/km interpolated to 80,000 km.\n\nThese interpolated values shall be carried out to a minimum of four places to the right of the decimal point\nbefore dividing one by the other to determine the deterioration factor.  The result shall be rounded to three\nplaces to the right of the decimal point.\n\nIf a deterioration factor is less than one, it is deemed to be equal to one."}
