{"chapter_id": "1.", "chapter_title": "INTRODUCTION", "raw_text": "This Annex applies to the functional aspects of on-board diagnostic (OBD) system for the emission control\nof motor vehicles."}
{"chapter_id": "2.", "chapter_title": "DEFINITIONS", "raw_text": "For the purposes of this Annex:"}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.", "chapter_title": "\"OBD\" means an on-board diagnostic system for emission control which shall have", "raw_text": "the capability of identifying the likely area of malfunction by means of fault codes stored\nin computer memory."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.", "chapter_title": "\"Vehicle type\" means a category of power-driven vehicles which do not differ in such", "raw_text": "essential engine and OBD system characteristics."}
{"chapter_id": "2.3.", "chapter_title": "\"Vehicle family\" means a manufacturer's grouping of vehicles which, through their", "raw_text": "design, are expected to have similar exhaust emission and OBD system\ncharacteristics.  Each vehicle of this family shall have complied with the requirements\nof this Regulation as defined in Appendix 2 to this Annex."}
{"chapter_id": "2.4.", "chapter_title": "\"Emission control system\" means the electronic engine management controller and", "raw_text": "any emission-related component in the exhaust or evaporative system which supplies\nan input to or receives an output from this controller."}
{"chapter_id": "2.5.", "chapter_title": "\"Malfunction indicator (MI)\" means a visible or audible indicator that clearly informs", "raw_text": "the driver of the vehicle in the event of a malfunction of any emission-related\ncomponent connected to the OBD system, or the OBD system itself.\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "2.6.", "chapter_title": "\"Malfunction\" means the failure of an emission-related component or system that", "raw_text": "would result in emissions exceeding the limits in Paragraph 3.3.2. or if the OBD system\nis unable to fulfil the basic monitoring requirements of this Annex."}
{"chapter_id": "2.7.", "chapter_title": "\"Secondary air\" refers to air introduced into the exhaust system by means of a pump", "raw_text": "or aspirator valve or other means that is intended to aid in the oxidation of HC and CO\ncontained in the exhaust gas stream."}
{"chapter_id": "2.8.", "chapter_title": "\"Engine misfire\" means lack of combustion in the cylinder of a positive-ignition engine", "raw_text": "due to absence of spark, poor fuel metering, poor compression or any other cause.  In\nterms of OBD monitoring it is that percentage of misfires out of a total number of firing\nevents (as declared by the manufacturer) that would result in emissions exceeding the\nlimits given in Paragraph 3.3.2 or that percentage that could lead to an exhaust\ncatalyst, or catalysts, overheating causing irreversible damage."}
{"chapter_id": "2.9.", "chapter_title": "\"Type I test\" means the driving cycle (Parts One and Two) used for emission", "raw_text": "approvals, as detailed in Annex 4, Appendix 1."}
{"chapter_id": "2.10.", "chapter_title": "\"A driving cycle\" consists of engine start-up, driving mode where a malfunction would", "raw_text": "be detected if present, and engine shut-off."}
{"chapter_id": "2.11.", "chapter_title": "\"A warm-up cycle\" means sufficient vehicle operation such that the coolant", "raw_text": "temperature has risen by at least 22 K from engine starting and reaches a minimum\ntemperature of 343 K\n(70° C)."}
{"chapter_id": "2.12.", "chapter_title": "A \"Fuel trim\" refers to feedback adjustments to the base fuel schedule.  Short-term", "raw_text": "fuel trim refers to dynamic or instantaneous adjustments.  Long-term fuel trim refers to\nmuch more gradual adjustments to the fuel calibration schedule than short-term trim\nadjustments.  These long-term adjustments compensate for vehicle differences and\ngradual changes that occur over time."}
{"chapter_id": "2.13.", "chapter_title": "A \"Calculated load value\" refers to an indication of the current airflow divided by peak", "raw_text": "airflow, where peak airflow is corrected for altitude, if available.  This definition provides\na dimensionless number that is not engine specific and provides the service technician\nwith an indication of the proportion of engine capacity that is being used (with wide\nopen throttle as 100%);\n\nCurrent airflow\nAtmospheric pressure (at sea level)\nCLV = ×\n\nPeak airflow at sea level( )\nBarometric pressure"}
{"chapter_id": "2.14.", "chapter_title": "\"Permanent emission default mode\" refers to a case where the engine management", "raw_text": "controller permanently switches to a setting that does not require an input from a failed\ncomponent or system where such a failed component or system would result in an\nincrease in emissions from the vehicle to a level above the limits given in Paragraph\n3.3.2.of this Annex."}
{"chapter_id": "2.15.", "chapter_title": "\"Power take-off unit\" means an engine-driven output provision for the purposes of", "raw_text": "powering auxiliary, vehicle mounted, equipment.\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "2.16.", "chapter_title": "\"Access\" means the availability of all emission-related OBD data including all fault", "raw_text": "codes required for the inspection, diagnosis, servicing or repair of emissions-related\nparts of the vehicle, via the serial interface for the standard diagnostic connection\n(pursuant to Appendix 1 to this Annex, Paragraph 6.5.3.5)."}
{"chapter_id": "2.17.", "chapter_title": "\"Unrestricted\" means:", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.17.1.", "chapter_title": "Access not dependent on an access code obtainable only from the", "raw_text": "manufacturer, or a similar device, or"}
{"chapter_id": "2.17.2.", "chapter_title": "Access allowing evaluation of the data produced without the need for any", "raw_text": "unique decoding information, unless that information itself is standardised."}
{"chapter_id": "2.18.", "chapter_title": "\"Standardised\" means that all data stream information, including all fault codes used,", "raw_text": "shall be produced only in accordance with industry standards which, by virtue of the\nfact that their format and their permitted options are clearly defined, provide for a\nmaximum level of harmonisation in the motor vehicle industry, and whose use is\nexpressly permitted in this Regulation."}
{"chapter_id": "2.19.", "chapter_title": "\"Repair information\" means all information required for diagnosis, servicing,", "raw_text": "inspection, periodic monitoring or repair of the vehicle and which the manufacturers\nprovide for their authorised dealers/repair shops.  Where necessary, such information\nshall include service handbooks, technical manuals, diagnosis information (e.g.\nminimum and maximum theoretical values for measurements), wiring diagrams, the\nsoftware calibration identification number applicable to a vehicle type, instructions for\nindividual and special cases, information provided concerning tools and equipment,\ndata record information and two-directional monitoring and test data.  The\nmanufacturer shall not be obliged to make available that information which is covered\nby intellectual property rights or constitutes specific know-how of manufacturers and/or\nOEM suppliers; in this case the necessary technical information shall not be improperly\nwithheld."}
{"chapter_id": "2.20.", "chapter_title": "\"Deficiency\" means, in respect of vehicle OBD systems, that up to two separate", "raw_text": "components or systems that are monitored contain temporary or permanent operating\ncharacteristics that impair the otherwise efficient OBD monitoring of those components\nor systems or do not meet all of the other detailed requirements for OBD.  Vehicles\nmay be type-approved, registered and sold with such deficiencies according to the\nrequirements of Paragraph 4 of this Annex."}
{"chapter_id": "3.", "chapter_title": "REQUIREMENTS AND TESTS", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.", "chapter_title": "All vehicles shall be equipped with an OBD system so designed, constructed and", "raw_text": "installed in a vehicle as to enable it to identify types of deterioration or malfunction over\nthe entire life of the vehicle.  In achieving this objective the approval authority shall\naccept that vehicles which have travelled distances in excess of the Type V durability\ndistance, referred to in Paragraph 3.3.1, may show some deterioration in OBD system\nperformance such that the emission limits given in Paragraph 3.3.2 may be exceeded\nbefore the OBD system signals a failure to the driver of the vehicle.\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.1.", "chapter_title": "Access to the OBD system required for the inspection, diagnosis, servicing or", "raw_text": "repair of the vehicle shall be unrestricted and standardised.  All emission-\nrelated fault codes shall be consistent with Paragraph 6.5.3.4. of Appendix 1\nto this Annex."}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.2.", "chapter_title": "No later than three months after the manufacturer has provided any authorised", "raw_text": "dealer or repair shop with repair information, the manufacturer shall make that\ninformation (including all subsequent  amendments and supplements)\navailable upon reasonable and non-discriminatory\npayment and shall notify the approval authority accordingly.\n\nIn the event of failure to comply with these provisions the approval authority shall act to ensure that repair\ninformation is available, in accordance with the procedures laid down for type-approval and in-\nservice surveys."}
{"chapter_id": "3.2.", "chapter_title": "The OBD system shall be so designed, constructed and installed in a vehicle as to", "raw_text": "enable it to comply with the requirements of this Annex during conditions of normal\nuse."}
{"chapter_id": "3.2.1.", "chapter_title": "Temporary Disablement of the OBD System", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.2.1.1.", "chapter_title": "A manufacturer may disable the OBD system if its ability to monitor is", "raw_text": "affected by low fuel levels.  Disablement shall not occur when the fuel\ntank level is above 20% of the nominal capacity of the fuel tank."}
{"chapter_id": "3.2.1.2.", "chapter_title": "A manufacturer may disable the OBD system at ambient engine", "raw_text": "starting temperatures below 266 K (-7° C) or at elevations over 2 500\nmetres above sea level provided the manufacturer submits data\nand/or an engineering evaluation which adequately demonstrate that\nmonitoring would be unreliable when such conditions exist.  A\nmanufacturer may also request disablement of the OBD system at\nother ambient engine starting temperatures if he demonstrates to the\nauthority with data and/or an engineering evaluation that misdiagnosis\nwould occur under such conditions.  It is not necessary to illuminate\nthe malfunction indicator (MI) if the OBD thresholds are exceeded\nduring a regeneration provided no defect is present."}
{"chapter_id": "3.2.1.3.", "chapter_title": "For vehicles designed to accommodate the installation of power take-", "raw_text": "off units, disablement of affected monitoring systems is permitted\nprovided disablement occurs only when the power take-off unit is\nactive."}
{"chapter_id": "3.2.2.", "chapter_title": "Engine Misfire in Vehicles Equipped with Positive-ignition Engines", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.2.2.1.", "chapter_title": "Manufacturers may adopt higher misfire percentage malfunction", "raw_text": "criteria than those declared to the authority, under specific engine\nspeed and load conditions where it can be demonstrated to the\nauthority that the detection of lower levels of misfire would be\nunreliable.\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "3.2.2.2.", "chapter_title": "When a manufacturer can demonstrate to the authority that the", "raw_text": "detection of higher levels of misfire percentages is still not feasible, or\nthat misfire cannot be distinguished from other effects (e.g. rough\nroads, transmission shifts, after engine starting; etc.) the misfire\nmonitoring system may be disabled when such conditions exist."}
{"chapter_id": "3.3.", "chapter_title": "Description of Tests", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.3.1.", "chapter_title": "The test are carried out on the vehicle used for the Type V durability test, given", "raw_text": "in Annex 9, and using the test procedure in Appendix 1 to this Annex.  Tests\nare carried out at the conclusion of the Type V durability testing.\n\nWhen no Type V durability testing is carried out, or at the request of the manufacturer, a suitably aged\nand representative vehicle may be used for these OBD demonstration tests."}

{"chapter_id": "3.3.3.", "chapter_title": "Monitoring Requirements for Vehicles Equipped with Positive-ignition Engines", "raw_text": "In satisfying the requirements of Paragraph 3.3.2 the OBD system shall, at a minimum, monitor for:"}
{"chapter_id": "3.3.3.1.", "chapter_title": "Reduction in the efficiency of the catalytic converter with respect to", "raw_text": "the emissions of HC only.  Manufacturers may monitor the front\ncatalyst alone or in combination with the next catalyst(s) downstream.\nEach monitored catalyst or catalyst combination shall be considered\nmalfunctioning when the emissions exceed the HC threshold given in\ntable in Paragraph 3.3.2.;"}
{"chapter_id": "3.3.3.2.", "chapter_title": "The presence of engine misfire in the engine operating region", "raw_text": "bounded by the following lines:\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\n(a) a maximum speed of 4 500 min-1 or 1 000 min-1 greater than the\nhighest speed occurring during a Type I test cycle, whichever is\nthe lower;\n\n(b) the positive torque line (i.e. engine load with the transmission in\nneutral);\n\n(c) a line joining the following engine operating points: the positive\ntorque line at 3 000 min-1 and a point on the maximum speed line\ndefined in (a) above with the engine's manifold vacuum at 13.33\nkPa lower than that at the positive torque line."}
{"chapter_id": "3.3.3.3.", "chapter_title": "Oxygen sensor deterioration", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.3.3.4.", "chapter_title": "If active on the selected fuel, other emission control system", "raw_text": "components or systems, or emission-related power-train components\nor systems which are connected to a computer, the failure of which\nmay result in tailpipe emissions exceeding the limits given in\nParagraph 3.3.2;"}
{"chapter_id": "3.3.3.5.", "chapter_title": "Unless otherwise monitored, any other emission-related power-train", "raw_text": "component connected to a computer, including any relevant sensors\nto enable monitoring functions to be carried out, shall be monitored for\ncircuit continuity;"}
{"chapter_id": "3.3.3.6.", "chapter_title": "The electronic evaporative emission purge control shall, at a", "raw_text": "minimum, be monitored for circuit continuity."}
{"chapter_id": "3.3.4.", "chapter_title": "Monitoring Requirements for Vehicles Equipped with Compression-ignition", "raw_text": "Engines\n\nIn satisfying the requirements of Paragraph 3.3.2 the OBD system shall monitor:"}
{"chapter_id": "3.3.4.1.", "chapter_title": "Where fitted, reduction in the efficiency of the catalytic converter;", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.3.4.2.", "chapter_title": "Where fitted, the functionality and integrity of the particulate trap;", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.3.4.3.", "chapter_title": "The fuel-injection system electronic fuel quantity and timing", "raw_text": "actuator(s) is/are monitored for circuit continuity and total functional\nfailure;"}
{"chapter_id": "3.3.4.4.", "chapter_title": "Other emission control system components or systems, or emission-", "raw_text": "related power-train components or systems, which are connected to\na computer, the failure of which may result in exhaust emissions\nexceeding the limits given in Paragraph 3.3.2.  Examples of such\nsystems or components are those for monitoring and control of air\nmass-flow, air volumetric flow (and temperature), boost pressure and\ninlet manifold pressure (and relevant sensors to enable these\nfunctions to be carried out).\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "3.3.4.5.", "chapter_title": "Unless otherwise monitored, any other emission-related power-train", "raw_text": "component connected to a computer shall be monitored for circuit\ncontinuity."}
{"chapter_id": "3.3.5.", "chapter_title": "Manufacturers may demonstrate to the approval authority that certain", "raw_text": "components or systems need not be monitored if, in the event of their total\nfailure or removal, emissions do not exceed the emission limits given in\nParagraph 3.3.2."}
{"chapter_id": "3.4.", "chapter_title": "A sequence of diagnostic checks shall be initiated at each engine start and completed", "raw_text": "at least once provided that the correct test conditions are met.  The test conditions\nshall be selected in such a way that they all occur under normal driving as represented\nby the Type I test."}
{"chapter_id": "3.5.", "chapter_title": "Activation of Malfunction Indicator (MI)", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.5.1.", "chapter_title": "The OBD system shall incorporate a malfunction indicator readily perceivable", "raw_text": "to the vehicle operator.  The MI shall not be used for any other purpose except\nto indicate emergency start-up or limp-home routines to the driver.  The MI\nshall be visible in all reasonable lighting conditions.  When activated, it shall\ndisplay a symbol in conformity with ISO 2575 (1).  A vehicle shall not be\nequipped with more than one general purpose MI for emission-related\nproblems.  Separate specific purpose telltales (e.g. brake system, fasten seat\nbelt, oil pressure, etc.) are permitted.  The use of red colour for an MI is\nprohibited."}
{"chapter_id": "3.5.2.", "chapter_title": "For strategies requiring more than two preconditioning cycles for MI activation,", "raw_text": "the manufacturer shall provide data and/or an engineering evaluation which\nadequately demonstrates that the monitoring system is equally effective and\ntimely in detecting component deterioration.  Strategies requiring on average\nmore than 10 driving cycles for MI activation are not accepted.  The MI shall\nalso activate whenever the engine control enters a permanent emission\ndefault mode of operation if the emission limits given in Paragraph 3.3.2 are\nexceeded or if the OBD system is unable to fulfil the basic monitoring\nrequirements specified in Paragraph 3.3.3. or 3.3.4. of this Annex.  The MI\nmust operate in a distinct warning mode, e.g. a flashing light, under any period\nduring which engine misfire occurs at a level likely to cause catalyst damage,\nas specified by the manufacturer.  The MI must also activate when the\nvehicle's ignition is in the \"key-on\" position before engine starting or cranking\nand de-activate after engine starting if no malfunction has previously been\ndetected."}
{"chapter_id": "3.6.", "chapter_title": "The OBD system must record fault code(s) indicating the status of the emission-control", "raw_text": "system.  Separate status codes must be used to identify correctly functioning emission\ncontrol systems and those emission control systems which need further vehicle\noperation to be fully evaluated.  If the MI is activated due to deterioration or malfunction\nor permanent emission default modes of operation, a fault code must be stored that\nidentifies the type of malfunction.  A fault code must also be stored in the cases referred\nto in Paragraphs 3.3.3.5.\nand 3.3.4.5. of this Annex.\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "3.6.1.", "chapter_title": "The distance travelled by the vehicle while the MI is activated shall be available", "raw_text": "at any instant through the serial port on the standard link connector (2)."}
{"chapter_id": "3.6.2.", "chapter_title": "In the case of vehicles equipped with positive-ignition engines, misfiring", "raw_text": "cylinders need not be uniquely identified if a distinct single or multiple cylinder\nmisfire fault code is stored.\n\n\n(1)\nInternational Standard ISO 2575-1982 (E), entitled 'Road vehicles: Symbols for control indicators and tell-tales', Symbol Number\n4.36.\n(2)\nThis requirement is only applicable from January 1, 2003 to new types of vehicles with an electronic speed input to the engine\nmanagement.  It applies to all vehicles entering into service from January 1, 2005."}
{"chapter_id": "3.7.", "chapter_title": "Extinguishing the MI", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "3.7.1.", "chapter_title": "If misfire at levels likely to cause catalyst damage (as specified by the", "raw_text": "manufacturer) is not present any more, or if the engine is operated after\nchanges to speed and load conditions where the level of misfire will not cause\ncatalyst damage, the MI may be switched back to the previous state of\nactivation during the first driving cycle on which the misfire level was detected\nand may be switched to the normal activated mode on subsequent driving\ncycles.  If the MI is switched back to the previous state of activation, the\ncorresponding fault codes and stored freeze-frame conditions may be erased."}
{"chapter_id": "3.7.2.", "chapter_title": "For all other malfunctions, the MI may be de-activated after three subsequent", "raw_text": "sequential driving cycles during which the monitoring system responsible for\nactivating the MI ceases to detect the malfunction and if no other malfunction\nhas been identified that would independently activate the MI."}

{"chapter_id": "1.", "chapter_title": "INTRODUCTION", "raw_text": "This Appendix describes the procedure of the test according to Paragraph 3 of Annex 11.  The procedure\ndescribes a method for checking the function of the on-board diagnostic (OBD) system installed\non the vehicle by failure simulation of relevant systems in the engine management or emission\ncontrol system.  It also sets procedures for determining the durability of OBD systems.\n\nThe manufacturer shall make available the defective components and/or electrical devices which would\nbe used to simulate failures.  When measured over the Type I test cycle, such defective\ncomponents or devices shall not cause the vehicle emissions to exceed the limits of Paragraph\n3.3.2by more than 20%.\nWhen the vehicle is tested with the defective component or device fitted, the OBD system is approved if\nthe MI is activated.  The OBD system is also approved if the MI is activated below the OBD\nthreshold limits."}
{"chapter_id": "2.", "chapter_title": "DESCRIPTION OF TEST", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.", "chapter_title": "The testing of OBD systems consists of the following phases:", "raw_text": ""}

{"chapter_id": "2.1.2.", "chapter_title": "Preconditioning of the vehicle with a simulated malfunction over", "raw_text": "preconditioning specified in Paragraph 6.2.1. or Paragraph 6.2.2.,"}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.3.", "chapter_title": "Driving the vehicle with a simulated malfunction over the Type I test cycle and", "raw_text": "measuring the emissions of the vehicle,"}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.4.", "chapter_title": "Determining whether the OBD system reacts to the simulated malfunction and", "raw_text": "indicates malfunction in an appropriate manner to the vehicle driver."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.", "chapter_title": "Alternatively, at the request of the manufacturer, malfunction of one or more", "raw_text": "components may be electronically simulated according to the requirements of\nParagraph 6. below."}

{"chapter_id": "6.5.", "chapter_title": "Diagnostic Signals", "raw_text": "COUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "6.5.1.1.", "chapter_title": "Upon determination of the first malfunction of any component or system, \"freeze-", "raw_text": "frame\" engine conditions present at the time shall be stored in computer memory.\nShould a subsequent fuel system or misfire malfunction occur, any previously stored\nfreeze-frame conditions shall be replaced by the fuel system or misfire conditions\n(whichever occurs first).  Stored engine conditions shall include, but are not limited to\ncalculated load value, engine speed, fuel trim value(s) (if available), fuel pressure (if\navailable), vehicle speed (if available), coolant temperature, intake manifold pressure\n(if available), closed- or open-loop operation (if available) and the fault code which\ncaused the data to be stored.  The manufacturer shall choose the most appropriate\nset of conditions facilitating effective repairs for freeze-frame storage.  Only one frame\nof data is required.  Manufacturers may choose to store additional frames provided\nthat at least the required frame can be read by a generic scan tool meeting the\nspecifications of Paragraphs 6.5.3.2 and 6.5.3.3.  If the fault code causing the\nconditions to be stored is erased in accordance with Paragraph 3.7 of Annex 11, the\nstored engine conditions may also be erased."}
{"chapter_id": "6.5.1.2.", "chapter_title": "If available, the following signals in addition to the required freeze-frame information", "raw_text": "shall be made available on demand through the serial port on the standardised data\nlink connector, if the information is available to the on-board computer or can be\ndetermined using information available to the on-board computer: diagnostic trouble\ncodes, engine coolant temperature, fuel control system status (closed-loop, open-loop,\nother), fuel trim, ignition timing advance, intake air temperature, manifold air pressure,\nair flow rate, engine speed, throttle position sensor output value, secondary air status\n(upstream, downstream or atmosphere), calculated load value, vehicle speed and fuel\npressure.\n\nThe signals shall be provided in standard units based on the specifications given in Paragraph 6.5.3.\nActual signals shall be clearly identified separately from default value or limp-home signals."}
{"chapter_id": "6.5.1.3.", "chapter_title": "For all emission control systems for which specific on-board evaluation tests are", "raw_text": "conducted (catalyst, oxygen sensor, etc.), except misfire detection, fuel system\nmonitoring and comprehensive component monitoring, the results of the most recent\ntest performed by the vehicle and the limits to which the system is compared shall be\nmade available through the serial data port on the standardised data link connector\naccording to the specifications given in Paragraph 6.5.3.  For the monitored\ncomponents and systems excepted above, a pass/fail indication for the most recent\ntest results shall be available through the data link connector."}

{"chapter_id": "1.", "chapter_title": "PARAMETERS DEFINING THE OBD FAMILY", "raw_text": "The OBD family may be defined by basic design parameters which shall be common to vehicles within\nthe family. {"chapter_id": "1.", "chapter_title": "INTRODUCTION", "raw_text": "This Annex describes the special requirements that apply in the case of an approval of a\nvehicle that runs on LPG or Natural Gas (NG), or that can run either on unleaded or LPG or\nNatural Gas, insofar as the testing on LPG or Natural Gas is concerned.\n\nIn the case of LPG and Natural Gas there is on the market a large variation in fuel\ncomposition, requiring the fuelling system to adapt its fuelling rates to these compositions.\nTo demonstrate this capability, the vehicle has to be tested in the test Type I on two extreme\nreference fuels and demonstrate the self-adaptability of the fuelling system.  Whenever the\nself-adaptability of a fuelling system has been demonstrated on a vehicle, such a vehicle may\nbe considered as a parent of a family.  Vehicles that comply with the requirements of\nmembers of that family, if fitted with the same fuelling system, need to be tested on only one\nfuel."}
{"chapter_id": "2.", "chapter_title": "DEFINITIONS", "raw_text": "For the purpose of this Annex:"}
{"chapter_id": "2.1.", "chapter_title": "A \"parent vehicle\" means a vehicle that is selected to act as the vehicle on which", "raw_text": "the self-adaptability of a fuelling system is going to be demonstrated, and to which\nthe members of a family refer.  It is possible to have more than one parent vehicle in\na family."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.", "chapter_title": "Member of the Family", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.1.", "chapter_title": "A \"member of the family\" is a vehicle that shares the following essential", "raw_text": "characteristics with its parent(s):\n\n(a) It is produced by the same manufacturer;\n\n(b) It is subject to the same emission limits;\n\n(c) If the gas fuelling system has a central metering for the whole engine:\n\nIt has a certified power output between 0.7 and 1.15 times that of the parent vehicle.\n\nIf the gas fuelling system has an individual metering per cylinder:\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\nIt has a certified power output per cylinder between 0.7 and 1.15 times that of the\nparent vehicle.\n\n(d) If fitted with a catalyst, it has the same type of catalyst i.e. three-way, oxidation, deNOx.\n\n(e) It has a gas fuelling system (including the pressure regulator) from the same system\nmanufacturer and of the same type: induction, vapour injection (single point,\nmultipoint), liquid injection (single point, multipoint).\n\n(f) This gas fuelling system is controlled by an ECU of the same type and technical\nspecification, containing the same software principles and control strategy."}
{"chapter_id": "2.2.2.", "chapter_title": "With regard to requirement (c): in the case where a demonstration shows", "raw_text": "two gas-fuelled vehicles could be members of the same family with the\nexception of their certified power output, respectively P1 and P2 (P1 < P2),\nand both are tested as if were parent vehicles, the family relation will be\nconsidered valid for any vehicle with a certified power output between 0.7 P1\nand 1.15 P2."}
{"chapter_id": "3.", "chapter_title": "GRANTING OF A TYPE APPROVAL", "raw_text": "Type approval is granted subject to the following requirements:"}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.", "chapter_title": "Exhaust emissions approval of a parent vehicle:", "raw_text": "The parent vehicle should demonstrate its capability to adapt to any fuel composition that\nmay occur across the market.  In the case of LPG there are variations in C3/C4 composition.\nIn the case of Natural Gas there are generally two types of fuel, high calorific fuel (H-gas)\nand low calorific fuel (L-gas), but with a significant spread within both ranges; they differ\nsignificantly in Wobbe Index.  These variations are reflected in the reference fuels."}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.1.", "chapter_title": "The parent vehicle(s) shall be tested in the test Type I on the two extreme", "raw_text": "reference fuels of Annex 10a."}

{"chapter_id": "3.1.2.", "chapter_title": "The vehicle(s) is (are) considered to conform if, with both reference fuels,", "raw_text": "the vehicle complies with the emission limits."}

{"chapter_id": "3.", "chapter_title": "TEST PROCEDURE", "raw_text": "The vehicle may be equipped with a switch capable of preventing or permitting the regeneration process\nprovided that this operation has no effect on original engine calibration.  This switch shall be\npermitted only for the purpose of preventing regeneration during loading of the regeneration\nsystem and during the pre-conditioning cycles.  However, it shall not be used during the\nmeasurement of emissions during the regeneration phase; rather the emission test shall be\ncarried out with the unchanged Original Equipment Manufacturer's (OEM) control unit.\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05"}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.", "chapter_title": "Exhaust Emission Measurement Between Two Cycles where Regenerative", "raw_text": "Phases\nOccur"}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.1.", "chapter_title": "Average emissions between regeneration phases and during loading of the", "raw_text": "regenerative device shall be determined from the arithmetic mean of several\napproximately equidistant (if more than 2) Type I operating cycles or\nequivalent engine test bench cycles.  As an alternative the manufacturer may\nprovide data to show that the emissions remain constant\n(± 15%) between regeneration phases.  In this case, the emissions measured during the\nregular Type I test may be used.  In any other case emissions measurement for at least two\nType I operating cycles or equivalent engine test bench cycles must be completed: one\nimmediately after regeneration (before new loading) and one as close as possible prior to a\nregeneration phase.  All emissions measurements and calculations shall be carried out\naccording to Annex 4, Paragraphs 5., 6., 7. and 8.  Determination of average emissions for a\nsingle regenerative system shall be calculated according to Paragraph 3.3. of this Annex and\nfor multiple regeneration systems according to Paragraph 3.4. of this Annex."}
{"chapter_id": "3.1.2.", "chapter_title": "The loading process and Ki determination shall be made during the Type I", "raw_text": "operating cycle, on a chassis dynamometer or on an engine test bench using\nan equivalent test cycle. {"chapter_id": "3.4.1.2.", "chapter_title": "If a single device of the multiple regeneration system changed only in strategy", "raw_text": "parameters (i.e. such as \"D\" and/or \"d\" for DPF) and the manufacturer could present\ntechnical feasible data and information to the Technical Service that:\n\n(a) There is no detectable interaction to the other device(s) of the system; and\n\n(b) The important parameters (i.e. construction, working principle, volume, location etc.) are\nidentical;\n\nThe necessary update procedure for ki could be simplified.\n\nAs agreed between the manufacturer and the Technical Service in such a case only a single event of\nsampling/storage and regeneration should be performed and the test results (\"Msi\", \"Mri\") in\ncombination with the changed parameters (\"D\" and/or \"d\") could be introduced in the relevant\nformula(s) to update the multiple ki − factor in a mathematical way under substitution of the\nexisting basis ki − factor formula(s)."}

{"chapter_id": "3.1.2.5.2.2.", "chapter_title": "Sampling shall begin (BS) before or at the initiation", "raw_text": "of the vehicle start up procedure and continue over\na number of repeat test cycles.  It shall end on\nconclusion of the final idling period in the first extra-\nurban (Part Two) cycle during which the battery\nreached the minimum state of charge according to\nthe criterion defined below (end of sampling (ES)).\n\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\nThe electricity balance Q [Ah] is measured over each combined cycle, using the procedure specified in\nAppendix 2 of Annex 8 to Regulation No.101, and used to determine when the battery\nminimum state of charge has been reached.\n\nThe battery minimum state of charge is considered to have been reached in combined cycle N if the\nelectricity balance measured during combined cycle N+1 is not more than a 3% discharge,\nexpressed as a percentage of the nominal capacity of the battery (in Ah) in its maximum state\nof charge, as declared by the manufacturer.  At the manufacturer's request additional test\ncycles may be run and their results included in the calculations in Paragraphs 3.1.2.5.5. and\n3.1.4.2.provided that the electricity balance for each additional test cycle shows less\ndischarge of the battery than over the previous cycle.\n\nIn between each of the cycles a hot soak period of up to 10 minutes is allowed.  The power train shall be\nswitched off during this period."}

{"chapter_id": "3.2.4.1.", "chapter_title": "In the case of testing according to Paragraph 3.2.2.6.2.1.", "raw_text": "For communication, the weighted values shall be calculated as below:\n\nMi = (De . M1i + Dav . M2i) / (De + Dav)\n\nWhere:\n\nMi = mass emission of the pollutant i in g/km\n\nM1i = average mass emission of the pollutant i in g/km with a fully charged electrical energy/power storage\ndevice calculated in Paragraph 3.2.2.7.\n\nM2i = average mass emission of the pollutant i in g/km with an electrical energy/power storage device in\nminimum state of charge (maximum discharge of capacity) calculated in\nParagraph 3.2.3.5.\n\nDe = vehicle electric range with the switch in pure electric position, according to the procedure described\nin Regulation No.101, Annex 9.  If there is not a pure electric position, the\nmanufacturer must provide the means for performing the measurement with the\nvehicle running in pure electric mode.\n\nDav = 25 km (average distance between two battery recharges)."}

M1i + Dav . M2i)/(Dovc + Dav)\nwhere:\n\nMi = mass emission of the pollutant i in g/km.\n\nM1i = average mass emission of the pollutant i in g/km with a fully charged electrical energy/power storage\ndevice calculated in Paragraph 3.2.2.7.\n\nM2i = average mass emission of the pollutant i in g/km with an electrical energy/power storage device in\nminimum state of charge (maximum discharge of capacity) calculated in\nParagraph 3.2.3.5.\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\nDovc = OVC range according to the procedure described in Regulation No.101,\nAnnex 9.\n\nDav = 25 km (average distance between two battery recharges)."}

{"chapter_id": "6.", "chapter_title": "TYPE IV TEST METHODS", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "6.1.", "chapter_title": "The vehicles shall be tested according to Annex 7.", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "6.2.", "chapter_title": "Before starting the test procedure (Paragraph 5.1 of Annex 7), the vehicles shall be", "raw_text": "preconditioned as follows:"}
{"chapter_id": "6.2.1.", "chapter_title": "For OVC Vehicles:", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "6.2.1.1.", "chapter_title": "OVC vehicles without an operating mode switch: the procedure", "raw_text": "shall start with the discharge of the electrical energy/power storage\ndevice of the vehicle while driving (on the test track, on a chassis\ndynamometer, etc.):\n\n– at a steady speed of 50 km/h until the fuel consuming engine of\nthe HEV starts up, or\n\n– if a vehicle cannot reach a steady speed of 50 km/h without starting\nup the fuel consuming engine, the speed shall be reduced until the\nvehicle can run a lower steady speed where the fuel consuming\nengine just does not start up for a defined time/distance (to be\nspecified between technical service and manufacturer), or\n\n– with manufacturer's recommendation.\n\nThe fuel consuming engine shall be stopped within 10 seconds of it being automatically\nstarted."}
{"chapter_id": "6.2.1.2.", "chapter_title": "OVC vehicles with an operating mode switch: the procedure shall", "raw_text": "start with the discharge of the electrical energy/power storage device\nof the vehicle while driving with the switch in pure electric position\n(on the test track, on a chassis dynamometer, etc.) at a steady speed\nof 70% ± 5% from the maximum thirty minutes speed of the vehicle.\n\nStopping the discharge occurs:\n\n– when the vehicle is not able to run at 65% of the maximum thirty\nminutes speed, or\n\n– when an indication to stop the vehicle is given to the driver by the\nstandard on-board instrumentation, or\nCOUNTRY :E.C.E. © InterRegs Ltd 2011\n\nORIGINAL :UNITED NATIONS of April 9, 1990\n\n\n\n\nTITLE:   Emissions –  Regulation No.83-05\n\n– after covering the distance of 100 km.\n\nIf the vehicle is not equipped with a pure electric mode, the electrical energy/power storage device\ndischarge shall be conducted with the vehicle driving (on the test track, on a chassis\ndynamometer, etc.):\n\n– at a steady speed of 50 km/h until the fuel consuming engine of\nthe HEV starts up, or\n\n– if a vehicle cannot reach a steady speed of 50 km/h without starting\nup the fuel consuming engine, the speed shall be reduced until the\nvehicle can run a lower steady speed where the fuel consuming\nengine does not start up for a defined time/distance (to be specified\nbetween technical service and manufacturer), or\n\n– with manufacturer's recommendation.\n\nThe engine shall be stopped within 10 seconds of it being automatically started."}
{"chapter_id": "6.2.2.", "chapter_title": "For NOVC Vehicles:", "raw_text": ""}
{"chapter_id": "6.2.2.1.", "chapter_title": "NOVC vehicles without an operating mode switch: the procedure", "raw_text": "shall start with a preconditioning of at least two consecutive\ncomplete driving cycles (one Part One and one Part Two) without\nsoak."}
{"chapter_id": "6.2.2.2.", "chapter_title": "NOVC vehicles with an operating mode switch: the procedure", "raw_text": "shall start with a preconditioning of at least two consecutive\ncomplete driving cycles (one Part One and one Part Two) without\nsoak, performed with the vehicle running in hybrid mode.  If several\nhybrid modes are available, the test shall be carried out in the mode\nwhich is automatically set after turn on of the ignition key (normal\nmode)."}
